قوله وليس نسبته الى الفقه كنسبة الميزان الخ
اس عبارت میں مصنف نے اصول فقہ وفقہ اور منطق و فلسفہ کے درمیان خصوصیت و نسبت ظاہر کرتے ہوئے صاحب محکم الاصول امان اللہ بنارسی پر رد کیا ہے۔ گذشتہ تقریر سے یہ واضح ہو گیا کہ فقہ واصول فقہ کے درمیان ایک نسبت خاصہ قائم ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ فقہ کی دلیل تفصیلی سے حاصل شدہ صغریٰ کے ساتھ اصول فقہ کی دلیل اجمالی سے اخذ کردہ کبری سے جب تک قیاس مرکب نہ ہو گا اس وقت تک حکم شرعی ثابت نہ ہو گا غرض اصول فقہ کو فقہ کے ساتھ ایسی خاص خصوصیت حاصل ہے جو دوسرے علوم کے ساتھ ایسی خصوصیت نہیں پائی جاتی ۔ اس کے برخلاف جناب امان اللہ بنارسی صاحب کا خیال یہ ہے اصول فقہ کو فقہ کے ساتھ وہی نسبت ہے جو منطق کو فلسفہ کے ساتھ حاصل ہے چنانچہ صاحب محکم رقمطراز ہیں ۔
" أن القضايا العقلية اما ضرورية او منتهية اليها في سلسلة الاكتساب الا أن کلامن معلوماتك لا يصلح كاسباً لكل من مجهولاتک بل بازاء كل مجهول معلومات مخصوصة تهديك ملاحظتها مرتبة اليه فمست الحاجة الى الة قانونية تعصم الذهن عن أن يضل هو المنطق كذالك الاحكام الشرعية ماخذها الوحى الا انه لايتيسر بدون ضبط احوال الادلة التى لها مدخل في احوال الاستنباط ككون اللفظ امراً ونهياً وعاماً وخاصاً والبحث عن احكامها بحيث يتعدى الى معروضا تها وهكذا شان المنطق فتوسط مسائل الاصول بين الاحكام والادلة في الحصول كتوسط المنطق بين المعلوم والمجهول من المعقول فتسميتها بالادلة لاوجه لا، اما التفصيلة فظاهر واما الاجمالية فاطلاقها على المسائل امالامر الاشارة اليه من أن احكامها متعدية الى الادلة ماخوذة على وجه كلى فمجاز لاحاجة الى ان كابه مع ظهور الوجه الصحيح
صاحب محکم الاصول کی مندرجہ بالا عبارتوں خصوصاً خط کشیدہ عبادت سے بہت واضح ہوتا ہے کہ مسئلہ اصولیہ کو احکام و دلائل کے درمیان وہی نسبت حاصل ہے جو معلومات و مجھولات کے درمیان منطق کو حاصل ہے۔ یا منطق کو فلسفہ کے ساتھ ہے۔ مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ بادی النظر میں صاحب محکم کی یہ بات غلط ہے۔ جو سبب و ہم سرزد ہو گئی ہے کیونکہ اصول فقہ کو فقہ کے ساتھ وہ نسبت نہیں ہے جو منطق کو فلسفہ کی طرف ہے چونکہ منطق کو فلسفہ، اصول اور فقہ وغیرہ جملہ علوم کی طرف ایک ہی نسبت ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ کیفیت انتاج کی معرفت میں صرف منطق کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے غرض جملہ علوم کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے منطق کی حیثیت ایک واسطہ اور علم آلی کی ہے بس۔
پھر اصول فقہ کی نسبت فقہ کی طرف منطق کی نسبت فلسفہ کی طرف، کی طرح کیونکر ہو سکتی ہے جب کہ مسئلہ فقہ کی دلیل تفصیلی (مثلاً اتو الزکوۃ ) اپنے مادے (ایتاء الزکوۃ ) اور ہیئت صیغیہ (بیت صیغہ امر مثلاً) کے ساتھ ، مسائل اصول فقہ کے موضوع کے افراد و مصداق میں سے ہوتے ہیں ، اس کو مثال سے یوں سمجھو کہ حکم ایتاء زکوۃ کے لئے مثلا آیۃ مبارکہ دوا تو الزکوۃ دلیل تفصیلی ہے اور مسائل
If one wants to argue for the obligation of Zakat, he will arrange the syllogism as follows: 'Zakat is a thing commanded by His statement 'and give Zakat'; and everything commanded is obligatory.' By this major premise that the command implies obligation, it follows that Zakat is obligatory. So the minor premise of the mentioned syllogism is taken from the detailed proof (āyah 'ātū al-zakāt) and the major is taken from the usul principle 'al-amr lil-wujūb'. As is clear from the arranged syllogism. From this it became known that 'Zakat is obligatory' is a fiqh ruling. Thus, if the usul principle 'al-amr lil-wujūb' were not present, the obligation of Zakat and the obligation of prayer etc. could not be known, even though from the detailed proof the very fact that prayer and fasting are commanded is known, but from merely being commanded, obligation does not necessarily follow. Therefore, when applying the detailed proof, the general proof is needed, because each usul principle has a specific relation to fiqh rulings, just as each of the two premises relates to the conclusion. The conclusion is that just as a conclusion is impossible without the two premises, likewise the proof of a legal ruling from a detailed proof without a general proof is impossible. This is the meaning of the author's statement 'when applying detailed proofs to their rulings'.
His statement: 'And its relationship to fiqh is not like the relationship of the scale [logic to philosophy] etc.' In this expression, the author, while showing the specific relationship between usul al-fiqh and fiqh and between logic and philosophy, refutes Aman Allah al-Banarsi, the author of Muḥkam al-Uṣūl. From the previous discussion it became clear that a specific relationship exists between fiqh and usul al-fiqh: namely, that until a compound syllogism is formed from the minor premise obtained from the detailed proof of fiqh and the major premise derived from the general proof of usul, the legal ruling is not established. In short, usul al-fiqh has such a specific relationship with fiqh that is not found with other sciences. Contrary to this, the opinion of Aman Allah al-Banarsi is that usul al-fiqh has the same relationship to fiqh as logic has to philosophy. Thus the author of Muḥkam writes: 'Intellectual propositions are either necessary or ultimately lead to them in the chain of acquisition, but not every piece of your knowledge can serve as a cause for each of your unknowns; rather, for each unknown there are specific pieces of knowledge whose observation, arranged, guides you to it. So there is need for a legal instrument that protects the mind from straying, and that is logic. Similarly, the legal rulings have their source in revelation, but it is not accessible without controlling the conditions of the proofs that have a role in the conditions of derivation – like whether a word is a command or prohibition, general or specific – and researching their rulings such that they extend to their subjects. So the role of the principles [usul] between rulings and proofs in derivation is like the role of logic between the known and the unknown among intelligibles. So calling them 'proofs' is not without basis: as for detailed proofs, it is obvious; as for general proofs, their application to the principles is metaphorical, because their rulings extend to the proofs taken as universal. There is no need for a book given the clear correct aspect.' From the above expressions of the author of Muḥkam, especially the underlined part, it is very clear that he considers the relationship of a usul principle to rulings and proofs to be the same as that of logic to knowns and unknowns, or that of logic to philosophy. The author (of al-Nuʿūt) says that at first glance this statement of the author of Muḥkam is wrong, an error that occurred due to misconception. Because usul al-fiqh does not have the relationship to fiqh that logic has to philosophy. Since logic has one and the same relationship to philosophy, usul, fiqh and all sciences – namely, that only logic is needed for the knowledge of the quality of inference. In short, with respect to all sciences, logic is a mere intermediary and an instrumental science. Then how can the relationship of usul to fiqh be like that of logic to philosophy, when the detailed proof of a fiqh issue (e.g., 'ātū al-zakāt') with its matter (the giving of Zakat) and its form (the imperative form) is among the individuals and instantiations of the subject matter of usul? Understand this through an example: for the ruling of giving Zakat, the blessed verse 'and give Zakat' is the detailed proof, and the principles are...
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the relationship between usul al-fiqh and fiqh, using a syllogism to illustrate. The author first demonstrates how a fiqh ruling (obligation of Zakat) is derived by combining a detailed proof from Quran (minor premise) with a universal principle from usul (major premise). This establishes that usul provides the major premise that converts a detailed command into a legal obligation. Without the usul principle 'al-amr lil-wujūb', the mere fact of being commanded does not entail obligation. The passage then critically examines the view of Aman Allah al-Banarsi (author of Muḥkam al-Uṣūl) who equated the relationship between usul and fiqh to that between logic and philosophy. The commentator argues that this analogy is flawed because logic has a universal instrumental relationship to all sciences, whereas usul has a unique and specific relationship to fiqh alone. In Hanafi usul, the detailed proofs (like specific Quranic verses) are the subject matter of usul principles; the principles analyze the linguistic and logical features of those proofs to derive general rules. Thus, usul is not merely an external tool (like logic) but its principles directly apply to the very proofs of fiqh. The commentator emphasizes that usul principles are applied to detailed proofs to extract rulings, and this is a one-to-one relationship, unlike the universal applicability of logic.

Key Terms
دليل تفصيلي (dalīl tafṣīlī): A specific textual evidence (like a Quranic verse or hadith) that directly indicates a particular ruling.
دليل إجمالي (dalīl ijmālī): A general principle from usul al-fiqh (e.g., 'al-amr lil-wujūb') that provides the major premise in legal deduction.
قياس (qiyās): A syllogism composed of a minor premise (detailed proof) and a major premise (usul principle) to produce a fiqh ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between the detailed proof and the general proof in deriving a fiqh ruling?
A) The detailed proof is the sole determinant; the general proof is only for confirmation.
B) The general proof provides the subject matter; the detailed proof provides the legal force.
C) The detailed proof provides the minor premise; the general proof provides the major premise; both are necessary.
D) The general proof replaces the need for detailed proof.

Key Takeaway
A fiqh ruling is the product of a two-premise syllogism: the detailed proof (text) and the general proof (usul principle); neither alone suffices.

Method of Learning
advanced
10 min
The Distinctive Relationship of Usul to Fiqh: Refuting the Logic-Philosophy Analogy
Refuting the analogy between usul/fiqh and logic/philosophy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate Aman Allah al-Banarsi's analogy between usul/fiqh and logic/philosophy, and articulate the Hanafi refutation that usul has a unique substantive relationship to fiqh.

Core Idea
Usul is not a universal tool like logic; its principles directly apply to the detailed proofs of fiqh as their subject matter.

In the previous lesson, we saw the mechanical process of deriving rulings. Now we examine a deeper methodological question: is usul al-fiqh merely an instrumental science like logic, or does it have a unique, substantive connection to fiqh? Aman Allah al-Banarsi argued the former, likening usul to logic. The Hanafi commentator refutes this by showing that logic relates universally to all sciences, whereas usul principles are specifically instantiated in the detailed proofs of fiqh. This lesson sharpens your understanding of the nature of usul al-fiqh as a discipline.

Guided Path
1
State Banarsi's analogy
Aman Allah al-Banarsi claims that usul stands between rulings and proofs just as logic stands between the known and unknown. Usul principles are called 'proofs' metaphorically because they extend to detailed proofs.
His view is based on the common instrumental role of providing a method.
2
Identify his supporting evidence
Banarsi argues that just as logic is a universal instrument for all intellectual sciences, usul is an instrument for fiqh. He sees the relationship as one of means to end, not as a substantive connection.
He considers detailed proofs as the matter and usul as the form.
3
Present the Hanafi objection
The commentator argues that logic has a uniform relationship to all sciences: it provides the method of inference. Usul, on the other hand, has a specific relationship only to fiqh: usul principles are directly applicable to the detailed proof texts of fiqh (e.g., a verse is an individual instance of the usul subject matter).
Detailed proofs are not just raw data; they are the very objects of usul analysis.
4
Explain why the analogy fails
Logic's relationship to any science is identical: it teaches how to reason. Usul's relationship to fiqh is unique: it analyzes the specific types of proofs found in fiqh (commands, prohibitions, etc.) and generates principles that are then applied back to those same proofs. The detailed proof is a specimen of the usul subject matter, not a separate domain.
Thus, usul is more like a meta-science of fiqh proofs than a mere instrument.
5
State the tarjih (preferred view)
The Hanafi view is that usul al-fiqh has a specific and substantive relation to fiqh, not an instrumental one. This is the correct understanding, and it affects how we teach and apply usul.
The commentator clearly sides with the Hanafi position.

وجوب زکوۃ پر استدلال کرنا ہے تو اس طرح قیاس کو ترتیب دیں گے۔
الركوة شئى مامور به بقوله تعالى واتو الزكوة
وكل ماهو مامور فهوواجب. بهذه الكلية ان الامر للوجوب. ينتج. أن الزكوة واجبة
پس قیاس مذکور کا صغری دلیل تفصیلی واتو الزکوۃ سے اور کبر کی مسئلہ اصولیہ الامر لوجوب سے ماخوذ ہے جیسا کہ قیاس مرتب سے بہت ظاہر ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہو گیا کہ "الزکوۃ واجبة" مثلا ایک مسئلہ فقہیہ ہے چنانچہ اگر اصول فقہ کی دلیل الامر للوجوب نہ ہوتی تو وجوب زکوة ووجوب نماز وغیرہ احکام اینجا با معلوم نہ ہو پاتے گو کہ دلیل تفصیلی سے نفس نماز ونفس روزہ کا مامور بہ ہونا معلوم ہو جاتا ہے مگر صرف مامور بہ کے ثبوت سے وجوب کا ثبوت لازم نہیں ہے اس لئے دلیل تفصیلی کو تطبیق دیتے وقت دلیل اجمالی کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے کہ اصول فقہ کے ہر ہر مسئلہ کی نسبت مسائل فقہیہ کی طرف دیسی ہی ہے جیسا کہ قیاس کے دونوں مقدموں میں سے ہر ایک کی نسبت نتیجہ کی طرف ہے حاصل یہ کہ نتیجہ دونوں مقدموں کے بغیر جس طرح محال ہے اسی طرح دلیل تفصیلیہ سے وجوب حکم کا ثبوت بغیر دلیل اجمالی محال ہے یہی معنی ہے ماتن کے قول عند تطبیق الدلائل التفصیلیہ علی احکامھا" کا ۔
قوله وليس نسبته الى الفقه كنسبة الميزان الخ
اس عبارت میں مصنف نے اصول فقہ وفقہ اور منطق و فلسفہ کے درمیان خصوصیت و نسبت ظاہر کرتے ہوئے صاحب محکم الاصول امان اللہ بنارسی پر رد کیا ہے۔ گذشتہ تقریر سے یہ واضح ہو گیا کہ فقہ واصول فقہ کے درمیان ایک نسبت خاصہ قائم ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ فقہ کی دلیل تفصیلی سے حاصل شدہ صغریٰ کے ساتھ اصول فقہ کی دلیل اجمالی سے اخذ کردہ کبری سے جب تک قیاس مرکب نہ ہو گا اس وقت تک حکم شرعی ثابت نہ ہو گا غرض اصول فقہ کو فقہ کے ساتھ ایسی خاص خصوصیت حاصل ہے جو دوسرے علوم کے ساتھ ایسی خصوصیت نہیں پائی جاتی ۔ اس کے برخلاف جناب امان اللہ بنارسی صاحب کا خیال یہ ہے اصول فقہ کو فقہ کے ساتھ وہی نسبت ہے جو منطق کو فلسفہ کے ساتھ حاصل ہے چنانچہ صاحب محکم رقمطراز ہیں ۔

Similarly, the legal rulings have their source in revelation, but it is not accessible without controlling the conditions of the proofs that have a role in the conditions of derivation – like whether a word is a command or prohibition, general or specific – and researching their rulings such that they extend to their subjects. So the role of the principles [usul] between rulings and proofs in derivation is like the role of logic between the known and the unknown among intelligibles. So calling them 'proofs' is not without basis: as for detailed proofs, it is obvious; as for general proofs, their application to the principles is metaphorical, because their rulings extend to the proofs taken as universal. There is no need for a book given the clear correct aspect.' From the above expressions of the author of Muḥkam, especially the underlined part, it is very clear that he considers the relationship of a usul principle to rulings and proofs to be the same as that of logic to knowns and unknowns, or that of logic to philosophy. The author (of al-Nuʿūt) says that at first glance this statement of the author of Muḥkam is wrong, an error that occurred due to misconception. Because usul al-fiqh does not have the relationship to fiqh that logic has to philosophy. Since logic has one and the same relationship to philosophy, usul, fiqh and all sciences – namely, that only logic is needed for the knowledge of the quality of inference. In short, with respect to all sciences, logic is a mere intermediary and an instrumental science. Then how can the relationship of usul to fiqh be like that of logic to philosophy, when the detailed proof of a fiqh issue (e.g., 'ātū al-zakāt') with its matter (the giving of Zakat) and its form (the imperative form) is among the individuals and instantiations of the subject matter of usul? Understand this through an example: for the ruling of giving Zakat, the blessed verse 'and give Zakat' is the detailed proof, and the principles are...
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the relationship between usul al-fiqh and fiqh, using a syllogism to illustrate. The author first demonstrates how a fiqh ruling (obligation of Zakat) is derived by combining a detailed proof from Quran (minor premise) with a universal principle from usul (major premise). This establishes that usul provides the major premise that converts a detailed command into a legal obligation. Without the usul principle 'al-amr lil-wujūb', the mere fact of being commanded does not entail obligation. The passage then critically examines the view of Aman Allah al-Banarsi (author of Muḥkam al-Uṣūl) who equated the relationship between usul and fiqh to that between logic and philosophy. The commentator argues that this analogy is flawed because logic has a universal instrumental relationship to all sciences, whereas usul has a unique and specific relationship to fiqh alone. In Hanafi usul, the detailed proofs (like specific Quranic verses) are the subject matter of usul principles; the principles analyze the linguistic and logical features of those proofs to derive general rules. Thus, usul is not merely an external tool (like logic) but its principles directly apply to the very proofs of fiqh. The commentator emphasizes that usul principles are applied to detailed proofs to extract rulings, and this is a one-to-one relationship, unlike the universal applicability of logic.

Key Terms
دليل تفصيلي (dalīl tafṣīlī): A specific textual evidence (like a Quranic verse or hadith) that directly indicates a particular ruling.
دليل إجمالي (dalīl ijmālī): A general principle from usul al-fiqh (e.g., 'al-amr lil-wujūb') that provides the major premise in legal deduction.
علم آلي (ʿilm ālī): An instrumental science that provides tools for reasoning, such as logic.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main reason the commentator gives for rejecting Banarsi's analogy between usul/fiqh and logic/philosophy?
A) Logic is an instrumental science, while usul is not a science at all.
B) Logic has a universal relationship to all sciences, whereas usul has a specific relationship only to fiqh.
C) Banarsi misunderstood the concept of 'proof' entirely.
D) The commentator does not reject it; he accepts the analogy.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is not merely an instrumental science like logic; it has a unique, substantive relationship to fiqh that distinguishes it from all other disciplines.

Refuting the Analogy Between Usul al-Fiqh and Logic-Philosophy Relations
Critiquing the claim that usul al-fiqh relates to fiqh as logic relates to philosophy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key difference between the subject matter of usul al-fiqh and logic, and evaluate why the analogy between usul-fiqh and logic-philosophy fails according to the Hanafi usul tradition.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh's subject includes external fiqh evidences as its individuals, unlike logic's purely mental subject—so the analogy fails.

This passage from Ashraf al-Nu'ut critiques a bold claim: that usul al-fiqh relates to fiqh just as logic relates to philosophy. The author argues that this analogy overlooks a fundamental difference in subject matter. We will unpack the argument and understand why Hanafi usul scholars insist that usul is not merely an instrumental science but has substantive content that directly encompasses the detailed evidences of fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing claim
What did the author of Muhkam al-Usul argue? He claimed that usul mediates between rulings and evidences just as logic mediates between knowns and unknowns, implying the same instrumental relationship.
2
State the Hanafi objection
The commentator rejects the analogy because the subject of usul (e.g., 'command') includes the detailed evidences of fiqh as its individuals, while logic's subject is mental and excludes external realities.
3
Contrast the subject matters
Usul's subject (e.g., command, prohibition) exists externally and is real; logic's subject is secondary intelligibles existing only in the mind.
4
Apply the test
Show that a fiqh detailed evidence (e.g., 'give zakat') is an individual of usul's subject 'command', while a philosophical premise (e.g., 'the celestial sphere has a single nature') is not an individual of logic's subject because it is external.
5
Conclude the thamarah al-khilaf
If usul were merely instrumental, its principles would be purely formal; but since its subject is substantive, its principles directly apply to real texts and are not just abstract tools.

پھر اصول فقہ کی نسبت فقہ کی طرف منطق کی نسبت فلسفہ کی طرف، کی طرح کیونکر ہو سکتی ہے جب کہ مسئلہ فقہ کی دلیل تفصیلی (مثلاً اتو الزکوۃ ) اپنے مادے (ایتاء الزکوۃ ) اور ہیئت صیغیہ (بیت صیغہ امر مثلاً) کے ساتھ ، مسائل اصول فقہ کے موضوع کے افراد و مصداق میں سے ہوتے ہیں ، اس کو مثال سے یوں سمجھو کہ حکم ایتاء زکوۃ کے لئے مثلا آیۃ مبارکہ دوا تو الزکوۃ دلیل تفصیلی ہے اور مسائل
اصولیہ میں سے الامر للوجوب اس کی دلیل اجمالی ہے، پس مسئلہ اصولیہ یعنی الامر للوجوب میں موضوع اس کا قول الا مر ہے جس کے افراد وہ تمام صیغے ہیں جو امر کے مادے و ہیئت کے ساتھ وارد ہیں جیسے اقیمو الصلوۃ و آتو الزکوۃ اتمو الصیام وغیرہ۔ اسی مفہوم کو مصنف نے اپنے قول ” فان الدلائل التفصيلية بموادها وصورها من افراد موضوع اصول الفقہ“ سے بیان کیا ہے۔ حالانکہ منطق کی نسبت فلسفہ کی طرف اس طرح کی نہیں ہوتی ہے کیونکہ مسائل فلسفیہ کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے جن صغریات کو ترتیب دی جاتی ہیں وہ مسائل منطق کے موضوع کے افراد سے نہیں ہو تیں چنانچہ کہا جاتا ہے۔ أن الفلك ذو طبعيه ، واحدة، وكل ماکان کذالک فشكله الطبعی کرہ چونکہ اس قیاس میں صغری ماخوذہ ”کون الفلك ذا طبعیة واحدة ، خارجی ونفس الامری ہے ذہنی نہیں تو پھر کیسے فلسفہ کی دلیل تفصیلی ، مسائل منطق کے موضوع کے افراد میں سے ہو سکتے ہیں کہ فلسفہ اعیان خارجیہ سے بحث کرتا ہے چنانچہ اس لئے دلائل تفصیلیہ فلسفیہ معقولات اولیٰ سے مرکب ہوتے ہیں اور اس کے موضوع اعیان خارجیہ ہوتے ہیں اس کے برخلاف منطق میں معقولات ثانیہ سے بحث ہوتی جس کا ظرف عروض صرف اور صرف ذہن ہوتا ہے پس جو خارجی ونفس الامری ہو وہ اشیاء ذہنیہ کے موضوع کے افراد سے کیونکر ہو سکتے ہیں؟ رہے اصول فقہ وفقہ تو ان دونوں پر منطق و فلسفہ کا قیاس صحیح نہیں ، اس لئے اصول فقہ بھی موجودات خارجیہ کے احوال سے بحث کرتا ہے چنانچہ مسئلہ اصولیہ کے موضوعات مثلا الامر، انھی وغیرہ خارج میں موجود ہوتے ہیں اور فقہ کی دلیل تفصیلی جیسے اقیمو الصلوۃ واتو الزکوة، لا تاكلوا الرباء وغيرها افراد بھی افراد خارجیہ ہوتے ہیں لہذا موضوع خارجی کے افراد، افراد خارجیہ تو ہو سکتے ہیں لیکن موضوع ذہنی کے افراد ، افراد خارجیہ ہوں کسی طرح ممکن نہیں۔
اس مقام پر مصنف نے حاشیہ نگاری کی ہے وہ یہ ہے۔
اعلم انه اذا قلنا هذا مامور به وکل مامور به فهو واجب فالصغرى ثبه ، بالدليل التفصيلى والكبرى من الاصول والكيفية العارضة لمجموع المتقدمتين من المنطق مطلب یہ ہے کہ علم منطق ایک علم آتی ہے ہر علم وفن کی طرف اسکی نسبت اور ضرورت مسادی
Intellectual propositions are either necessary or ultimately reducible to them in the chain of acquisition, but not everything you know is suitable as an acquirer for each of your unknowns; rather, for each unknown there are specific knowns whose ordered observation guides you to it. So there is a need for a legal instrument that protects the mind from error, and that is logic. Similarly, the sources of legal rulings are revelation, but it is not possible without regulating the conditions of the evidences that have a role in the conditions of derivation, such as whether a word is command or prohibition, general or specific, and investigating their rulings such that they extend to their subjects. And thus is the case of logic. So the issues of usul mediate between the rulings and evidences in attainment, just as logic mediates between the known and unknown of the intellect. So calling them evidences has no basis. As for the detailed (evidences), it is apparent; as for the summary (evidences), applying it to the issues is metaphorical due to the indication that their rulings extend to evidences taken in a universal manner. There is no need for concealment when the correct aspect is apparent.

The author of Muhkam al-Usul's above statements, especially the underlined phrase, make it very clear that the usuli issue has the same relationship to rulings and evidences as logic has to knowns and unknowns, or as logic has to philosophy. The author says that at first glance, the statement of the author of Muhkam is false, and an error occurred due to illusion, because usul al-fiqh does not have the same relationship to fiqh as logic has to philosophy. Since logic has one relationship to philosophy, usul, fiqh, and all sciences, and that is that in the knowledge of the method of production, only logic is needed. In short, when relating to all sciences, the status of logic is that of an intermediary and an instrumental science.

Then how can the relationship of usul al-fiqh to fiqh be like the relationship of logic to philosophy, when the detailed evidence of a fiqh issue (e.g., 'give zakat') with its material (giving zakat) and its form (imperative form) are among the individuals and instantiations of the subject matter of usul al-fiqh? Understand this with an example: For the ruling of giving zakat, for instance, the blessed verse 'give zakat' is the detailed evidence, and from the usuli issues, 'the command is for obligation' is its summary evidence. So in the usuli issue, i.e., 'the command is for obligation', its subject is the word 'command', whose individuals are all imperative forms that come with the material and form of command, such as 'establish prayer', 'give zakat', 'complete the fast', etc. The author has expressed this meaning in his words: 'For detailed evidences with their materials and forms are among the individuals of the subject of usul al-fiqh.' Whereas the relationship of logic to philosophy is not like this, because the minor premises arranged to prove philosophical issues are not from the individuals of the subject of logic. Thus it is said: 'The celestial sphere has a single nature, and whatever is like that, its natural shape is a sphere.' Since in this syllogism, the taken minor premise 'the celestial sphere has a single nature' is external and real, not mental, then how can philosophy's detailed evidence be among the individuals of the subject of logic? Because philosophy discusses external entities. Therefore, philosophical detailed evidences are composed of primary intelligibles, and its subject is external entities. In contrast, logic discusses secondary intelligibles, whose locus of occurrence is only the mind. So how can something external and real be among the individuals of the subject of mental things? As for usul al-fiqh and fiqh, the analogy of logic and philosophy is not correct with respect to both. Because usul al-fiqh also discusses the states of external existents. Thus, the subjects of usuli issues, e.g., command, prohibition, etc., exist externally, and the detailed evidence of fiqh, such as 'establish prayer', 'give zakat', 'do not eat usury', etc., are also external individuals. Therefore, the individuals of an external subject can be external individuals, but it is impossible for an external individual to be an individual of a mental subject.

The author has made a marginal note here, which is: "Know that when we say 'this is commanded, and everything commanded is obligatory', then the minor is established by detailed evidence, the major is from usul, and the accidental quality of the combination of the two premises is from logic. The point is that the science of logic is an instrumental science; its relationship and necessity to every science and art."
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by the author of Ashraf al-Nu'ut (commentator on Muslim al-Thubut) against a claim made by the author of Muhkam al-Usul. The author of Muhkam had likened the relationship of usul al-fiqh to fiqh to that of logic to philosophy, and also to the relationship of knowns (ma'lumat) to unknowns (majhulat). The author of Ashraf al-Nu'ut argues that this analogy is false.

The text begins by acknowledging the general principle that intellectual propositions are either self-evident or derived from self-evident premises, and that specific knowns lead to specific unknowns. This necessitates the science of logic as an instrument to protect the mind from error. Similarly, legal rulings (ahkam) derive from revelation, but require a discipline that regulates the evidences—such as command/prohibition, general/specific—and their implications. This discipline is usul al-fiqh, which mediates between the rulings and the evidences, just as logic mediates between the known and unknown. The author then quotes the claim that usuli issues are called 'summary evidences' (adillah ijmal) because their rulings extend to the detailed evidences universally.

The core critique begins when the author states that at first glance, the claim of Muhkam's author is mistaken. Logic relates to all sciences equally as an instrumental science (al-ilm al-ali), teaching the method of inference. Usul al-fiqh, however, does not relate to fiqh in the same instrumental way because the detailed evidences of fiqh (e.g., the verse 'give zakat') are themselves individuals (afrad) of the subject matter of usul al-fiqh. For example, the usuli principle 'al-amr li al-wujub' (the command indicates obligation) has as its subject the word 'command' (al-amr), and the actual imperative forms in revelation (like 'establish prayer') are its individuals. Thus, fiqh's detailed evidences fall under usul's subject, meaning usul is not merely an instrument but a science whose subject includes the very evidences of fiqh.

In contrast, logic and philosophy have separate subject matters. Philosophy deals with external entities (a'yan kharijiyya) and uses primary intelligibles (ma'qulat uwali), while logic deals with secondary intelligibles (ma'qulat thaniyya) which exist only in the mind. The minor premise in a philosophical syllogism (e.g., 'the celestial sphere has a single nature') is an external reality, not a mental concept, so it cannot be an individual of logic's mental subject. Therefore, the analogy fails. For usul and fiqh, both deal with external existents (e.g., commands and prohibitions are real utterances), so fiqh's evidences can be individuals of usul's subject.

A marginal note clarifies that in a syllogism like 'this is commanded, and everything commanded is obligatory', the minor is from fiqh (detailed evidence), the major is from usul (summary evidence), and the form of syllogism is from logic. Thus logic remains instrumental, but usul is not merely instrumental; it has a substantive subject matter.

This passage is important for understanding the Hanafi usul tradition's view of the relationship between usul and fiqh: usul is not just a logical tool but a science whose subject matter (the sources and their implications) includes the very evidences of fiqh. It guards against the misunderstanding that usul al-fiqh is merely an instrument like logic.

Key Terms
دلیل تفصیلی (dalil tafsili): A specific evidence from revelation (Quran or hadith) that directly indicates a ruling for a particular act, e.g., 'give zakat' (āyat al-zakāt).
دلیل اجمالی (dalil ijmalī): A general usuli principle that applies to multiple detailed evidences, e.g., 'al-amr li al-wujub' (command indicates obligation). It is called 'summary' because it encompasses many instances universally.
معقولات ثانیه (ma'qulat thaniyya): Concepts that exist only in the mind, such as subject, predicate, universal, particular. Logic deals with these.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author of Ashraf al-Nu'ut reject the analogy between usul-fiqh relation and logic-philosophy relation?
A) Because logic is a revealed science, while usul is rational.
B) Because usul al-fiqh's subject matter (e.g., command) is external and includes the detailed evidences of fiqh as its individuals, whereas logic's subject (secondary intelligibles) is mental and does not include philosophical external realities.
C) Because the author of Muhkam al-Usul was not a Hanafi.
D) Because usul al-fiqh has no connection to detailed evidences.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is not merely an instrumental science like logic; its subject matter includes the actual detailed evidences of fiqh as its individuals, giving it a substantive connection to revelation.

Defending the Definition of Fiqh: Objections and the Role of Rasm
Defending the definition of fiqh against two objections and clarifying the role of rasm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two objections to the Hanafi definition of fiqh, explain the author's response using rasm, and evaluate the super-commentator's critique regarding the type of lazim.

Core Idea
A definition of fiqh as 'knowledge of rulings' is defended as a rasm using a necessary concomitant, but later scholars refine the condition of the lazim.

In this passage, the commentator defends the classic Hanafi definition of fiqh (العلم بالأحكام) against two objections. The second objection's response leads to a further difficulty that is resolved by clarifying that the definition is a rasm, not a hadd. However, a super-commentator notes that the chosen lazim is not predicated, so it would be invalid; the author responds by citing the early scholars' practice of using mubayinat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and the two objections
State the famous definition of fiqh as 'knowledge of the rulings from detailed evidences'. Then, from the passage, identify the two earlier objections that were answered: the first concerning the need for acquired knowledge, the second concerning the meaning of 'adillah' as indicators.
The first objection is resolved by taking 'ilm as acquired knowledge; the second by taking 'adillah as imarat.
2
Trace the consequence of the second response
The author's answer to the second objection (that 'adillah means imarat) implies that the definition produces 'knowledge of the obligation to act'. This seems to restrict fiqh to only the category of wujub, which is problematic.
The new difficulty is that fiqh would then exclude knowledge of the other four categories of rulings.
3
Analyze the rasm defense
The author responds by stating that the definition is a rasm, not a hadd. In a rasm, it is permissible to use a necessary concomitant (lazim) of the definiendum. Here, the obligation to act (wujub al-amal) is a lazim of knowledge of rulings.
Rasm by lazim is valid because the lazim helps distinguish the definiendum.
4
Evaluate the super-commentator's critique and resolution
The super-commentator (in the hashiya) observes that the lazim used is not predicated (mamluk) but real (tahqeeqi), and definition by a real lazim is not valid according to later usul. The author counters by citing the early scholars (qudama') who allowed definition even by distinct (mubayin) factors.
Thus, the definition stands as valid according to the early Hanafi method.

Source Text

علم کا جزم مقلد کے لئے قول مجتہد ہے اور مجتہد کے لئے مجبتد کان ہے۔ اور دونوں میں بڑا فرق ہے۔ قوله - نعم يلزم أن يكون عبارة عن العلم الخ فقہ کی تعریف مشہور کی جامعیت و مانعیت پر جو دواعتراضات وارد ہوئے تھے دونوں کا جواب مصنف نے دے دیا تھا۔ اول کا جواب لان المراد المملکۃ اور دوم کا جواب لان المراد بالا دلہ الامارات سے دیا لیکن اعتراض دوم کے جواب پر ایک اشکال لازم آتا ہے اس اشکال کو مصنف نے اپنے قول نعم ملزم ان یکون الخ سے بیان کیا ہے۔

اشکال کی تقریر : اعتراض دوم کے جواب کی تقریر سے واضح ہے کہ ادلہ سے امارات مراد ہیں اور امارات اس ظن کا افادہ کرتا ہے جو مجتہد کو وجوب العمل بالا حکام کے علم تک پہونچاتا ہے مگر اس سے یہ لازم آ رہا ہے کہ تعریف فقہ میں اعلم بالا حکام سے العلم بوجوب العمل بالا حکام مراد ہو کیونکہ آپ نے ادلہ سے امارات مراد لیا ہے کہ امارات وجوب العمل بالا حکام کے علم تک مفضی ہوتا ہے۔ اس تقدیر پر فقہ علم بالا حکام کا نام نہیں رہجائے گا بلکہ فقہ، العلم بوجوب العمل بالا حکام کا نام ہو جائے گا پس وجوب صوم وصلوۃ، حرمت زنا و شرب خمر وغیرہ احکام فقہ میں داخل نہ رہیں گے بلکہ ان احکام پر عمل کے علم ہونے کا نام فقہ قرار پائے گا حالانکہ یہ تصریحات فقہاء کے خلاف ہے کیونکہ فقہ تو نفس احکام کے علم کا نام ہے ان احکام پر عمل کے واجب ہونے کے علم نام نہیں۔

علاوہ ازیں اعلم بالا حکام سے اعلم بوجوب العمل بالا حکام مراد لینے پر فقہ اپنے اقسام خمسہ یعنی وجوب، حرمت، ندب، اباحت اور کراہت میں سے صرف اور صرف ایک قسم وجوب پر محدود و منحصر ہوکر رہے گا حالانکہ فقہ کا اطلاق احکام کے اقسام خمسہ پر ہوتا ہے۔

قوله الا أن يقال انه رسم فيجوز باللازم

اس عبارت میں اعتراض مذکور کا جواب مسطور ہے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ در حقیقت فقہ تو علم احکام ہی کا نام ہے مگر علم بوجوب العمل بالا حکام سے اس لئے تعبیر کیا جارہاہے کہ علم احکام کے لئے علم وجوب عمل لازم ہے۔ چونکہ یہ تعریف حدی نہیں ہے بلکہ رسی ہے اور شیء کی تعریف رسمی اس کے لازم سے صحیح ہوتی ہے چنانچہ یہ ظاہر ہے کہ احکام شرعیہ کے جانے کالازمہ اس پر عمل کرتا ہے بنابر ایں وجوب عمل علم احکام شرعیہ کے لئے لازم ٹہرا۔ لہذا اب یہ لازم نہیں آئے گا کہ وجوب صوم وصلوۃ اور حرمت زنا و شرب خمر و غیر حا فقہ میں نہ رہیں البتہ اگر یہ تعریف حدی ہوتی تو اعتراض بجا ہوتا۔ قوله فيه مافيه : درج بالا جواب کے ضعف کی طرف اشارہ ہے وجہ ضعف یہ ہے کہ یہ صحیح ہے که تعریف رسمی لازم سے صحیح ہے لیکن علی الاطلاق شئی کی تعریف ہر لازم سے (خواہ لا زم محمولہ ہو یا لازم تحقیقیہ صحیح نہیں ہے بشئی کی تعریف اس لازم سے صحیح ہے جو لازم کہ اپنے ملزوم پر محمول ہو یعنی لوازم محمولہ کے قبیل سے ہو اور اس مقام پر علم وجوب عمل گرچہ علم احکام کے لئے لازم ہے تاہم یہ لازم ( وجوب عمل ) اپنے ملزوم (علم احکام ) پر محمول نہیں ہوتا ہے کیونکہ یہ نہیں کہا جاتا ہے کہ علم وجوب عمل کا نام علم احکام ہے غرض علم وجوب احکام علم احکام کے لئے لوازم تحقیقیہ کے قبیل سے ہے لہذ . اس لازم سے تعریف صحیح نہیں اس مفہوم کی طرف مصنف نے اپنے حاشیہ میں اشارہ کیا ہے۔

اشارة الى انه لازم من حيث الوجود فليس بمحمول فلايكون معرفا جواب:۔ یہ ہے کہ رسم مبائن سے بھی جائز ہے جیسا کہ قدماء سے مروی ہے چنانچہ قدماء تعریف میں مبائنات ذکر کرنے میں حرج نہیں محسوس کرتے لہذا وجوب عمل گو کہ علم احکام پر محمول نہیں ہے کہ مبائن ہے پھر بھی اس سے تعریف بر بنائے مذہب قد ماء صحیح ہے۔

قوله من ههنا علمت اندفاع ماقيل الفقه من باب الظنون الخ اس عبارت سے ایک اعتراض پھر اس کے جواب کی طرف اشارہ ہے قوم نے فقہ کی تعریف جو اعلم سے کی ہے اس پر اعتراض ہے کہ العلم" سے فقہ کی تعریف کرنا صحیح نہیں ورنہ فقہ کا ، متد بہ حصہ جیسے قیاس خبر واحد اور اجماع منقول عن الواحد فقہ سے خارج ہو جائے گا کیونکہ علم اعتقاد جازم اور یقین کامل کا نام ہے اور جبکہ فقہ کے اکثر مسائل قیاس ، خبر واحد اور اجماعات منقولہ سے ثابت ہیں اور سب از قبیل ظنیات ہیں پس جو از قبیل ظنیات ہیں وہ فقہ میں کیونکر داخل ہوں گے جس کو علم یعنی اعتقاد جازم سے مقید کر دیا گیا ہے۔ جواب :۔ اس کا جواب ما سبق میں گذر چکا اور وہ یہ ہے کہ فقہ وجوب عمل بالا حکام کے علم سے عبارت ہے اور اسطرح کا علم بذریعہ امارات مجتہد ہی کو حاصل ہوتا ہے پھر یہ احکام گر چه ادلہ ظنیہ خبر واحد، قیاس
For the muqallid, the definitive ruling is the statement of the mujtahid; for the mujtahid, it is his ijtihad. There is a big difference between them. His statement: 'Yes, it necessarily follows that it is an expression of knowledge...' The author had answered the two objections regarding the comprehensiveness and exclusiveness of the famous definition of fiqh. The first objection was answered by 'because what is meant is the acquired knowledge' and the second by 'because what is meant by evidences are indicators'. But upon the answer to the second objection, a difficulty arises. The author expressed this difficulty with his statement 'Yes, it necessarily follows that it is...' The explanation of the difficulty: It is clear from the explanation of the answer to the second objection that by 'adillah' are meant 'imarat' (indicators), and these indicators produce the conjecture that leads the mujtahid to the knowledge of the obligation to act upon the rulings. But from this it follows that in the definition of fiqh, 'ilm bil-ahkam' means 'ilm bi wujub al-'amal bil-ahkam', because you interpreted 'adillah' as indicators that lead to the knowledge of the obligation to act upon the rulings. According to this assumption, fiqh would no longer be called knowledge of the rulings, but rather knowledge of the obligation to act upon them. Then the obligation of fasting and prayer, the prohibition of adultery and drinking wine, etc., would not be included in fiqh; rather, fiqh would be the name of knowing that these rulings must be acted upon. This contradicts the clear statements of the jurists, because fiqh is the name of knowledge of the rulings themselves, not knowledge of the obligation to act upon them. Moreover, taking 'ilm bil-ahkam' to mean 'ilm bi wujub al-'amal bil-ahkam' would restrict fiqh to only one of the five categories (obligation, prohibition, recommendation, permissibility, and disapproval), namely obligation, whereas fiqh applies to all five categories. His statement: 'Except that it is said that it is a definition by description (rasm), so it is permissible by a necessary concomitant.' In this phrase, the answer to the mentioned objection is recorded. The summary of the answer is that fiqh in reality is indeed knowledge of the rulings themselves, but it is expressed as knowledge of the obligation to act because knowledge of the rulings necessarily entails knowledge of the obligation to act. Since this definition is not a hadd (essential definition) but rather a rasm (descriptive definition), and a thing's rasm definition is correct by its necessary concomitant. It is apparent that the necessary concomitant of knowing the legal rulings is acting upon them. Therefore, the obligation to act is a necessary concomitant of knowledge of the legal rulings. Hence, it will no longer follow that the obligations of fasting and prayer and the prohibitions of adultery and drinking wine, etc., are not included in fiqh. However, if this definition were a hadd, the objection would be valid. His statement: 'There is something in it': This points to the weakness of the above answer. The reason for the weakness is that it is correct that a rasm definition is valid by a necessary concomitant, but absolutely, a thing's definition is not correct by every necessary concomitant (whether it is a predicated necessary or a real necessary). A thing's definition is correct by that necessary concomitant which is predicated on its subject (i.e., of the category of predicated necessities). In this place, knowledge of the obligation to act is indeed a necessary concomitant of knowledge of the rulings, but this necessary concomitant (obligation to act) is not predicated on its subject (knowledge of rulings), because it is not said that 'knowledge of the obligation to act is called knowledge of the rulings'. In essence, knowledge of the obligation to act is of the category of real necessities, so a definition by this necessary concomitant is not correct. The author pointed to this meaning in his margin. The answer: It is that a rasm definition by a distinct (mubayin) factor is also permissible, as is narrated from the early scholars. The early scholars did not find any harm in mentioning distinct factors in a definition. Hence, even though the obligation to act is not predicated on knowledge of the rulings and is distinct, still a definition by it is correct according to the school of the early scholars. His statement: 'From here you know the repulsion of what was said that fiqh is of the category of conjecture...' This phrase points to another objection and its answer. An objection is made on the definition of fiqh from the term 'ilm' that defining fiqh by 'ilm' is not correct, otherwise the predominant part of fiqh, such as qiyas, khabar wahid, and ijma' transmitted by one, would be excluded from fiqh. Because 'ilm' is the name of definitive belief and complete certainty, whereas most issues of fiqh are established by qiyas, khabar wahid, and transmitted ijma's, and all are of the category of conjectural matters. So how can what is conjectural be included in fiqh which is restricted to 'ilm' i.e., definitive belief? The answer: Its answer has already passed in what preceded, and it is that fiqh is expressed as knowledge of the obligation to act upon the rulings, and this kind of knowledge is obtained by the mujtahid through indicators. Then these rulings, even though they are from conjectural evidences like khabar wahid and qiyas...
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the definition of fiqh from Muslim al-Thubut, addressing two objections raised against the definition. The author first responds to the second objection, clarifying that the term 'adillah' in the definition refers to 'imarat' (indicators) that lead to the knowledge of the obligation to act (wujub al-'amal). This raises a further issue: if 'ilm' means knowledge of the obligation to act, then fiqh would be limited to only that knowledge, excluding knowledge of the rulings themselves. The author explains that this is acceptable because the definition is a 'rasm' (descriptive definition) using a necessary consequent (lazim), not a 'hadd' (essential definition). However, a super-commentator (hashiya) notes that this consequent is a 'lazim tahqeeqi' (real necessary) not a 'mamluk' (predicated), so it cannot properly define. The answer is that the early scholars (qudama') allowed definition by mutabayin (distinct) factors. Then a new objection is raised: fiqh is often based on speculative evidences (zanniyat) like qiyas and khabar wahid, yet the definition uses 'ilm' which implies certainty. The response is that the 'ilm' intended is the knowledge of the obligation to act, which is certain for the mujtahid even if the evidence is speculative.

Key Terms
الفقه (al-fiqh): Knowledge of the legal rulings (or, after response, knowledge of the obligation to act) derived from detailed evidences. The passage discusses its definition as a rasm.
الرسم (al-rasm): A descriptive definition using necessary concomitants or distinct features rather than essential properties.
اللازم (al-lazim): A necessary concomitant. Two types: mamluk (predicated, e.g., writer from human) and tahqeeqi (real, e.g., obligation to act from knowledge of rulings).
مبائن (mubayin): A distinct factor that is not necessarily concomitant but helps distinguish the thing defined.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what kind of definition does the author claim the famous definition of fiqh (العلم بالأحكام) is, in order to defend against the objection that it would limit fiqh to only one category (wujub)?
A) A hadd (essential definition)
B) A rasm (descriptive definition) by necessary concomitant
C) A rasm by distinct (mubayin) factor
D) A definition by example

Key Takeaway
The definition of fiqh is defended as a rasm (descriptive definition) using a necessary concomitant, though later scholarship refines the conditions for such definitions.

The Universality of Science Names: Four Estimations
Conceptual analysis of science name universality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain each of the four estimations through which the names of sciences are proven to be universals (kulli) and apply this principle to defining the subject matter of a science in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Science names are universal, not proper—each estimation shows collective plurality making them generic.

Is 'Fiqh' a proper name for a specific body of knowledge, or a universal that applies to all instances of that knowledge? In Hanafi usul, the names of sciences must be universal for the definition of a science to hold across all its issues. This passage from Ashraf al-Nu'ut resolves the objection by showing four ways in which the name of a science is universal, countering the claim that it might be particular.

Guided Path
1
First Estimation: Collection of Issues
Understand that the collection of issues (majmūʻ al-masāʼil) is a particular set in reality, but it has multiplicity adh-hanan (mentally) because different minds can conceive different subsets or aspects. That mental multiplicity suffices for universality.
The key is that universality does not require actual external multiplicity; mental multiplicity is enough.
2
Second Estimation: Collection of Perceptions
The collection of perceptions of issues (majmūʻ idrākāt al-masāʼil) has as its individuals the sciences that exist in many minds. Since there are many minds, there are many individuals, making the name universal.
This estimation focuses on the subjective existence of science in multiple knowers.
3
Third Estimation: Mental Faculty (Malaka)
The mental faculty of knowing the issues (malaka) cannot itself be multiple in one person, but the individuals of that faculty are the faculties present in many scholars' minds. The universality of the name stems from its applicability to those multiple individuals.
The faculty is one per scholar, but multiple scholars make multiple individuals.
4
Fourth Estimation: Considerable Number
The considerable number (qadr muʻtabar bi-hi) has no fixed limit, and the actually extracted issues also have no fixed limit as they increase daily. This indefinite extensibility gives the name a universal scope.
This estimation emphasizes the open-ended nature of a science's issues.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چاروں تقادیر پر اسماء علوم کے کلی ہونے میں کوئی شبہ نہیں رہ جاتا ہے اس لئے کہ بر تقدیر اول مجموعہ مسائل گرچہ ایسا امر شخص ہے کہ گھٹ بڑھ نہ سکے تاہم اذہان کے اعتبار سے اس میں تکثر وتعدد ہونا امر مشاہد ہے اور کسی امر شخصی کو کلی ہونے کے لئے فقط اس قدر تکثر کافی ہے۔ یونہی تقدیر دوم پر بھی کلی ہے کیونکہ مجموعه ادراکات مسائل کے افراد وہ علوم ہوتے ہیں جو اذھان کثیرہ میں موجود و ثابت میں اور اس پر کلی صادق آتی ہے۔ تیسری تقدیر پر کی اس لئے ہے کہ ملکہ کے افراد کا تعدد اور پھر اس افراد پر ملکہ کا صدق ملکہ کے کثرت محال کے اعتبار سے ہے اور محال اذھان علماء ہیں۔ اس طرح چوتھی تقدیر پر بھی کلی ہے کیونکہ قدر معتد بہ کے لئے کوئی حد متعین نہیں ہوتی رہے وہ مسائل جو بالفعل مستخرجہ ہیں اس کے لئے بھی کسی حد کا تعین نہیں کیا جا سکتا اس لئے کہ مسائل دن بدن بڑھتے رہتے ہیں۔ الغرض ان محتملات اربہ کی بنیاد پر اسماء علوم اسماء اجناس ہیں اس لئے مصنف کا مذہب حق ہے۔
There remains no doubt in the universality of the names of sciences according to the four estimations. Because on the first estimation, the collection of issues, although it is a particular matter that cannot increase or decrease, yet according to minds, multiplicity and plurality in it is witnessed, and for something particular to be universal, this extent of multiplicity is sufficient. Similarly, on the second estimation, it is also universal because the individuals of the collection of perceptions of issues are the sciences that exist and are established in many minds, and universality applies to it. On the third estimation, it is because of the multiplicity of the individuals of the faculty (malakah) and then the applicability of the faculty to those individuals is in terms of the impossibility of multiplicity of the faculty, and the loci are the minds of scholars. Thus, on the fourth estimation, it is also universal because for a considerable number, no limit is determined, and for those issues that are actually extracted, no limit can be determined because issues keep increasing day by day. In short, on the basis of these four probabilities, the names of sciences are generic names, therefore the author's opinion is correct.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage addresses the objection that the names of sciences (like Fiqh, Usul) might be proper names (particular) rather than universals. The author demonstrates that regardless of which interpretation we adopt—(1) the collection of issues, (2) the collection of perceptions, (3) the mental faculty, or (4) the considerable number—each yields a universal meaning. This is a conceptual analysis defending the view that science names are generic (asmāʼ ajnās), a necessary premise for defining the subject matter of a science.

Key Terms
كلي (kullī): Universal; applies to multiple individuals or instances.
مجموع مسائل (majmūʻ masāʼil): Collection of issues; the set of all rulings or topics belonging to a science.
مجموع ادراکات (majmūʻ idrākāt): Collection of perceptions; the mental comprehension of the issues of a science.
ملکہ (malaka): Mental faculty; a stable disposition enabling the recall and application of a science's issues.
قدر معتد بہ (qadr muʻtabar bi-hi): Considerable number; a quantity considered sufficient for the name to apply universally without a fixed limit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, on the first estimation, the collection of issues is considered universal because:
A) It can increase or decrease in reality.
B) It has multiplicity according to minds, even if it is particular in itself.
C) It is a proper name that applies to only one thing.
D) It is the same as the mental faculty.

Key Takeaway
The names of sciences are universals (kulli) across four distinct estimations, each proving that the name applies to multiple individuals, not a single particular.

The Subject of Usul al-Fiqh and the Concept of Essential Accident
Definition and expansion of essential accident and subject matter of usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the subject of usul al-fiqh as the four proofs in summary, and distinguish between direct and coextensive-mediated essential accidents.

Core Idea
The subject of a science is defined by what attaches to it essentially, directly or via a coextensive medium.

This passage introduces two foundational concepts: the 'subject' (mawḍūʿ) of a science and the 'essential accident' (ʿaraḍ dhātī). Together they define what usul al-fiqh actually studies – not every attribute of the proofs, but only those that belong to them essentially. The commentator uses examples from grammar to illustrate how accidents can be predicated at different levels, and clarifies the technical definition of essential accident from Mulla Jalal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of the subject of a science
Look at the statement: 'The subject of every science is that in which its essential accidents are investigated.' Note that the investigation refers back to this subject.
2
Understand the two types of essential accident
An essential accident can attach directly (lā bi-wāsiṭa) or through a coextensive medium (bi-wāsiṭatin musāwiyatin). The medium must be equal in scope to the thing.
The example: 'laughter' attaches directly to 'laughing person', but attaches to 'man' through 'laughing person' as a coextensive medium.
3
Distinguish the four modes of accident predication
Accidents can be predicated of: (1) the subject itself, (2) a type of the subject, (3) an essential accident of the subject, or (4) a type of an essential accident. The passage gives grammar examples for each.
For usul al-fiqh, the subject is the four proofs; accidents like 'specific' and 'general' are predicated of them.
4
Apply the definition to usul al-fiqh
The passage concludes: the subject of usul al-fiqh is the four proofs (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas) in summary, and scholars investigate their essential accidents such as specific, general, ruling, etc.
This defines the scope of the discipline.
5
Check the condition of coextensiveness
For a mediated essential accident, the medium must be coextensive (musāwin) with the thing. If it is broader or narrower, the accident is not essential to that science.
E.g., 'animal' is not coextensive with 'man', so 'animal' is not an essential accident of 'man' in this sense.

قوله وموضوعه -
تعريف موضوع علم : ملا جلال میں ہے۔ موضوع كل علم ما يبحث فيه عن عوارضه الذاتية اى يرجع البحث اليه
یعنی فن کا موضوع وہ ہوتا ہے جس میں اس کے عوارض ذاتیہ سے بحث کی جاتی ہے یعنی وہی مرجع بحث ہوتا ہے، اور تعریف عرض ذاتی اسطرح کی جاتی ہے الـعــرض الـذاتـي ما يعرض للشئي اما اولاً وبالذات واما بواسطة امر مساوٍ لذالك الشيء ۔ یعنی عرض ذاتی وہ ہے جو شئی کو یا تو اولا و بالذات یا اس شئی کے امر مساوی کے واسطہ سے لاحق ہو۔
فن میں اعراض سے بحث کرنے کے معنی یہ ہیں۔ کہ یا تو وہ اعراض اس علم کے موضوع پر محمول ہو سکتے ہوں جیسے تحویوں کا قول "الكلمة اما معرب اپنی اس میں اعراب و بنا علم نحو کے موضوع الکلمہ پر محمول ہے۔ یادہ اعراض اس علم کے موضوع کے انواع پرمحمول ہوتے ہوں جیسے " الحروف كلها مبنية" اس مثال میں بنائیت کا حمل موضوع علم پر نہیں بلکہ موضوع علم کی قسم حروف پر ہے چونکہ کلمہ نحو کا موضوع ہے اور حروف کلمہ کی ایک نوع ہے...... یادہ اعراض اس کے اعراض ذاتیہ پر محمول ہوتے ہوں جیسے المعرب اما لفظي او تقديري ۔ اس مثال میں لفظي و تقديري کا حمل موضوع علم کلمہ کی عرض ذاتی یعنی معرب پر ہے۔ ياوہ اعراض اس علم کے اعراض ذاتیہ کے انواع پر محمول ہوں جیسے المعرب اللفظي اما مرفوع او منصوب او مجرور‘ اس مثال میں رفعیت و نصبیت اور مجروریت کا حمل موضوع علم کلمہ کی عرض ذاتی جو معرب ہے اس کی نوع لفظي پر ہے۔ رہے عرض ذاتی تو اس کی تعریف گذر چکی ہے کہ شی کی عرض ذاتی وہ کہلاتی ہے جو شی پر اولا و بالذات بلا واسطہ محمول ہوتی ہے جیسے متعجب کا حمل انسان پر بلا واسطہ ہوتا ہے یا امر مساوی کے واسطہ سے محمول ہو جیسے ضاحک کہ اسکا حمل حقیقت میں متعجب پر ہوتا ہے اور متعجب کے واسطے سے انسان پر ہوتا ہے اس مفہوم کو ملا جلال میں ان الفاظ کے ساتھ ادا کیا گیا ہے۔ ” وهى الخارج المحمول الذى يلحق الشئى لذاته او لما يساويه لذاته“ عارض ہونے کا معنی یہ ہوتا ہے کہ کسی دوسری شئی کے ساتھ لاحق ہوئے بغیر یا بلا واسطہ شئی کو لاحق ہو اور امر مساوی کے واسطہ سے لاحق ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہوتا ہے کہ وہ واسطہ ذوالواسطہ کے ساتھ صدق و تحقق میں مساوی ہو۔ حاصل یہ کہ اولاً وبالذات یا لذاتہ کی قید سے واسطہ فی العروض کی نفی اور واسطہ فی الثبوت کی دو قسموں میں سے ایک تہ جس میں واسطه وذ والواسطہ صفت کے ساتھ حقیقہ متصف ہوتا ہے کی نفی مقصود ہے البتہ وہ عرض جوشئی کو امر مساوی کے واسطہ سے عارض ہو اصل میں دونوں منفی واسطوں میں سے ایک کا اثبات ہوتا ہے جس کی طرف " اما بواسطة“ سے اشارہ ہے لیکن اس شرط کے ساتھ کہ وہ واسطہ ذوالواسطہ کے ساتھ صدق و تحقق میں مساوی ہو۔
خلاصہ کلام یہ ہے کہ جو عرض ذاتی فن میں مجوث ہے اس میں معتبر یہ ہے کہ وہ شئی کو بلا واسطہ لاحق ہو جیسے کہ تعجب انسان کو یا وہ معتبر ہے جو لاحق ہوشی کو واسطہ فی الثبوت کی دو قسموں میں سے ایک قسم کے واسطہ سے۔ اور وہ قسم ہوتی ہے جس میں صرف ذوا لواسطہ صفت کے ساتھ بالذات متصف ہوتا ہے اور واسطہ کی حیثیت سفیر محض کی ہوتی ہے جیسے الصابغ للخطوب ۔ لیکن وہ عرض جوشی کو کسی دوسر ی شی کے واسطے سے واسطہ فی العروض کے طور پر عارض ہو یا واسطہ فی الثبوت کی دوسری قسم جس میں واسطہ وذ والواسطہ دونوں بالذات صفت سے متصف ہوتے ہیں تو ان دونوں سے فن میں اس وقت بحث ہوتی ہے جب یہ واسطہ ذوالواسطہ کے مساوی ہو ۔
قوله الادلة الاربعة اجمالا-الخ
یعنی اصول فقہ کا موضوع ادلہ اربعہ اجمالا ہے وہ کتاب اللہ سنت رسول اللہ ، اجماع اور قیاس ہیں جن کے عوارض ذاتیہ سے بطور اجمال اصولیین بحث کرتے ہیں مثلاً خاص الكتاب كذا، خاص من السنت كذاء الاجماع كذا، وحكمه كذا، عامها كذا و حكمه كذا و غیرہ کہتے ہیں اور کتاب اللہ کی ہر ہر آیت سے
His statement: 'And its subject' - Definition of the subject of a science: In Mulla Jalal: The subject of every science is that in which its essential accidents are investigated, i.e., the investigation refers back to it. That is, the subject of an art is that in which its essential accidents are discussed, i.e., it is the reference point of investigation. And the definition of essential accident is given as: 'The essential accident is that which attaches to a thing either primarily and essentially, or through a medium coextensive with that thing.' That is, an essential accident is that which attaches to a thing either primarily and essentially, or through a coextensive matter. The meaning of discussing accidents in an art is that either those accidents are predicated of the subject of that science, like the grammarians' statement 'The word is either declinable or indeclinable' - here [the accident of] declinability and indeclinability is predicated of the subject of grammar, which is 'word'. Or those accidents are predicated of the types of the subject of that science, like 'All letters are indeclinable' - in this example, indeclinability is not predicated of the subject of the science, but of a type of the subject, the letter, because 'word' is the subject of grammar and 'letter' is a type of word. Or those accidents are predicated of its essential accidents, like 'The declinable is either literal or estimated' - in this example, literal and estimated are predicated of the essential accident of the subject, i.e., declinable. Or those accidents are predicated of the types of the essential accidents of that science, like 'The literal declinable is either nominative, accusative, or genitive' - in this example, nominative, accusative, and genitive are predicated of the type of the essential accident of the subject, which is the literal. As for the essential accident, its definition has already passed: That which is predicated of a thing primarily and essentially without an intermediate, like the predication of 'laughing' of man without an intermediate, or is predicated through a coextensive medium, like 'laughter' - its predication is in reality of 'laughing', and through 'laughing' it is predicated of man. This meaning is expressed in Mulla Jalal with these words: 'And it is the external predicate that attaches to a thing due to its essence or due to what equals it due to its essence.' The meaning of being an accident is that it attaches to a thing without attaching to something else or without an intermediate, and the meaning of attaching through a coextensive medium is that that medium is equal in truth and actualization to the thing with the medium. The conclusion is that the condition 'primarily and essentially' negates the intermediate in the attachment (wasita fi al-urud) and one of the two types of intermediate in the existence (wasita fi al-thubut) where the medium and the thing with the medium are both essentially described with the attribute is intended to be negated. But the accident that attaches to a thing through a coextensive medium is actually the affirmation of one of the two negated intermediates, to which 'or through a medium' points, but with the condition that that medium is equal in truth and actualization to the thing with the medium. The summary is that the essential accident discussed in the art is considered either to attach to the thing without an intermediate, like 'laughter' to man, or it is considered to attach to the thing through one of the two types of intermediate in existence. And that type is the one in which only the thing with the medium is essentially described with the attribute, and the medium is merely a conveyor, like 'one who dyes tribulations'. But the accident that attaches to a thing through another thing by way of intermediate in attachment, or the second type of intermediate in existence where both the medium and the thing with the medium are essentially described with the attribute, then from these two it is discussed in the art only when the medium is equal to the thing with the medium. His statement: 'The four proofs in summary, etc.' That is, the subject of usul al-fiqh is the four proofs in summary: the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, consensus, and analogy. The usul scholars discuss their essential accidents in a summary manner, for example, saying: 'The specific of the Book is such, the specific from the Sunnah is such, consensus is such, its ruling is such, the general of them is such, its ruling is such, etc.' And from every verse of the Book of Allah...
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the subject matter of usul al-fiqh and the concept of essential accident. The commentator begins by quoting the matn's statement 'wa mawdu'uhu' (and its subject) and then defines what is meant by the subject of a science. According to Mulla Jalal (a well-known gloss on the Tahdhib), the subject of any science is that in which its essential accidents (awāriḍ dhātiyya) are investigated. The essential accident is defined as an attribute that attaches to a thing either primarily and directly (lā bi-wāsiṭa) or through a coextensive medium (amr musāwin). The commentator then illustrates with examples from grammar (naḥw): the subject of naḥw is 'word' (kalima), and accidents like declinability are predicated of it. He distinguishes four ways accidents can be discussed: (1) predicted of the subject itself; (2) predicated of a type of the subject; (3) predicated of an essential accident of the subject; (4) predicated of a type of the essential accident. The essential accident itself is then further clarified: it can attach directly (e.g., 'laughter' to 'laughing person') or through a coextensive medium (e.g., 'laughter' attaches to 'man' via 'laughing person'). The condition is that the medium must be equal in scope to the thing. The passage then returns to the main point: the subject of usul al-fiqh is the four proofs (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas) taken in summary, and the scholars investigate their essential accidents such as specific, general, ruling, etc. This establishes the scope of the discipline.

Key Terms
العرض الذاتي (al-ʿaraḍ al-dhātī): An attribute that attaches to a thing either directly or through a coextensive medium due to the thing's essence.
الموضوع (al-mawḍūʿ): The subject matter of a science, which is the locus of investigation of its essential accidents.
الواسطة في الثبوت (al-wāsiṭa fī al-thubūt): A medium in existence; the thing with the medium is essentially described while the medium merely conveys.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the subject of usul al-fiqh?
A) The specific proofs in detail
B) The four proofs (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas) in summary
C) The general principles of Islamic law
D) The essential accidents of legal rulings

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh investigates the essential accidents of the four proofs (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas) in summary, where 'essential' means attaching directly or via a coextensive medium.

The Subject of Usul al-Fiqh: Four Sources in General
Stating that usul al-fiqh deals with the four sources generally

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four sources that constitute the subject matter of usul al-fiqh and explain why usul al-fiqh discusses them only in general terms.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh studies the four sources only in general, leaving detailed analysis to other sciences.

Usul al-fiqh is often misunderstood as a detailed commentary on every verse and hadith. In reality, its scope is precisely defined: it treats the four primary sources only in terms of general principles of interpretation. This lesson clarifies that boundary and explains why specialization across Islamic sciences is necessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Subject Claim
Read the passage and note what the author states as the subject (mawdu') of usul al-fiqh. He says it is the 'four sources in general'.
Remember: 'mawdu' refers to the object of study of a science.
2
List the Four Sources
The four sources are: the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of His Messenger, consensus (ijma'), and analogy (qiyas). Write them down as the foundational sources of Islamic law in the Hanafi school.
Hanafis include qiyas as a source; other schools may differ slightly.
3
Understand 'In General' (Ijmalan)
Usul scholars discuss these sources in terms of their 'essential accidents' (al-awarid al-dhatiyya) — general rulings like specific vs. general, conditions of validity, etc. They do not apply these to every individual verse or hadith.
For example, they say 'the specific of the Book is such' without delving into which verse is specific.
4
Map the Division of Labor
The text explicitly assigns detailed treatment to other sciences: tafsir for Quranic verses, hadith criticism for ahadith and narrators, siyar for consensus specifics, and fiqh for detailed qiyas issues.
This ensures each science maintains its proper scope.
5
Reflect on Hanafi Methodology
The Hanafi tradition emphasizes this systematic boundary to avoid overlap. Usul al-fiqh provides the principles, not the exhaustive application.
This distinction is crucial for proper legal derivation.

Source Text

قوله الادلة الاربعة اجمالا-الخ یعنی اصول فقہ کا موضوع ادلہ اربعہ اجمالا ہے وہ کتاب اللہ سنت رسول اللہ ، اجماع اور قیاس ہیں جن کے عوارض ذاتیہ سے بطور اجمال اصولیین بحث کرتے ہیں مثلاً خاص الكتاب كذا، خاص من السنت كذاء الاجماع كذا، وحکمہ کذا، عامها كذا و حکمہ کذا و غیرہ کہتے ہیں اور کتاب اللہ کی ہر ہر آیت سے تفصیلی بحث علم تفسیر میں ہوتی ہے۔ سنت رسول اللہ میں سے ہر ہر حدیث سے علم حدیث اور ان اسمائے رجال میں بحث کی جاتی ہے اجماع کی تفصیل مع خصوصیات کے علم سیر کا وظیفہ ہے۔ اور قیاس کی تفصیلی نحث اور اس کے مسائل کی خصوصیات فقہ میں بیان ہوتی ہے۔
His statement 'the four sources in general' means that the subject of usul al-fiqh is the four sources in general: they are the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, consensus, and analogy. The scholars of usul discuss them in terms of their essential accidents in a general manner, for example, they say: the specific of the Book is such, the specific from the Sunnah is such, consensus is such, and its ruling is such, the general of them is such and its ruling is such, etc. Detailed discussion of every verse of the Book of Allah occurs in the science of tafsir. Detailed discussion of every hadith from the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah occurs in the science of hadith and the study of narrators. The details of consensus with its particularities is the function of the science of siyar. And the detailed discussion of analogy and its particular issues are explained in fiqh.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage clarifies the subject matter of usul al-fiqh. According to the author, usul al-fiqh deals with the four sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas) only in a general way (ijmalan). That is, it discusses the general rulings regarding these sources, such as the distinction between general and specific terms, the conditions for validity, etc., but it does not delve into the details of every verse or hadith. Those details are left to other sciences: tafsir for the Quran, hadith criticism for the Sunnah, siyar for details of consensus, and fiqh for the particulars of analogy. This distinction is important to define the scope of usul al-fiqh and avoid overlap with other Islamic sciences. The Hanafi tradition emphasizes this methodological division to maintain the specific function of usul as the principles of interpretation and derivation, not exhaustive exegesis.

Key Terms
موضوع (mawdu'): The subject matter of a science; that which the science investigates in terms of its essential accidents.
ادلہ اربعہ (adillah arba'ah): The four sources of Islamic law: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which science is responsible for the detailed discussion of consensus?
A) Usul al-fiqh
B) Siyar
C) Fiqh
D) Tafsir

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh studies the four sources only in general, leaving detailed analysis to specialized sciences like tafsir, hadith, siyar, and fiqh.

Unifying Multiple Subjects: The Concept of Jihah
Responding to the doubt that multiple subjects imply multiple sciences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers usul al-fiqh a single science despite its multiple sources, and apply the concept of jihah to defend the unity of a discipline.

Core Idea
The four sources are unified under one aspect: leading to legal rulings – that makes usul al-fiqh one science.

You have learned that usul al-fiqh deals with the four sources: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. But if there are four distinct subjects, why isn't usul al-fiqh four separate sciences? In this lesson, we explore a classical doubt and its Hanafi solution: the concept of jihah (aspect) unifies them into one discipline.

Guided Path
1
State the doubt (shubha)
Identify the objection: multiplicity of subjects implies multiplicity of sciences, so usul al-fiqh should be multiple sciences.
The doubt is based on a superficial reading of the sources.
2
Identify the Hanafi response
The response argues that multiplicity only leads to multiple sciences when the aspects (jihāt) are different; here all four sources share the same aspect.
The key is the shared aspect.
3
Define jihah and apply it
Jihah is the perspective under which a subject is considered. For usul al-fiqh, the common jihah is īṣāl ilā al-ḥukm al-shar'ī (leading to the legal ruling).
This is the unifying factor.
4
Examine the analogy with logic
The text compares with logic, which studies definition and proof under the common aspect of leading to the unknown, thus being one science.
The analogy reinforces the argument.
5
Understand the consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical outcome: without this argument, usul al-fiqh would lose its status as a single, independent science.
The Hanafi position preserves its unity.

قوله - وهى مشتركة فى الايصال الخ ایک شبہ کا جواب ہے۔ شبہ یہ ہوتا ہے کہ تعدد موضوع تعد دفن پر دلالت کرتا ہے اس لئے ادلہ اربعہ کو موضوع قرار دینے سے علم اصول کا تعد ولا زم آتا ہے۔ جواب : یہ ہے کہ تعدد موضوع تعددفن پر اس وقت دلالت کرتا ہے جب جہات متفائر ہوں لیکن موضوع متعدد ہونے کے باوجود ایک جہت سے ملحوظ ہو تو تعدد موضوع تعددفن پر دلالت نہیں کرتا۔ اسی مفہوم کی طرف ماتن نے اپنے قول وہی مشترکہ فی الا یصال سے اشارہ کیا۔ یعنی ان ادلہ میں سے ہر ایک حکم شرعی تک موصل ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ انہیں سے ہر ایک سے مسئلہ کا استخراج ہوتا ہے پس ادلہ اربعه حکم شرعی تک موصل ہونے میں مشترک ہونے کے اعتبار سے گویا متحد ہے لہذا تعدد موضوع کے با وجود علم اصول متعدد نہ ہو ا چنا نچہ علماء نے تصریح کی ہے کہ اشیاء متعددہ علم واحد کے موضوع ہو سکتے ہیں لیکن اس شرط کے ساتھ کہ اس کو ایک ایسے امر مشترک کے ساتھ مناسبت ہو جس امر میں وہ اشیاء متعددہ بھی مشترک ہوں ۔ حاصل وہی ہے جو مذکور ہوا کہ تعدد موضوع تعدد فن پر اس وقت دلالت کرتا ہے جب ہر ایک کی جہت بھی مختلف ہو اور یہاں ایسا نہیں، بلکہ چاروں کی جہت ایک ہے اور وہ جہت ، جہت ایصال الی حکم شرعی ہے۔ جس طرح منطق کا موضوع معقولات ثانیہ من حیث الا یصال الی الجھول ہے اس کے موضوع میں تعدد ہے کہ اس کا موضوع معرف و حجت ہے اس کے باوجود محمول تک پہنچانے میں مشترک ہونے کے سبب منطق متعدد فن نہیں ہے فائدہ :۔ جب یہ بات واضح ہوگئی کہ اس علم میں ادلہ مذکورہ سے الا یصال الی حکم شرعی کی حیثیت سے بحث ہوتی ہے پس نظر باحث میں یہ حیثیت ایصال یا تو حیثیت تقیید یہ ہے یا حیثیت تعلیلیہ ہوگی جس کا مفاد یہ ہے کہ جمیع مباحث میں یہ معنی کلی ( ایصال ) ملحوظ ہو گا۔ یہ معنی نہیں ہے کہ جمیع عوارض جس سے بحث ہوگی ان عوارض کا لحوق و عروض موضوع کو اس حیثیت کے واسطہ سے ہوگا تا کہ نفس حیثیت
His statement 'and they are shared in leading to [the ruling]' is an answer to a doubt. The doubt is that multiplicity of subjects indicates multiplicity of sciences, so making the four sources the subject necessitates the multiplication of the science of usul. The answer is that multiplicity of subjects indicates multiplicity of sciences only when the aspects (jihāt) are different. But if the subjects are multiple yet considered under one aspect, then multiplicity of subjects does not indicate multiplicity of sciences. The author indicated this meaning by his statement 'they are shared in leading to [the ruling]', meaning that each of these sources leads to a legal ruling in the sense that from each one an issue is derived. So the four sources, by virtue of being shared in leading to a legal ruling, are as if unified. Therefore, despite the multiplicity of subjects, the science of usul is not multiple. As scholars have stated: multiple things can be the subject of a single science, but on condition that they are related to a common matter in which those multiple things share. The conclusion is that multiplicity of subjects indicates multiplicity of sciences only when each has a different aspect, and that is not the case here; rather, all four have one aspect, which is the aspect of leading to a legal ruling. Just as the subject of logic is secondary intelligibles from the aspect of leading to the unknown; its subject is multiple (definition and proof), yet despite that, logic is not multiple sciences because they share in leading to the conclusion. Benefit: When it is clear that in this science the mentioned sources are discussed from the aspect of leading to a legal ruling, then in the view of the researcher, this aspect of leading is either a restrictive aspect (jihah taqyidiyyah) or a causal aspect (jihah ta'liliyyah). Its import is that in all discussions this universal meaning (leading) will be kept in view. It does not mean that all accidents discussed will attach to the subject by virtue of this aspect, so that the aspect itself...
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage addresses a potential objection (shubha) against the unity of usul al-fiqh as a single science. The objection claims that since usul al-fiqh has four distinct subjects (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas), it should actually be four different sciences. The author responds by explaining that multiplicity of subjects only entails multiplicity of sciences if the subjects are considered under different aspects (jihāt mutafā'irah). However, here all four sources are considered under one common aspect: they all lead to the legal ruling (īṣāl ilā al-ḥukm al-shar'ī). This shared function unifies them as a single subject for one science. The author draws an analogy with logic, which also has multiple subjects (ta'rīf and ḥujjah) but is considered one science because both aim at leading to the unknown. The passage concludes with a beneficial note: the researcher must keep in view the universal meaning of 'leading to the ruling' in all discussions. This is a classic Hanafi argument to justify the scope of usul al-fiqh, emphasizing the teleological unity of the sources.

Key Terms
جہت (jihah): The aspect or perspective under which a subject is considered in a science.
ایصال الی حکم شرعی (īṣāl ilā al-ḥukm al-shar'ī): Leading to a legal ruling; the function of the sources to derive fiqh rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What unifies the four sources of Islamic law into a single subject for usul al-fiqh?
A) Their divine origin
B) Their historical occurrence
C) Their shared function of leading to a legal ruling
D) Their linguistic form

Key Takeaway
Multiplicity of subjects does not necessarily split a science; it is the aspect (jihah) under which they are studied that determines unity.
