Why the Four Sources Form One Subject of Usul al-Fiqh
Defending the unity of usul al-fiqh's subject matter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the four sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) constitute a single subject for usul al-fiqh, using the concept of īṣāl and the analogy with logic.

Core Idea
A single aspect (īṣāl) makes multiple evidences one subject — unity of aspect prevents multiplicity of disciplines.

This passage tackles a fundamental doubt: if usul al-fiqh discusses four distinct sources, why isn't it four separate sciences? The commentator answers by highlighting the common aspect of 'leading' (īṣāl) to a legal ruling. Just as logic remains one science despite having multiple subject-matter items (definition and proof) because they share the purpose of leading to the unknown, the four sources share the same purpose of leading to a ruling, so they form one subject. This lesson unpacks this argument and explores what counts as a legitimate topic in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Doubt
Recognize the problem: multiplicity of subject matters (the four sources) seems to necessitate multiple disciplines. What is the basis for this concern?
The doubt is implicit in the matn's phrase; the commentator makes it explicit.
2
Extract the Solution
Find the key condition: multiplicity requires differing aspects (jihāt). Here, all sources share one aspect: īṣāl (leading to a ruling). Copy the sentence that states this principle.
Look for the phrase 'عند اختلاف الجهة'.
3
Analyze the Analogy with Logic
Examine how the analogy from 'ilm al-manṭiq works. Identify the subject (secondary intelligibles), the aspect (leading to the unknown), and the multiple items within that subject (definition and proof). Why does logic remain one science?
The shared aspect overrides the multiplicity of items.
4
Understand the Restrictive vs Causal Aspect
The passage introduces a 'fā'idah' about the aspect being either restrictive (taqyīdiyyah) or causal (ta‘līliyyah). Briefly note what this means for how we consider the sources.
This refines the perspective from which we view each source.
5
Relate Subject of Science to Issues
Review the examples that show how the subject of the science (the four sources) can be directly or indirectly the subject of individual issues. Understand the concept of 'araḍ dhātī (intrinsic accident) and its role in defining valid topics.
This explains why discussions about generality, ambiguity, etc. are part of usul al-fiqh.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله - وهى مشتركة فى الايصال الخ. إيضاح: إشارة إلى جواب شبهة، وهي أن تعدد الموضوع يقتضي تعدد الفنون، فجعل الأدلة الأربعة موضوعاً يلزم منه تعدد علم الأصول. والجواب: أن تعدد الموضوع يقتضي تعدد الفنون عندما تكون الجهات مختلفة، أما إذا كانت الجهة واحدة مع تعدد الموضوع فلا يلزم تعدد الفن. وقد أشار الماتن بقوله "وهى مشتركة فى الايصال" إلى أن كل واحد من هذه الأدلة يوصل إلى الحكم الشرعي من حيث إن منها يستخرج الحكم، فالأدلة الأربعة متحدة باعتبار اشتراكها في الإيصال إلى الحكم الشرعي، فلا يلزم التعدد. وقد نص العلماء على أن الأشياء المتعددة يمكن أن تكون موضوعاً لعلم واحد بشرط مناسبتها لأمر مشترك تشارك فيه. والحاصل: أن تعدد الموضوع يدل على تعدد الفن عند اختلاف الجهة، وليس كذلك هنا، بل الجهة واحدة وهي جهة الإيصال إلى الحكم الشرعي. ومثاله: علم المنطق موضوعه المعقولات الثانية من حيث الإيصال إلى المجهول، وفيه تعدد في الموضوع (المعرف والحجة) ومع ذلك ليس بفنون متعددة لاشتراك جهة الإيصال. فائدة: لما تبين أن البحث في هذا العلم عن الأدلة المذكورة من حيث الإيصال إلى الحكم الشرعي، فالنظر في هذه الجهة إما تقييدية أو تعليلية. والمفاد أن جميع المباحث يلحظ فيها هذا المعنى الكلي (الإيصال)، وليس معناه أن جميع الأعراض التي يبحث عنها تعرض الموضوع بواسطة هذه الجهة، بل قد يبحث عن نفس الجهة كما في علم الطبيعي حيث يبحث عن الجسم من حيث الحركة والسكون، وفيه يبحث عن نفس الحركة والسكون. كذلك في أصول الفقه يبحث عن جهة الإيصال. معنى البحث عن موضوع العلم: ليس معناه أن موضوع العلم يجب أن يكون موضوع المسألة، بل المراد أن موضوع العلم قد يكون موضوعاً للمسألة، مثال: الأدلة الأربعة تكون موضوعاً للمسائل كما في قولنا: الكتاب يفيد القطع بالحكم، الكتاب يكون ناسخاً للكتاب، السنة والقياس يفيدان الظن، الإجماع لا يكون ناسخاً، السنة تكون ناسخاً لمثلها وللكتاب. وقد لا يكون نفس موضوع العلم موضوعاً للمسألة بل نوعه، مثال: أنواع الأدلة الأربعة تكون موضوعات للمسائل: الأمر للوجوب، المجمل يحتاج إلى البيان، التواتر لا يشترط فيه عدد معين. وقد يكون عرض ذاتي لموضوع العلم موضوعاً للمسألة كقولنا: العام يفيد القطع. وقد يكون نوع العرض الذاتي موضوعاً كقولنا: العام المخصوص منه البعض يفيد الظن. بالجملة: مرجع البحث في هذا الفن هو الأدلة وأحوالها. فالأحوال التي تعم موضوعات المسائل إن لم تتجاوز في عمومها موضوع العلم يبحث عنها، بل الأمر الذي يعرض تلك الأحوال إن لم يتجاوز موضوع العلم يبحث عنه أيضاً، لأن الجميع من الأعراض الذاتية التي يبحث عنها في الفن. المختصر: جميع مباحث أصول الفقه إذا كانت بحيث الإيصال الموصل إلى الأحكام فهي أعراض ذاتية للأدلة الأربعة ويصح البحث عنها في الفن.
His saying: "And they are common in leading" etc. Explanation: It is an indication of the answer to a doubt, which is that multiplicity of subject matters necessitates multiplicity of disciplines. So making the four evidences a subject matter would necessitate multiplicity of the science of usul. The answer: That the multiplicity of subject matters necessitates multiplicity of disciplines when the aspects are different. But if the aspect is one despite multiplicity of subject matter, then multiplicity of discipline does not necessarily follow. The matn indicated by his saying "and they are common in leading" that each of these evidences leads to the legal ruling from the perspective that from it the ruling is extracted. So the four evidences are unified in consideration of their sharing in leading to the legal ruling, thus multiplicity does not follow. Scholars have stated that multiple things can be the subject matter of a single science on condition that they have a connection to a common matter in which those multiple things share. Bottom line: Multiplicity of subject matter indicates multiplicity of discipline when the aspect is different. Here it is not so; rather the aspect is one, namely the aspect of leading to the legal ruling. Example: The science of logic, its subject is secondary intelligibles from the aspect of leading to the unknown. There is multiplicity in its subject (definition and proof), yet it is not multiple disciplines because of the shared aspect of leading. Benefit: When it became clear that the investigation in this science concerns the mentioned evidences from the aspect of leading to the legal ruling, then the consideration of this aspect is either a restrictive aspect or a causal aspect. The purport is that in all discussions this universal meaning (leading) is taken into account. It does not mean that all accidents discussed inhere in the subject by virtue of this aspect; rather the aspect itself may be discussed as in natural philosophy where the subject is the body from the aspect of motion and rest, and therein motion and rest themselves are discussed. Similarly in usul al-fiqh, the aspect of leading is discussed. Meaning of investigating the subject of a science: It does not mean that the subject of the science must be the subject of the issue. Rather, the intent is that sometimes the subject of the science becomes the subject of the issue. Example: The four evidences become subjects of issues as in our saying: The Book yields certainty of the ruling; The Book can abrogate the Book; the Sunnah and analogy yield probability; Ijma cannot abrogate; the Sunnah can abrogate its like and the Book. Sometimes the subject of the science itself is not the subject of the issue, but rather its type. Example: Types of the four evidences become subjects of issues: The command indicates obligation; the ambiguous requires explanation; frequency does not require a specific number. Sometimes the intrinsic accident of the subject of the science becomes the subject of the issue like our saying: The general yields certainty. Sometimes the type of the intrinsic accident becomes the subject like our saying: The general from which some is excluded yields probability. In summary: The locus of investigation in this science is the evidences and their states. So those states which are common to the subjects of issues, if they do not exceed the subject of the science in generality, are investigated. Rather, even that which attaches to those states, if it does not exceed the subject of the science, is investigated because all are among the intrinsic accidents investigated in the science. In short: All discussions of usul al-fiqh, if they are in terms of leading to rulings, are intrinsic accidents of the four evidences and it is valid to investigate them in the science.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn's statement "وهى مشتركة فى الايصال" (and they are common in leading). The author addresses a doubt: since usul al-fiqh discusses four distinct sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas), why isn't it four separate disciplines? The answer is that multiplicity of subject matters requires multiplicity of disciplines only when the aspects (jihāt) differ. Here, all four sources share a single aspect: they lead (īṣāl) to a Sharīʿah ruling. Therefore, they can be the subject of one science. The author supports this with the analogy of logic, which has multiple subject-matter types (definition and proof) but is one discipline because they share the aspect of leading to the unknown. A benefit (fāʿidah) clarifies that the aspect of īṣāl is either restrictive or causal, and it is the lens through which all discussions are viewed. The passage then explains how the subject of a science relates to the subjects of issues: sometimes the subject itself becomes a subject of an issue (e.g., 'the Book yields certainty'), sometimes its type, sometimes its intrinsic accident, etc. Ultimately, all valid discussions in usul al-fiqh must relate to the four sources in terms of their being evidence leading to rulings, and such discussions are considered intrinsic accidents (aʿrāḍ dhātiyyah) of the subject.

Key Terms
إيصال (īṣāl): The quality of leading or conducing to a legal ruling; the common aspect that unifies the four sources as a single subject matter.
جهة (jihah): Aspect or perspective from which a thing is considered; used here to argue that a single jihah (īṣāl) prevents multiplicity of disciplines.
عرض ذاتي (ʿaraḍ dhātī): Intrinsic accident; a property that necessarily follows the thing itself, e.g., for the four sources, being leading to rulings is intrinsic.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do the four sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) form a single subject for usul al-fiqh rather than four separate disciplines?
A) Because each source is independent and unrelated to the others.
B) Because they all share a single aspect: leading to a legal ruling.
C) Because usul al-fiqh only considers Quran and Sunnah.
D) Because the matn explicitly states they are one.

Key Takeaway
The four sources are unified under usul al-fiqh because they all share the common aspect of leading to a legal ruling (īṣāl).

12 min
Is Hujjiyah of Ijma and Qiyas a Mas'ala of Fiqh? The Limmi-Inni Distinction
Debate on whether hujjiyah of ijma and qiyas is badihi or nazari

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the limmi-inni distinction to classify a given usul issue as badihi or nazari, and explain how Ibn al-Humam's two statements on hujjiyah of qiyas are reconciled.

Core Idea
Hujjiyah of qiyas is both self-evident (from effect to cause) and theoretical (from cause to effect) — the apparent contradiction dissolves with the definition.

This lesson delves into a subtle debate in Hanafi usul: Is the authoritative nature (hujjiyah) of ijma and qiyas a theoretical issue studied within the discipline, or is it a self-evident truth independent of any field? The passage from Ashraf al-Nu'ut addresses an apparent contradiction in Ibn al-Humam's statements, and resolves it by distinguishing two cognitive pathways — dalil inni (a posteriori) and dalil limmi (a priori). Understanding this distinction deepens your grasp of how usul scholars define the boundaries of their discipline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central claim of the 'speaker'
The passage begins by presenting the view that hujjiyah of ijma and qiyas is not a mas'ala of any discipline because it is a religious necessity (daruriyya diniyya). This view seems to contradict Ibn al-Humam's earlier statement that it is a fiqhi mas'ala. Recognize this as the catalyst for the discussion.
The 'speaker' is Ibn al-Humam according to the commentator.
2
Analyze the matn's refutation using the limmi-inni distinction
The matn argues that from the perspective of dalil inni (effect to cause: the obligation to act proves hujjiyah), hujjiyah appears self-evident because the effect is obvious. But from dalil limmi (cause to effect: hujjiyah is the cause, obligation the effect), it is theoretical because the causal link requires proof. Thus hujjiyah can be both badihi and nazari depending on the perspective.
This is the core analytical move.
3
Examine the second refutation and summary
The second refutation notes that many rulings are established by ijma/qiyas without need for proof, which suggests self-evidence in practice. But in reality (fi nafs al-amr), hujjiyah needs evidence, making it theoretical. Therefore the mas'ala is not part of any discipline in one sense, but is indeed a mas'ala of usul in another.
4
Investigate the tahqiqi answer clearing Ibn al-Humam
The commentator provides the investigative answer: Ibn al-Humam's two statements are conditional on different definitions of qiyas. If qiyas is the mujtahid's act of analogical reasoning, then its hujjiyah is a fiqhi mas'ala (since it involves ijtihad). If qiyas is the Shari' equality in cause, then it is a religious necessity (badihi) and not a mas'ala. Hence no contradiction.
This is the final resolution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله - ومن قال ان الحجية ليست بمسئلة اصلا ان هذه العبارة من ماتن ترقي لكي يظهر اضطراب في كلام ابن الهمام ويرد عليه. المصنف يظهر التعارض هكذا: هذا القائل قال فيما سبق أن "حجية الإجماع والقياس مسئلة فقهية"، ثم قال في موضع آخر أن القياس ليس مسئلة أي فن، لا فقه ولا غيره، لأن حجية الإجماع والقياس من القضايا التي تعد من ضروريات الدينية، أي من الأمور الضرورية البديهية في الدين، بينما كونها مسئلة فن يقتضي أن تكون نظرية ليحصل بالبرهان. وحجية الإجماع والقياس بديهية لأن من يعرف معنى الإجماع والقياس ويفهم مفادهما لا يتوقف في حجيتهما ولا يحتاج إلى دليل وتنبيه. 

ههنا اعتراض: أن الإجماع حجة، الطرفان موضوع ومحمول نظريان، فكيف يكون الحكم بديهيا؟ والجواب: أن الاعتبار في بديهية القياس ونظريته بالحكم، فإذا كان الحكم بديهيا فالقياس بديهي وإن كان الطرفان نظريين. 

ورد المصنف: يقول الماتن هذا القول بعيد عن الحق والصواب، لأن حجية الإجماع والقياس وإن كانت بديهية باعتبار الدليل الإني (من المعلول إلى العلة)، لكنها ليست بديهية باعتبار الدليل اللمي (من العلة إلى المعلول) بل نظرية. وتذكر أن محل البحث: وجوب العمل معلول، وحجية الإجماع والقياس علته. فمقصود الماتن أن حجية الإجماع والقياس وإن كانت بديهية بالنظر إلى معلولها وجوب العمل فلا تكون مسئلة فن، لكن وجوب العمل بالنظر إلى علته حجية الإجماع نظري. 

بلفظ آخر: لا نسلم أن حجية الإجماع والقياس في نفس الأمر لا تحتاج إلى دليل. الحق أنها في نفس الأمر والواقع تحتاج إلى دليل، وإن كان في علمنا لا تحتاج لكثرة الشهرة حتى صارت من ضروريات الدين، لكنها في نفس الأمر ليست بديهية. فلا يصح إطلاقا جعل الحجة ضرورية وخارجة عن العلم. وقد يمكن أن يكون هذا المسئلة من حيث اللم نظرية مطلوبة في الفن، ومن حيث الإني بديهية لا تدخل في فن. 

التقرير الثاني للرد: لا شك أن الأحكام الثابتة بالإجماع والقياس كثيرة، فثبوت تلك الأحكام الكثيرة يدل على علم حجية الإجماع والقياس من حيث أن إثباتها لا يحتاج إلى برهان ونظر، لأنها ثابتة بالإجماع، لكن من جهة اللم كون حجيتهما بديهية غير مسلم، لأن في نفس الأمر يحتاج إقامة الدليل على حجيتهما. خلاصة الكلام: أن مسئلة حجية الإجماع والقياس بديهية باعتبار ثبوت الأحكام بهما وبسبب اشتهارها، فلا تكون مسئلة فن. لكنهما في نفس الأمر نظريان لأن نفس الأمر هو المدار لثبوت الأحكام بهما، فهي مسئلة فن من هذه الجهة. 

قال المصنف في حاشيته على قوله "ومن قال": أي القائل ابن الهمام. انتهى. 

الجواب التحقيقي: التحقيق أن هذا الانتساب إلى الشيخ ابن الهمام واضطراب في كلامه ليس بصحيح، فإنه قال في مقدمة تحريره بعد قوله "إنها من الفقه": وهو في القياس على تقدير كونه فعل المجتهد، وأما على أنه المساواة الكائنة عن تسوية الله تعالى بين الأصل والفرع في العلة فليست مسئلة لأنها ضرورية دينية. يعني أن ما قلنا إن حجية القياس مسئلة فقهية لا أصولية، ذلك على تقدير أن القياس فعل المجتهد، وأما على تقدير أن القياس هو المساواة التي جعلها الله بين الأصل والفرع في العلة، فليست مسئلة لأنها ضرورية دينية.
His statement: 'And whoever said that hujjiyah is not a mas'ala at all' - The matn proceeds with this expression to show inconsistency in Ibn al-Humam's speech and refute him. The author shows the contradiction thus: this speaker had said previously that 'hujjiyah of ijma and qiyas is a fiqhi mas'ala,' then he said in another place that qiyas is not a mas'ala of any discipline, neither fiqh nor other, because hujjiyah of ijma and qiyas is among propositions that are counted as religious necessities, i.e., among matters that are necessary and self-evident in religion, whereas being a mas'ala of a discipline requires it to be theoretical so that it can be attained through proof. And hujjiyah of ijma and qiyas is self-evident because whoever knows the meaning of ijma and qiyas and understands their import does not hesitate in their hujjiyah and does not need evidence or alert. 

Here an objection: That ijma is a proof, both subject and predicate are theoretical, so how can the ruling be self-evident? The answer: Consideration in the self-evidence or theoretically of qiyas is based on the ruling. So if the ruling is self-evident, then qiyas is self-evident even if the two sides are theoretical. 

And the author's refutation: The matn says this statement is far from truth and correctness, because hujjiyah of ijma and qiyas, although self-evident in terms of the 'inna' proof (from effect to cause), is not self-evident in terms of the 'limma' proof (from cause to effect) but rather theoretical. Remember that the subject under discussion: obligation to act is the effect, and hujjiyah of ijma and qiyas is its cause. So the matn's intent is that hujjiyah of ijma and qiyas, although self-evident in relation to its effect (obligation to act), thus cannot be a mas'ala of a discipline, but the obligation to act, in relation to its cause (hujjiyah of ijma), is theoretical. 

In other words: We do not accept that hujjiyah of ijma and qiyas in reality does not need evidence. The truth is that in reality and actual fact it needs evidence, even if in our knowledge it does not need due to widespread fame until it became among religious necessities, but in reality it is not self-evident. So it is not correct to absolutely make hujjiyah necessary and outside discipline. And it is possible that this mas'ala is theoretical in terms of 'limma' and sought in the discipline, and self-evident in terms of 'inna' and not included in any discipline. 

The second exposition of the refutation: There is no doubt that rulings established by ijma and qiyas are many, so the establishment of those many rulings indicates knowledge of hujjiyah of ijma and qiyas, in the sense that their establishment does not require proof and reflection, because they are established by ijma, but from the 'limma' aspect, their hujjiyah being self-evident is not conceded, because in reality evidence needs to be adduced for their hujjiyah. Summary: The mas'ala of hujjiyah of ijma and qiyas is self-evident in terms of the establishment of rulings by them and due to their fame, thus in this respect it is not a mas'ala of any discipline. But they are theoretical in reality because reality is the criterion for the establishment of rulings by them, so in this respect it is indeed a mas'ala of some discipline. 

The author said in his gloss on his statement 'And whoever said': i.e., the speaker is Ibn al-Humam. End. 

The investigative answer: The reality is that this attribution to Shaykh Ibn al-Humam and inconsistency in his speech is not correct, because he said in the introduction of his book al-Tahrir, after his statement 'it is from fiqh': That is concerning qiyas on the assumption that it is the action of the mujtahid. But if it is the equality arising from Allah's equation between the original and the branch in the cause, then it is not a mas'ala because it is a religious necessity. Meaning: What we said that hujjiyah of qiyas is a fiqhi mas'ala not usuli is on the assumption that qiyas is the action of the mujtahid. But on the assumption that qiyas is the equality made by Allah between the original and the branch in the cause, it is not a mas'ala because it is a religious necessity.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about the epistemological status of hujjiyah (authoritativeness) of ijma (consensus) and qiyas (analogy). The commentator, the author of Ashraf al-Nu'ut, is expanding on the matn (Muslim al-Thubut) and addressing an apparent contradiction in the statements of Ibn al-Humam. The core issue: is hujjiyah of ijma and qiyas a mas'ala (issue/topic) of some discipline (e.g., fiqh or usul al-fiqh) or is it self-evident (badihi) and thus not belonging to any discipline? 

The passage presents two positions. First, some say it is not a mas'ala at all because it is from religious necessities (daruriyat diniyyah) - anyone who understands the concepts immediately accepts their authority without proof. The matn refutes this by distinguishing two perspectives: from the 'inna' aspect (effect to cause: from the obligation to act we infer hujjiyah) it is self-evident, but from the 'limma' aspect (cause to effect: from hujjiyah we deduce obligation) it is theoretical (nazari). Thus hujjiyah can be both: in one sense it is outside any discipline (because self-evident), in another sense it is a mas'ala of usul al-fiqh (because theoretical). 

The commentator then provides a second refutation and finally a 'tahqiqi' (investigative) answer that clears Ibn al-Humam of contradiction: Ibn al-Humam's two statements are conditional on different definitions of qiyas. If qiyas is the mujtahid's act (istinbat), then its hujjiyah is a fiqhi mas'ala (since it involves ijtihad). If qiyas is the Shari' equality in cause, then its hujjiyah is a religious necessity (badihi) and not a mas'ala. Thus no contradiction. The passage thus clarifies the nuanced classification of usul topics based on perspective and definition.

Key Terms
حجية (hujjiyah): The quality of being a valid proof (hujjah) that obligates action; authoritativeness of a legal source.
بديهي (badihi): Self-evident knowledge that does not require proof; opposite of nazari (theoretical).
نظري (nazari): Knowledge that is acquired through proof and reflection; not self-evident.
دليل لمي (dalil limmi): Proof from the cause to the effect (a priori).
دليل إني (dalil inni): Proof from the effect to the cause (a posteriori).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the investigative answer (tahqiqi), why is there no contradiction in Ibn al-Humam's statements about hujjiyah of qiyas?
A) Because he changed his view over time.
B) Because hujjiyah is always self-evident and never a mas'ala.
C) Because the two statements apply to different meanings of qiyas: one as the mujtahid's act (fiqhi mas'ala) and one as Shari' equality (badihi).
D) Because the matn misinterpreted him.

Key Takeaway
Hujjiyah of qiyas can be both self-evident and theoretical depending on the direction of proof (limmi vs inni) and the definition of qiyas, reconciling apparent contradictions.

6 min
Why Usul Scholars Focus on Ijma and Qiyas
Answering why Usul scholars only treat ijma and qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rationale behind the Hanafi usuli's selective focus on ijma and qiyas over Quran and Sunnah in establishing hujjiyya.

Core Idea
The hujjiyya of Quran and Sunnah is unanimously accepted; usul scholars only need to defend what is disputed — ijma and qiyas.

Have you ever wondered why books of usul al-fiqh dedicate entire chapters to proving the authority of ijma and qiyas, yet hardly give separate treatment to the Quran and Sunnah? The passage from the sharh of Musallam al-Thubot addresses this very question. It reveals a key methodological insight: the usuli's task is not to prove the obvious, but to establish what is contested. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and its significance for the structure of Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Central Question
The passage begins by asking why the author of the matn (Musallam al-Thubot) only mentions ijma and qiyas when discussing hujjiyya. Recognize that this is a question about the scope of usul al-fiqh.
The question arises from the observation that Quran and Sunnah are also sources of law, yet they are not separately proven.
2
Locate the Author's Answer
The commentator answers with the phrase 'But the usuli's discussion...' (ولكن تعرض الاصولی). Focus on the summarizing statement: the hujjiyya of Quran and Sunnah is 'musallam wa muttafaq alayh' (agreed upon) among the entire Ummah.
The key term is 'musallam' — unquestioned/uncontested.
3
Follow the Reasoning: Why Ijma and Qiyas Are Disputed
The passage lists specific groups that reject or restrict ijma (e.g., Nizam al-Mu'tazili, Khawarij, Zahiris) and qiyas (Zahiris). This illustrates the 'severe disagreement' (shadeed ikhtilaf) that necessitates proof.
Note the diversity of opposition: theological (Mu'tazila), sectarian (Rafidis, Khawarij), and methodological (Zahiris).
4
Recognize the Impact on Usul Methodology
The passage concludes that because ijma and qiyas are foundational to usul issues, proving their authority is essential. This explains why usul works give them prominence over the primary texts.
The foundational nature is described with the metaphor of a 'wall' on which usul issues are built.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اسی طرح جیت کتاب و سنت کے مسئلہ کو بھی بطور مبدئیت واصالت ذکر کرنا چاہئے ۔ آخر کار صرف حجیت اجماع وقیاس کے مسئلہ کو ذکر کرنے کی کیا وجہ ہے؟ جواب: ۔ مصنف نے اپنے قول مذکور ولکن تعرض الاصولی سے دیا ہے۔ اس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ قرآن وسنت کی حجیت تمام امت محمدیہ کے نزدیک مسلم و متفق علیہ ہے اس میں کسی کا اختلاف نہیں اس لئے اصولیین اس کو نہیں چھیڑتے ، اس کے برعکس حجیت اجماع و قیاس میں بین الامتہ شدید اختلاف پایا جاتا ہے چنانچہ نظام معتزلی اور بعض روافض و خوارج نے سرے سے اجماع ہی سے انکار کر دیا۔ داؤد ظاہری اور ان کے متبعین نے اور ایک روایت کے مطابق امام احمد نے اجماع کو صحابہ کے ساتھ مختص کردیا ہے، شیعہ میں زیدیہ اور امامیہ نے صرف عزت رسول کے اجماع کو معتبر مانا ہے اسی طرح اہل الظواہر نے حجیت قیاس سے انکار کیا ہے اسی وجہ سے، حجیت اجماع و قیاس کے اثبات کو اصولیین نے ضروری سمجھا چونکہ اجماع وقیاس کی حجیت میں اس قدر شدید اختلاف و نزاع مسائل اصولیہ میں اختلاف و نزاع کا باعث موجب ہوا کیونکہ مسائل اصولیہ کی بنیاد جیت اجماع وقیاس کی دیوار پر قائم ہے اس لئے خاص طور پر ان دونوں کے ذکر کی ضرورت پڑی اور کتاب وسنت میں چونکہ کوئی اختلاف نہیں اس لئے اس کے ذکر کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں۔
Similarly, the issue of the Book and Sunnah should also be mentioned as foundational and original. Finally, what is the reason for only mentioning the issue of hujjiyya of ijma and qiyas? Answer: The author gave it with his statement 'But the usuli's discussion...'. The summary is that the hujjiyya of Quran and Sunnah is agreed upon by the entire Ummah of Muhammad, there is no disagreement in it, so the usuli scholars do not touch it. On the contrary, in the hujjiyya of ijma and qiyas, there is severe disagreement among the Ummah. Thus, Nizam al-Mu'tazili and some Rafidis and Khawarij denied ijma entirely. Dawud al-Zahiri and his followers, and according to one narration Imam Ahmad, restricted ijma to the Companions. Among Shia, the Zaydis and Imamis considered only the ijma of the Family of the Prophet as valid. Similarly, the Zahiris denied the hujjiyya of qiyas. For this reason, the usuli scholars considered the establishment of hujjiyya of ijma and qiyas as necessary, because the severe disagreement and conflict in their hujjiyya caused disagreement and conflict in usul issues, since the foundation of usul issues is built upon the wall of ijma and qiyas. Therefore, there was a need to mention these two specifically, and since there is no disagreement in the Book and Sunnah, their mention is not so necessary.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a justification by the commentator for why the author of Musallam al-Thubut specifically treats the hujjiyya of ijma and qiyas in his work, while not separately treating the hujjiyya of Quran and Sunnah. The reason given is that the authoritative nature of Quran and Sunnah is universally accepted among Muslims, so there is no need to prove it. In contrast, ijma and qiyas are highly disputed; various groups reject or restrict them. Thus, usul scholars focus on establishing their validity because the entire structure of usul al-fiqh depends on these two sources. This passage is a typical Hanafi usul rationale: it acknowledges the centrality of ijma and qiyas as sources of law that require defense, while assuming the unquestioned authority of primary texts.

Key Terms
حجیت (hujjiyya): Authoritativeness or binding force of a source of Islamic law.
اجماع (ijma): Consensus of the mujtahid scholars of the Ummah on a legal ruling after the death of the Prophet.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a shared effective cause (illa).
اصولی (usuli): A scholar specializing in usul al-fiqh, the methodology of deriving rulings.
نظام معتزلی (Nizam al-Mu'tazili): A prominent Mu'tazilite theologian (Ibrahim al-Nazzam) known for rejecting ijma as a source of law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do usul scholars specifically discuss the hujjiyya of ijma and qiyas according to this passage?
A) Because Quran and Sunnah are not considered authoritative.
B) Because ijma and qiyas are universally agreed upon.
C) Because there is severe disagreement about ijma and qiyas, while Quran and Sunnah are agreed upon.
D) Because the author only wanted to discuss secondary issues.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul methodology focuses on proving ijma and qiyas because their authority is contested, whereas Quran and Sunnah are unanimously accepted.

The Subject Matter of Usul al-Fiqh: Proofs or Rulings?
Explaining the disagreement on whether Usul al-Fiqh's subject is proofs, rulings, or both.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three positions on the subject matter (mawdu') of Usul al-Fiqh and evaluate the Hanafi argument that only proofs (adillah) constitute the subject, with rulings (ahkam) discussed only for illustration (taswir wa tanwi').

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh studies proofs; rulings are only discussed to illustrate how proofs work.

In this passage, the commentator on Muslim al-Thubut addresses a foundational question: What exactly does the discipline of Usul al-Fiqh study? Is it the proofs (adillah), the rulings (ahkam), or both? This dispute has significant consequences for how we understand the scope and purpose of usul. By the end of this lesson, you will grasp the Hanafi position and the competing views, and you will be able to follow the detailed argument that only proofs are the true subject matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the three positions
The issue is the mawdu' of Usul al-Fiqh. The passage presents three positions: (1) Jumhur (majority) – only proofs, (2) Imam Ghazali – only rulings, (3) Sadr al-Shariah and al-Amidi – both. Taftazani also supports the 'both' position.
Keep track of who said what for the dispute map.
2
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi argument is that all discussions in usul relate to the indication (dalalah) of proofs. Rulings are mentioned only to clarify how proofs indicate different rulings (taswir wa tanwi').
The concept of 'jihah al-dalalah' (direction of indication) is key.
3
Understand the opposing argument (Taftazani)
Taftazani argues that some discussions in usul (e.g., types of hukm) refer directly to rulings, not just proofs. Therefore, both must be part of the subject.
This is a methodological objection: arbitrarily assigning some discussions to objectives and others to appendages is unjustified.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The commentator responds that even discussions that seem to be about rulings are actually about the direction of indication, which is a property of the proof. Thus, the subject remains the proofs.
The end goal is to maintain the unity of the discipline by reducing all discussions to one kind of object.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وفى موضوعية الاحكام اختلاف
تشريح : ۔ چونکہ اصول فقہ میں ادلہ کے ساتھ احکام سے بھی بحث ہوتی ہے اس لئے ضرورت ہوئی بیان کرنے کی کہ احکام سے بحث کس طور پر ہوتی ہے ایا ادلہ کے ساتھ بحیثیت موضوع علم ہونے کے بحث ہوتی ہے یا علی سبیل الفرعیت استر ادا بحث ہوتی ہے لہذا مصنف نے کہا "وفی موضوعیة الخ اس عبارت سے مصنف کی مراد یہ ہے کہ احکام کے موضوع اصول فقہ ہونے کے بارے میں اختلاف ہے..... جمہور اصولیین کے نزدیک اصول فقہ کا موضوع صرف ادلہ ہیں امام غزالی سے منقول ہے کہ اصول فقہ کا موضوع احکام ہیں ادلہ سے ثبوت کی حیثیت سے..... صاحب توضیح صدر الشریعہ اور صاحب احکام آمدی اس طرف گئے ہیں کہ اصول فقہ کا موضوع ادلہ اور احکام دونوں ہیں ۔ مگر ایک روایت میں ان دونوں کے مذہب کے نقل میں اضطراب پایا جاتا ہے۔ یہاں یہ بات ذہن نشین رہے کہ جنہوں نے احکام کو موضوع قرار دیا ہے ان کے نزدیک ادلہ سے من حیث الاثبات، متعلق بحثیں، احوال احکام کی طرف من حیث الثبوت راجع ہیں اور جنہوں نے صرف ادلہ کو موضوع قرار دیا ہے انکے نزدیک احکام سے " من حیث الثبوت متعلق بحثیں" احوال ادلہ کی طرف من حیث الاثبات راجع ہیں تا کہ جہات و حیثیات کی وحدت کے اعتبار سے جو علم وحدت پر دلالت کرتا ہے اس میں کثرت موضوع نہ ہونے پائے۔
علامہ تفتازانی نے تلویح میں کہا ہے "صحیح یہ ہے کہ اس کا موضوع ادلہ اور احکام دونوں ہیں کیونکہ جب ہم ادلہ کو چار کی طرف اور احکام کو پانچ قسموں کی طرف پھیر دیتے ہیں پھر نظر کرتے ہیں ان مباحث میں جو ادلہ سے احکام کو ثابت کرنے کی کیفیت سے متعلق ہیں تو پاتے ہیں ان میں بض بحث احوال ادلہ کی طرف راجع ہے اور بعض بحث احوال احکام کی طرف راجع ہے لہذا ایک کو مقاصد میں داخل کرنا اور دوسرے کو لواحق میں شامل کرنا تحکم اور ترجیح بلا مرجح ہوگا۔ چونکہ اثبات ادلہ کی کیفیت سے متعلق بحثوں میں سے بعض جب راجع بسوئے دلیل ہوئے اور بعض راجع بسوئے احکام ہوئے تو دونوں کے دونوں مقاصد فن سے ہوئے کہ ان دونوں ہی سے فقہ کی طرف پہونچا جا سکتا ہے اور ان دونوں پر اصول فقہ کی تعریف بھی صادق آتی ہے اس لئے کوئی وجہ نہیں ہے کہ احکام کو خارج مانا جائے اور ان کی بحثوں کو از قبیل مبادیات قرار دیا جائے ورنہ لازم آئے گا کہ اصول فقہ کی تعریف دخول غیر سے مانع نہ رہی۔ اور امام غزالی جنہوں نے اصول فقہ کے موضوع کو صرف احکام میں منحصر کر دیا ہے تو اس کی وجہ یہ بیان کی جاتی ہے کہ ادلہ کا موضوع اصول فقہ ہونا مشہور و معروف ہے پس موضوعیت ادلہ کی شہرت کی وجہ سے کوئی یہ نہ سمجھ لے کہ احکام موضوع نہیں ہے جیسا کہ مصنف سمجھ بیٹھے ہیں چنانچہ امام غزالی کا یہ نظریہ نہیں ہے کہ ادلہ کا موضوع ہو نا صحیح نہیں ہے۔
قوله والحق لاوانما الغرض التصوير والتنويع الخ اس عبارت سے مصنف نے ان تمام لوگوں پر رد فرمایا ہے جو احکام کو موضوع قرار دیتے ہیں مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ حق یہ ہے کہ احکام موضوع نہیں ہیں رہے اس فن میں احکام کا ذکر کیا جانا تو اس ذکر سے مقصود احکام کی تصویر و تویع یعنی حکم کا معنی اور اس سے مختص احوال کا بیان کرنا ہے تا کہ تمیز نام حاصل ہو اور احکام کے انواع سے ادلہ کے انواع ثابت کئے جاسکیں تا کہ اس کی مزید تو ابح وتشریح ہو سکے ۔ مثلا اصولی حکم کے انواع وجوب و حرمت اور جواز اور کراہت وندب کو اس لئے بیان کرتے ہیں تا کہ معلوم ہو جائے کہ وجوب مثلا دلیل قطعی سے ثابت ہوتا ہے اور کراہت مثلا دلیل ظنی سے یا اس دلیل سے مثلا حکم کی قسم عزیمت ثابت ہوتی ہے اور اس دلیل سے رخصت کا حکم مستفاد ہوتا ہے وغیرہ۔ حاصل یہ کہ حضرات اصولیین مدلول پر دلیل کی دلالت کی جہت سے ہی بحث کرتے ہیں اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ دلالت دلیل کی حالت کا نام ہے پس وہ احوال جو اصول فقہ میں بہت دلالت ذکر کئے جاتے ہیں وہ دلائل ہی کی طرف راجع ہیں اس لئے دلائل ہی مقصود اصلی ہوئے جن کے احوال سے اس فن میں بحث ہوتی ہے۔
قوله وما من علم الايذكر فيها الاشياء الخ
یہ عبارت ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے۔
اعتراض کی تقریر یہ ہے کہ صدر الشریعہ نے کہا نظر شخص حاکم ہے کہ وہ احوال جن سے اس فن میں بحث ہوتی ہے ان میں سے بعض ادلہ کی طرف راجع ہے جبکہ بعض احکام کی طرف بھی راجع ہوتے ہیں پس بعض کو مقاصد میں سے قرار دینا اور بعض کو لواحق و مبادی میں سے ماننا تحکم ہے!
His saying: 'And regarding the subject-ness of rulings, there is disagreement.' Explanation: Since in Usul al-Fiqh, rulings are also discussed along with proofs, it became necessary to explain how rulings are discussed—whether they are discussed alongside proofs as part of the subject matter of the science, or they are discussed as subsidiary. Therefore the author said: 'And regarding the subject-ness...' By this phrase, the author means that there is disagreement about rulings being the subject of Usul al-Fiqh. According to the majority of Usul scholars, the subject of Usul al-Fiqh is only the proofs. It is transmitted from Imam Ghazali that the subject of Usul al-Fiqh is the rulings, with the proofs being in the capacity of evidence. The author of al-Tawdih, Sadr al-Shariah, and the author of al-Ahkam, al-Amidi, inclined to the view that the subject of Usul al-Fiqh is both proofs and rulings. However, in one narration, there is inconsistency in transmitting their doctrine. Here it should be kept in mind that those who consider rulings as the subject—according to them, the discussions related to proofs from the aspect of proof are referred back to the states of rulings from the aspect of establishment; and those who consider only proofs as the subject—according to them, the discussions related to rulings from the aspect of establishment are referred back to the states of rulings from the aspect of proof. This is so that with the unity of perspectives and aspects, which indicate the unity of the science, there may not be multiplicity of subjects. Allamah Taftazani said in al-Talwih: 'The correct view is that its subject is both proofs and rulings, because when we turn proofs to four types and rulings to five types, then look at the discussions related to the manner of establishing rulings from proofs, we find that some discussions refer to the states of proofs and some discussions refer to the states of rulings. Therefore, to include one among the objectives and the other among the appendages would be arbitrary and preference without preponderance. Since some discussions concerning the manner of establishing proofs refer to proofs and some refer to rulings, both are among the objectives of the discipline, because from both one can reach fiqh, and the definition of Usul al-Fiqh applies to both. Hence there is no reason to consider rulings as external and to deem their discussions as belonging to the preliminaries. Otherwise it would be necessary that the definition of Usul al-Fiqh would not prevent the inclusion of something external.' And regarding Imam Ghazali confining the subject of Usul al-Fiqh to only rulings, the reason given is that the proofs being the subject of Usul al-Fiqh is well-known; so due to the fame of the proofs being the subject, lest someone think that rulings are not the subject, as the author thought. Thus it is not Imam Ghazali's view that the proofs being the subject is incorrect. His saying: 'And the truth is that the purpose is only depiction and classification...' By this phrase, the author refutes all those who consider rulings as the subject. The author says: The truth is that rulings are not the subject. As for the mention of rulings in this discipline, the purpose of this mention is only the depiction and classification of rulings, i.e., to explain the meaning of hukm and its specific states, so that distinction is achieved and from the types of rulings the types of proofs can be established, so that further elaboration and explanation can occur. For example, they explain the types of usuli ruling—obligation, prohibition, permissibility, dislike, recommendation—so that it is known that obligation, for example, is established by a definitive proof, and dislike, for example, by a speculative proof, or that from this proof the type of ruling of azimah is established, and from that proof the ruling of rukhsah is derived, etc. The conclusion is that the Usul scholars only discuss the direction of the proof's indication of the indicated, and it is clear that indication is a state of the proof. Therefore, the states that are mentioned in Usul al-Fiqh in relation to indication all refer back to proofs. Hence proofs are the primary objective, whose states are discussed in this discipline. His saying: 'And there is no science in which things are not mentioned...' This phrase is an answer to an objection. The formulation of the objection is that Sadr al-Shariah said: The discerning person observes that among the states discussed in this discipline, some refer to proofs and some refer to rulings. So to consider some as among the objectives and others as among the appendages and preliminaries is arbitrary!
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about the subject matter (mawdu') of Usul al-Fiqh. The author, commenting on the matn of Muslim al-Thubut, explains that there is ikhtilaf among scholars. The majority (Jumhur) hold that the subject is only the proofs (adillah). Imam Ghazali is reported to have said that the subject is only the rulings (ahkam). Sadr al-Shariah (author of al-Tawdih) and al-Amidi (author of al-Ahkam) hold that both proofs and rulings constitute the subject, though there is some inconsistency in the transmission of their view. The commentator then explains how each position resolves the issue of unity of the science: those who say rulings is the subject refer proof-discussions to rulings; those who say proofs is the subject refer ruling-discussions to proofs. Taftazani in al-Talwih argues for the 'both' position, claiming that since some discussions refer to proofs and some to rulings, arbitrarily assigning one to objectives and the other to appendages is unjustified. The author, however, supports the view that only proofs are the subject. He argues that rulings are mentioned in Usul al-Fiqh only for 'taswir wa tanwi'' (depiction and classification) — i.e., to define types of rulings and their attributes, so that one can understand how proofs indicate different rulings. For example, obligation (wujub) is established by decisive proof, dislike (karahah) by speculative proof, etc. Ultimately, all discussions about rulings are actually about the indication (dalalah) of proofs, and indication is a property of the proof. Therefore, the true subject is the proofs themselves; rulings are merely illustrative. Finally, he answers Sadr al-Shariah's objection by implying that the apparent reference to rulings in some discussions does not make rulings part of the subject; rather, those discussions are ultimately about the proofs' indications.

Key Terms
موضوع (mawdu'): The subject matter of a discipline; what the discipline primarily studies.
ادلہ (adillah): The proofs or sources of Islamic law (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas).
احکام (ahkam): The legal rulings (e.g., wajib, haram, mandub, makruh, mubah).
تصویر (taswir): Depiction; clarifying the meaning and attributes of rulings.
تنویع (tanwi'): Classification; dividing rulings into types to understand how proofs indicate them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of this commentary, what is the true subject matter (mawdu') of Usul al-Fiqh?
A) Only the proofs (adillah)
B) Only the rulings (ahkam)
C) Both proofs and rulings
D) Neither proofs nor rulings

Key Takeaway
Usul al-Fiqh's proper subject is the proofs (adillah); rulings are discussed only to illustrate how proofs indicate them.

The Benefit and Subject Matter of Usul al-Fiqh
Answering an objection and stating the benefit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the benefit of Usul al-Fiqh and distinguish its subject matter from rulings according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The benefit of Usul is knowing how to derive rulings, not the rulings themselves.

After defining Usul al-Fiqh and its subject matter, the author now clarifies its purpose. He explains that the benefit (fā’idah) is not merely knowing the rulings, but mastering the method of extraction. He also addresses a subtle objection: because rulings are discussed in Usul, some might think they are the subject. The Hanafi position, endorsed by the majority, is clear.

Guided Path
1
Identify the benefit
Find the sentence where the author states the benefit (fā’idah) of Usul al-Fiqh. It is knowledge of the method of extraction and derivation of shar'i rulings.
2
Understand the objection about subject matter
Some scholars argue that because rulings (ahkam) are discussed in Usul, they must be its subject matter (mawdu'). Recognize this as the opposing position.
3
Trace the Hanafi response
The passage rejects that view: the inclusion of rulings is incidental (istitradan) for refining the principles. The true subject is the evidences and methods of derivation. This is the madhhab of the majority (jumhur) and the author's chosen view.
4
Recognize the qiyas structure
The author explains that benefit is realized by properly structuring qiyas: the minor premise (sughra) from a detailed proof (dalil tafsili) and the major premise (kubra) from general principles (dalil ijmail).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواب :۔ یہ ہے کہ ہر فن میں مقاصد کے علاوہ بہت سی ایسی چیزیں تبعا بطور تمہ اور فن کی غایات مقصودہ کی اصلاح و درستگی کے لئے ذکر کی جاتی ہیں لہذا بعض احوال کا احکام کی طرف راجع ہونا مستلزم نہیں اس بات کو کہ احکام اصول فقہ کا موضوع ہیں یہی مذہب جمہور کا ہے اور مصنف کا مذہب مختار اور امام ابن الحمام کا بھی یہی پسندیدہ ہے اور احکام میں آمدی نے بھی اس پر جزم کیا ہے مگر ان سے احکام کی بھی روایت منقول ہے۔
قوله وفائدته معرفة الاحكام الشرعية وهى الخ جب مصنف فن کی تعریف اور اس کے موضوع کے بیان سے فارغ ہو گئے تو اس عبارت سے اس کی غرض و غایت کی طرف اشارہ کیا اس لئے کہ بلا غرض کسی فن کا طلب کرنا عبث ہے اور نفس ناطقہ عبث سے منزہ ہے۔ پھر شارع فی العلم کی نگاہ میں فن کی غرض و غایت اور اسکا فائدہ جب ملحوظ رہتا ہے تو اس کو اس فن سے کمال رغبت اور دلچسپی پیدا ہوتی ہے اور شارع فی العلم اس فن کی حصولیابی میں ہمہ تن مصروف ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے مصنف نے اس کے فائدہ کو ذکر کیا۔ تو کہا ہے کہ اصول فقہ کا فائدہ احکام شرعیہ کے استخراج و استنباط کے کیفیت کی معرفت ہے بایں طور کہ احکام شرع کے حکم جاننے کے لیے قیاس کو اس طرز پر ترتیب دیں کہ قیاس کا صغری دلیل تفصیلی ( آیت قرآنیہ) سے ماخوذ ہو اور اس کا کبری دلیل اجمالی یعنی قواعد اصولیہ سے حوز ہو سکی تفصیل گذر چکی ہے اور چونکہ اصول الفقہ اشرف العلوم ہے کہ وہ علوم شرعیہ کی معرفت کا اعلیٰ ترین ذریعہ ہے اس لئے اس کی معرفت دائمی نیک بختی اور سرمدی سعادتمندی کا سبب بھی ہے چنانچہ قرآن حکیم اور احادیث نبویہ کے اوراق علم علماء کی فضیلتوں سے مالا مال ہیں ۔ رہے ہیں
Answer: It is that in every field, besides the main objectives, many things are mentioned incidentally as a prelude and for the correction and refinement of the intended ends of the field. Therefore, some conditions referring back to rulings does not necessitate that rulings are the subject matter of Usul al-Fiqh. This is the madhhab of the majority. The author's chosen madhhab and Imam Ibn al-Humam's preferred view are also the same. Al-Amidi also affirmed this, but a narration from him that rulings are the subject is also transmitted. 
His statement: 'And its benefit is knowledge of the shar'i rulings, etc.' When the author finished defining the field and its subject matter, he indicated its purpose and goal by this expression because seeking any field without purpose is futile and the rational soul is free from futility. Then when the one studying the field keeps in mind its purpose and goal and its benefit, he develops great enthusiasm and interest in it, and he becomes fully engaged in attaining that field. Therefore, the author mentioned its benefit. He said that the benefit of Usul al-Fiqh is knowledge of the method of extraction and derivation of shar'i rulings, such that to know the ruling of a shar'i matter, Qiyas is arranged in this manner: its minor premise is taken from a detailed proof (a Quranic verse) and its major premise is taken from a general proof, i.e., the principles of Usul. The detail has already passed. And because Usul al-Fiqh is the noblest of sciences as it is the highest means of knowing the legal sciences, its knowledge is also the cause of eternal good fortune and perpetual bliss. Indeed, the pages of the Noble Quran and the Prophetic hadiths are filled with the virtues of scholars. End.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a teacher's explanation of the benefit and subject matter of Usul al-Fiqh. The author begins by answering an objection: some might think that because rulings (ahkam) are often discussed in Usul, they must be its subject matter. The author counters that such incidental mention does not make rulings the subject, and this is the view of the majority (jumhur), the author's own chosen position, and also preferred by Imam Ibn al-Humam. Al-Amidi also affirmed this, though a different opinion is attributed to him. 

Then the author explains the statement of the matn: 'And its benefit is knowledge of the shar'i rulings.' After defining the field and its subject, the author now mentions its purpose, because studying a field without purpose is futile. The benefit (fā'idah) of Usul al-Fiqh is knowing how to extract and derive shar'i rulings correctly. This is done by properly structuring qiyas (analogy): the minor premise (sughra) comes from a detailed proof (dalil tafsili, e.g., a Quranic verse) and the major premise (kubra) comes from the general principles of Usul (dalil ijmail). The author concludes by extolling the virtue of Usul al-Fiqh as the noblest science and the key to eternal success.

Key Terms
فائدة (fā’idah): The intended result or benefit of a science; here it is knowledge of the method of deriving shar'i rulings through Qiyas using detailed and general proofs.
استخراج و استنباط (istikhraj wa istinbat): Extraction and derivation of rulings from their evidences by applying usul principles.
دلیل تفصیلی (dalil tafsili): A specific textual proof, such as a Quranic verse or hadith, from which the minor premise of qiyas is taken.
دلیل اجمالی (dalil ijmail): The general principles of Usul al-Fiqh itself, which form the major premise of qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the benefit (fā’idah) of Usul al-Fiqh?
A) Memorizing the rulings of fiqh.
B) Knowledge of the method of extraction and derivation of shar'i rulings.
C) Learning the definitions of fiqh terms.
D) Knowing the names of the four imams.

Key Takeaway
The benefit of Usul al-Fiqh is not the rulings themselves, but the systematic method of deriving them from detailed and general evidences.

12 min
The Many Definitions of Nazar (Speculative Reasoning)
Scholarly definitions of nazar in usul al-fiqh

Core Idea
Nazar is an intentional, structured mental movement from known premises to unknown conclusions.

The term 'nazar' (speculative reasoning) is foundational in Hanafi usul al-fiqh as the engine of ijtihad. However, its precise definition has been refined by scholars over time. In this passage, the author presents definitions from Qadi Abu Bakr, Ibn Hajib, Qadi Adud, Ibn al-Humam, and finally adopts the view of Taftazani. Understanding these nuances is crucial to grasping how Hanafi jurists derive rulings through qiyas and istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core definition
Find the common thread across all definitions: nazar is a mental activity aimed at acquiring knowledge or conjecture.
All definitions agree on intentionality and purpose.
2
List the key components
Extract the recurring elements: movement/transition, prior knowns, purposeful seeking, ordering/composition.
These elements constitute the 'anatomy' of nazar.
3
Note the variations
Observe how each definition adds or emphasizes a different aspect: some equate nazar with fikr, others distinguish it; some specify the object (intelligibles vs. known matters).
The variation reflects different epistemological emphases.
4
Determine the preferred Hanafi definition
Identify the author's chosen definition: 'observation of intelligibles for attainment of the unknown' (after Taftazani). Understand why he modifies 'order' to 'observation'.
This definition highlights that nazar deals with universals (ma'qulat) and requires a second movement (from premises to demand).
5
Understand the justification
Explain the three reasons given for using 'intelligibles' instead of 'known': avoiding ambiguity, indicating universality, and maintaining rhyme.
These reasons reflect the precision expected in usul definitions.

(۱) قاضی ابوبکر نے کہا۔
النظر هو الفكر الذى يطلب به من قام به علماً او ظناً كذاذكر الآمدي في الاحكام یعنی نظر اس فکر کو کہتے ہیں جس کے ذریعہ صاحب فکر علم یاظن کو حاصل کرے، ا! ' ہی آمدی نے احکام میں کہا ہے ۔
(۲) ابکار الاحکام میں بایں الفاظ نظر کی تعریف کی گئی ہے۔
النظر عبارة عن التصرف بالعقل فى الامور السابقة بالعلم او الظن المناسبة للمطلوب بتألف خاص قصد التحصيل ماليس حاصلافي العقل یعنی ۔ مطلوب کے مناسب امور معلومہ سابقہ یا امور مظنونہ سابقہ میں ایک خاص ترکیبی کیفیت کے ساتھ عقل میں غیر حاصل نشی کے حصول کے لئے بذریعہ مقتل تصرف کرنے کا نام نظر ہے۔
(۳) علامہ ابن حاجب نے مختصر میں فرمایا۔
النظر الفكر الذى يطلب به علم اوظن انتهى یعنی نظر ایسی فکر کو کہتے ہیں جس کے ذریعہ علم باطن کو طلب کیا جاتا ہے۔
(۴) شرح مختصر قاضی عضد میں ہے۔
النظر هو انتقال النفس فى المعانى بالقصد وذالك قديكون بطلب علم او ظن فيسمى نظرا وقدلايكون كذالك كاكثر حديث النفس فلايسمى نظراً وبهذا صرح الامام اى امام الحرمين في الشامل وقول الامدى مراده أن النظر هو الفكر ثم تفسيره بانه الذى يطلب به ظن او علم بعید انتهی ۔
یعنی نظر نفس کا بالقصد معانی میں منتقل ہونے کا نام ہے اور انتقال نفس کبھی طلب علم کے لئے یا طلب ظن کے لئے ہوتا ہے تو اسکو نظر کہتے ہیں اور کبھی طلب علم یا ظن کے لئے نہیں ہوتا جیسے نفسانی باتیں تو اس کو نظر نہیں کہیں گے ۔ چنانچہ امام الحرمین نے شامل میں یہی تصریح کی ہے۔ اور آمدی کا یہ کہنا کہ نظر فکر کو کہتے ہیں اور پھر الذي يطلب به ظن او علم سے اس کی تفسیر بعید ہے۔
(۵) امام ابن الہمام نے تحریر میں نظر کی اس طرح تعریف کی ہے۔
النظر حركة النفس من المطالب فى الكيف طالبة للمبادى باستعراض الصور اى تكيفها بصورة بصورة لتجد المناسب وهو الوسط فترتبه مع طرفي المطلوب على وجه مستلزم یعنی مطالب تصور یہ و تصد یقیہ سے کیف میں نفس ناطقہ کا حرکت کرنا ، مبادی کو طلب کر کے بایں طور که نفس مباری کی صورتوں سے یکے بادیگر متکیف ہوتا کہ نفس امر مناسب حاصل کرے اور امر مناسب وہ واسطہ ہے پھر واسطہ کی ترتیب مطلوب کے دونوں طرف کے ساتھ اس طرح ہو کہ مطلوب کو مستلزم ہو۔ نظر کہلاتا ہے۔
(1) مصنف نے سعد الدین تفتازانی کی پیروی کرتے ہوئے نظر کی یہ تعریف کی ہے النظر ترتيب المعقول لتحصيل المجهول، صرف اتنا فرق ہے کہ ترتیب المعقول کے بجائے ملاحظہ المعقول کہا ہے تا ہم دونوں کا مفاد ایک ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ نفس ناطقہ کا ام معلوم کی طرف متوجہ ہونا غیر معلوم کے حصول کے لئے ۔ معقول کے وجوہ :۔ امر معلوم کے بجائے معقول کہنے کی کئی حکمتیں ہیں ۔ ایک وجہ یہ ہے کہ معلوم لفظ مشترک ہے اور مقام تعریف میں لفظ مشترک کے استعمال سے احتر از چاہیئے ۔ (۲) معقول کہکر اشارہ اور تنبیہ کرنا ہے اسبات پر کہ نظر وفکر معقولات یعنی امور کلیہ میں جاری ہوتی ہے جس کا ظرف عروض ذہن ہے امور جزئیہ میں نہیں کیونکہ جزئی کا سب و مکتب نہیں ہوتی ۔ (۳) رعایت مجمع کی وجہ سے معقول لایا تا کہ بعد کو آنے والا لفظ ” مجہول کے آخری حرف کی رعایت ملحوظ رہے۔
یادر ہے کہ نظر کی یہ تعریف متاخرین کے مذہب مختار پر ہے جس کے لئے حرکت ثانیہ لازم ہے، یعنی مبادی سے مطالب کی حرکت ۔ چنانچہ سید محق شریف نے شرح مواقف میں کہا ہے کہ جب ہمارے ذہن میں امر تصوری یا تصدیقی کا کچھ شعور پیدا ہو پھر اس کو ہم کامل طور پر حاصل کرنا چاہیں تو اس کے لئے پہلے ضروری ہے کہ خزانہ ذہن میں محفوظ معلومات میں سے ایک معلوم دوسرے معلوم کی طرف حرکت کرے تا کہ اس مطلوب کے مناسب معلومات کو پاسکے اور یہی مبادی ہے پھر با دیگر ذہن
There are also various opinions of scholars regarding the terminological definition of nazar. (1) Qadi Abu Bakr said: 'Nazar is the thought by which the one who undertakes it seeks knowledge or conjecture.' As Aamidi mentioned in al-Ahkam. That is, nazar is called that thought by which the possessor of thought attains knowledge or conjecture. Aamidi said this in al-Ahkam. (2) In Abkar al-Ahkam, nazar is defined in these words: 'Nazar is the management by the intellect of prior matters that are known or conjectured and appropriate to the desired object, with a specific composition, intending to attain what is not already present in the intellect.' That is, the management of the intellect among prior known or conjectured matters appropriate to the desired object, with a specific compositional quality, for the attainment of what is not already possessed in the intellect, is called nazar. (3) Allama Ibn Hajib said in al-Mukhtasar: 'Nazar is the thought by which knowledge or conjecture is sought.' That is, nazar is such thought by which knowledge or conjecture is sought. (4) In the commentary on Mukhtasar Qadi Adud: 'Nazar is the intentional transition of the soul among meanings. That may be for seeking knowledge or conjecture, and it is called nazar; or it may not be like that, like most inner thoughts, so it is not called nazar.' Imam al-Haramayn stated this in al-Shamil. And the statement of Aamidi that nazar is thought and then interpreting it as that by which conjecture or knowledge is sought, is far-fetched. (5) Imam Ibn al-Humam defined nazar in al-Tahrir as: 'Nazar is the movement of the soul from the demands concerning quality, seeking the premises by surveying the forms, i.e., taking on forms one by one to find the appropriate middle term, then ordering it with the two extremes of the desired object in a way that necessitates the conclusion.' That is, the movement of the rational soul from conceptual or affirmational demands concerning quality, seeking the premises, in such a way that the soul takes on forms one after another until it obtains the appropriate matter—and the appropriate matter is the middle term—then ordering the middle term with the two extremes of the desired object in a way that necessitates the desired object, is called nazar. (A) The author, following Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani, defined nazar as: 'Nazar is the observation of the intelligibles for the attainment of the unknown.' The only difference is that instead of 'arrangement of the intelligibles' he said 'observation of the intelligibles.' Nevertheless, the meaning is the same: the rational soul's turning towards known matters for the attainment of the unknown. Reasons for using 'intelligibles' instead of 'known': (1) The word 'known' is ambiguous (common), and in a definition one should avoid using an ambiguous word. (2) By saying 'intelligibles', it is indicated and pointed out that nazar and thought operate on intelligibles, i.e., universal matters, whose locus of occurrence is the mind, not on particular matters, because particulars have no occasion for order. (3) For the sake of rhyme, the word 'intelligibles' was brought so that the final letter of the following word 'unknown' is taken into account. Remember that this definition of nazar is according to the chosen view of the later scholars, which requires a second movement, i.e., movement from premises to the demands. As Sayyid Sharif al-Jurjani said in Sharh al-Mawaqif: When there is some awareness of a conceptual or affirmational matter in our mind, and we want to fully obtain it, it is first necessary that the mind move from one known to another known among the stored information in the treasury of the mind, so that it can find the information appropriate to that desired object—and these are the premises—then, by way of another...
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of multiple definitions of the term 'nazar' (speculative reasoning) from various classical scholars of usul al-fiqh. The author presents each definition in Arabic followed by an Urdu explanation. The purpose is to show the evolution and refinement of the concept. The first definition from Qadi Abu Bakr (as quoted by Aamidi) equates nazar with 'fikr' (thought) that seeks knowledge or conjecture. The second definition from Abkar al-Ahkam adds the element of the intellect's management of prior known or conjectured matters to attain what is not yet known. The third definition from Ibn Hajib is concise, simply stating nazar is thought seeking knowledge or conjecture. The fourth definition from the commentary of Qadi Adud specifies that nazar is the intentional transition of the soul among meanings, and distinguishes it from idle thoughts. The fifth definition from Ibn al-Humam is more detailed: it describes nazar as the soul's movement from demands to premises, surveying forms to find the middle term, then ordering it with the two extremes. Finally, the author gives his own definition following Taftazani: 'Nazar is the observation of intelligibles for the attainment of the unknown.' He explains why the term 'intelligibles' (ma'qulat) is used instead of 'known' (ma'lum): first, 'known' is ambiguous; second, it indicates nazar deals with universals; third, for rhyme. The passage concludes by noting that this definition requires a 'second movement' (haraka thaniya) from premises to the demand, as explained by Sayyid Sharif al-Jurjani. The overall discussion is about the precise nature of nazar, which is foundational for understanding ijtihad and istidlal in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
النظر (al-nazar): The intentional movement of the soul from known premises to the unknown, aiming at knowledge or conjecture, particularly through the arrangement/observation of intelligibles.
الفكر (al-fikr): Thought, which seeks knowledge or conjecture; often used synonymously with nazar but sometimes distinguished as more general.
المعقول (al-ma'qul): Intelligible matters, i.e., universal concepts that exist in the mind, as opposed to particular sensory objects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's preferred definition following Taftazani, what is the object of nazar?
A) Ordering known matters to obtain unknown
B) Observation of intelligibles to obtain unknown
C) Movement of soul from demands to premises
D) Thought seeking knowledge or conjecture

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi preferred definition of nazar is the intentional observation of intelligibles to attain the unknown, requiring a structured movement from premises to conclusion.

Method of Learning
intermediate
8 min
Definition of Nazar and Impossibility of Defining Simple Concepts
Commentary on definition of nazar and critique of Sharh al-Mawaqif

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that nazar requires two movements (tartib) and explain why simple concepts (baseet) cannot be defined or acquired.

Core Idea
Nazar requires two ordered movements; a simple concept cannot be defined — its requisites are self-evident.

This passage from Ashraf al-Nu'ut's commentary on Musallam al-Thubut presents a critical analysis of the definition of nazar (speculative thought) and the nature of simple concepts. The author rejects the view that nazar can be based on a single movement of observation, arguing that true nazar requires a sequence of two mental movements. He then proves that simple concepts (baseet) cannot serve as causes (sabab) in definition or be acquired through reasoning, because any attempt to define them leads to circularity or dependence on accidents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing definitions of nazar
One definition requires two movements (tartib); the other suffices with one movement plus observation (mulahazah). The author argues the latter is invalid.
The verbal disagreement between these views yields no practical consequence but is important for methodology.
2
Understand the author's first objection: observation is not acquisition
The author states that observation (mulahazah) is not called kasb by consensus. If it were, verbal definitions would become real definitions and mentioning nazar would produce new knowledge each time, which is absurd.
This objection targets the view of the commentator of al-Mawaqif.
3
Understand the second objection: requisites are not acquired
Even if observation yields knowledge of the essence, that knowledge is an evident requisite (lazim bayyin) of the simple meaning. Requisites necessarily follow; they are not acquired through effort.
Thus, simple meanings cannot be 'acquired' (muktasab).
4
Analyze the proof that simple concepts cannot be defined
A simple concept cannot be defined through itself (circular) or through a compound. Defining via a compound fails whether it uses essential attributes, accidental attributes, or both: essentials would turn it into a compound, accidents do not convey essence, and the mix reduces to accidents.
Therefore, baseet can be neither a cause (sabab) for knowledge nor a definition.
5
State the conclusion: nazar requires two movements; simple concepts are neither causes nor acquirable
The correct definition of nazar involves tartib (sequence) of two movements. A simple concept cannot be a cause or acquired, reinforcing that nazar must involve deliberate sequential reasoning.
This conclusion aligns with Hanafi usul methodology.

خلاصہ یہ کہ بسیط کے سب ہونے نہ ہونے میں اختلاف لفظی ہے پس جس نے نظر کی تعریف میں دوحرکتیں لازم قرار دی ہیں ان کے نزدیک بلاشبہ ترتیب حرکت ثانیہ کے لوازم میں سے ہوگی لہذاوہ جس میں صرف حرکت واحدہ پائی جائینگی کا سب نہ ہوگا، اس کے برعکس جنہوں نے نظر میں حرکت واحدہ پر اکتفا کیا تو ان کے نزدیک بلاشبہ مجہول کے حاصل ہونے کے لئے حرکت ثانیہ کا پایا جانا ضروری نہیں ہے جس کے لئے ترتیب لازم ہے بلکہ ذہن میں مطلوب کے مناسب امر موجود کا لحاظ کرنا حصول مطلوب کے لئے کافی ہے مگر یہ بات پوشیدہ نہیں کہ لفظی اختلاف شان عقلاء سے بعید ہے۔ کیونکہ اس پر کوئی ثمرہ مرتب نہیں ہوتا غالباً اس تفصیل کی طرف اشارہ کرتے ہوئے مصنف نے حاشیہ میں کہا ہے۔

" وقول شارح المواقف ان من جوز التعريف بالمعاني البسيطة فله أن يقول أن المعانى البسيطة قد لا تكون ملحوظة قصداً فاذا استحضرت ولوحظت قصداً افادت العلم بالمهية وان كان ذالك نادراً

شارح مواقف کے قول پر مصنف نے متعدد وجوہ سے اعتراض کرتے ہوئے کہا۔
مكابرة مر دودة فان ملاحظة الماهية لا تُسَمَّى كسباً بالاتفاق والالكان التعريف اللفظي تعريفا حقيقياً وكان تذكر النظر مفيداً لعلم جديد الى غير ذالک من المفاسد اللازمة وأن الماهية المعلومة من اللوازم البينة للمعنى البسيط وان كان اللزوم بعد استحضاره فتد برانتهت

عبارت حاشیہ فان ملاحظة الماهیة الخ سے قول شارح مواقف پر پہلا اعتراض وارد ہے۔ اعتراض کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ملاحظہ کو بالاتفاق "کسب نہیں کہا جاتا کیونکہ اگر ملاحظہ کسب کے ہم معنی ہو تو تعریف لفظی کا تعریف حقیقی ہونا لازم آئے گا اس لئے کہ تعریف لفظی میں حقیقی کی طرح ملاحظہ کا وجود ہوتا ہے۔ پھر اگر نظر میں ملاحظہ معتبر ہو تو لازم آئے گا کہ جب جب نظر کو ذکر کیا جائے تو ہر مرتبہ حد جدید یا علم جدید حاصل ہو کیونکہ ہر مرتبہ تذکر نظر میں قصداً ملاحظہ "پایا جاتا ہے۔ عبارت حاشیہ وأن المهية المعلومة سے قول شارح مواقف پر ایک دوسرا اعتراض ہے۔

اعتراض کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اگر چہ معنی بسیط کا استحضار و ملاحظہ ممکن ہے اور ان سے ماہیت معلومہ حاصل ہے تا ہم اس استحضار و ملاحظہ معنی بسیط کو کسب نہیں کہتے اس لئے کہ ماہیت معلومہ معنی بسیط کے لوازم بدینہ میں سے ہے اور یہ ظاہر و بد یہی کہ شی کے لوازم مکتب نہیں ہوتے گو کہ معنی بسیط کے استحضار کے بعد ہی حاصل ہوا ہو ۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ معنی بسیط کا تصور اس کے لوازم بینہ کے تصور کو ستلزم ہے اور لوازم کسب سے حاصل نہیں ہوتے ۔

اس لئے ملاحظہ سے نظر کی تعریف مردود ہے صحیح یہ ہے کہ نظر کی تعریف ترتیب سے لیا جائے جو دو حرکتوں کو مستلزم ہے اس صورت میں بسیط حد اور سما کا سب نہیں ہوسکتا۔

وقوله ولامكتسباً لان العارض لايفيد الكنه

یعنی بسیط جس طرح کا سب نہیں ہوسکتا مکتب بھی نہیں ہو سکتا معنی یہ ہے کہ امر بسیط کی معرفت بھی حاصل نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ اگر بسیط کی معرفت حاصل ہو تو اس کی معرفت بسیط ہی کے ذریعہ ہوگی یا کسی مرکب کے ذریعہ سے ہوگی شق اول یعنی بسیط کی معرفت کا بسیط سے ہونا باطل ہے جیسا گذرا کہ بسیط کا سب نہیں ہو سکتا۔ اور شق دوم یعنی بسیط کی معرفت مرکب سے ہونا بھی باطل ہے وہ اسطرح کہ اس کا سب مرکب کی ترکیب ذاتیات سے ہوگی یا عرضیات سے یا پھر ذاتی وعرضی دونوں سے ہرسہ صورت باطل ہے وجہ اول (ذاتیات سے مرکب ہو ) کا بطلان بدیہی ہے اس لئے کہ کلام ' بسیط میں ہے پس اگر کا سب مرکب ہو جائے گا تو مکتب بسیط بسیط نہ رہ جائے گا بلکہ مرکب ہو جائے گا اور وجہ دوم ( عرضیات سے مرکب ہونا) بھی باطل ہے اس لئے کہ اس صورت میں علم بالکنہ کا فائدہ نہ دیے گا کہ عرضیات سے علم بالحقیقہ حاصل نہیں ہوتا ۔ رہے وجہ سوم (ذاتی وعرضی سے مرکب ہو ) تو اس کا بطلان بھی ظاہر ہے اس لئے کہ ذاتی و عرضی کا مجموعہ عرضی ہوتا ہے جس طرح داخل و خارج کا مجموعہ خارج ہوتا ہے کہ نتیجہ ادون کے تابع ہوتا ہے پس وجہ سوم مال کے اعتبار سے وجہ دوم کی طرف راجع ہے چنانچہ جس طرح وجہ دوم یعنی عرضیات سے علم بالکنہ حاصل نہیں ہوسکتا بعینہ اس طرح وجہ سوم یعنی ذاتی
He did not pay attention to the definition and restricted definition to compound meanings, for this is what is considered in the acquisition of sciences.

Summary: Whether a simple concept can be a cause (sabab) or not is a verbal disagreement. For those who consider two movements necessary in the definition of nazar, undoubtedly tartib (sequence) will be among the requisites of the second movement; hence that which contains only a single movement will not be a cause. On the contrary, those who suffice with a single movement in nazar, according to them, the existence of a second movement for which tartib is necessary is not required for obtaining the unknown; rather, considering in the mind something present that is appropriate to the sought-after is sufficient. But it is not hidden that verbal disagreement is far from the dignity of rational people, because no practical consequence (thamar) is attached to it. Probably the author indicated this explanation in the margin.

"And the statement of the commentator of al-Mawaqif: 'Whoever permits definition by simple meanings can say that simple meanings are not intentionally observed; when they are present and intentionally observed, they impart knowledge of the essence, even if that is rare.'

The author objected to the statement of the commentator of al-Mawaqif from multiple aspects, saying: 'It is obstinate and rejected. For the observation of the essence is not called acquisition by consensus; otherwise, verbal definition would be real definition, and the mention of nazar would produce a new knowledge, besides other necessary corruptions. And that the known essence is among the evident requisites of the simple meaning, even if the requisition occurs after its presence. So reflect on this.'

The margin text 'fa-in mulahazat al-mahiyyah...' is the first objection to the statement of the commentator of al-Mawaqif. The outcome of the objection is that observation is not called 'acquisition' by consensus, because if observation were synonymous with acquisition, then a verbal definition would necessarily be a real definition, since in a verbal definition, like a real one, observation exists. Then, if observation is considered in nazar, it would necessarily follow that whenever nazar is mentioned, a new limit or new knowledge would be obtained each time, because each time nazar is mentioned, observation is intentionally found.

The margin text 'wa an al-mahiyyah al-ma'lumah...' is a second objection to the statement of the commentator of al-Mawaqif.

The outcome of the objection is that even if the presence and observation of a simple meaning is possible and from them the known essence is obtained, nevertheless this presence and observation of the simple meaning is not called acquisition, because the known essence is among the evident requisites of the simple meaning. And it is self-evident that the requisites of a thing are not acquired, even if they are obtained after the presence of the simple meaning. In summary, the conception of a simple meaning entails the conception of its evident requisites, and requisites are not obtained through acquisition.

Therefore, defining nazar by observation is rejected. The correct view is that nazar should be defined by sequence (tartib), which entails two movements. In that case, a simple concept (baseet) cannot be a cause or a definition.

And his statement 'wa la muktasaban' because the accident does not convey the essence.

That is, just as a simple concept cannot be a cause, it also cannot be acquired. The meaning is that the knowledge of a simple thing cannot be obtained. For if knowledge of a simple thing is obtained, it would be either through the simple itself or through a compound. The first alternative (knowledge of a simple through itself) is invalid, as stated earlier that a simple cannot be a cause. The second alternative (knowledge of a simple through a compound) is also invalid. In that case, its definition would be composed of essential attributes, or accidental attributes, or both. All three possibilities are invalid. The invalidity of the first (composition of essentials) is self-evident, because the discussion is about a simple concept. If its definition becomes composite, it would no longer be simple but composite. The second (composition of accidents) is also invalid because it would not yield knowledge of the essence, as accidents do not give knowledge of reality. As for the third (composition of both essentials and accidents), its invalidity is also clear, because the sum of essential and accidental is accidental, just as the sum of inside and outside is outside, since the result follows the lower. Thus, the third aspect, in terms of meaning, reverts to the second aspect. Therefore, just as knowledge of the essence cannot be obtained from the second aspect (accidents), likewise from the third aspect (essential)...
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a detailed critical commentary on the definition of nazar (speculative thought) and the nature of simple concepts (baseet). The commentator begins by summarizing a verbal disagreement: some scholars define nazar as requiring two movements (harakatayn) such that a single movement would not be sufficient to cause knowledge; others accept a single movement with observation (mulahazah) of a suitable present meaning. The commentator notes that such a verbal disagreement is unseemly for scholars as it yields no practical consequence. He then cites and critiques the view of the commentator of al-Mawaqif, who allows definition by simple meanings on the grounds that even if rarely, observation of a simple meaning can impart knowledge of the essence. The author (presumably the commentator Ashraf al-Nu'ut) launches multiple objections: first, that observation (mulahazah) is not classified as 'acquisition' (kasb) by consensus; if it were, then every mention of nazar would produce new knowledge, which is absurd. Second, even if observation of a simple meaning is possible, the resulting knowledge of the essence is an evident requisite (lazim bayyin) of that simple meaning, and requisites are not acquired—they follow necessarily. Therefore, the definition of nazar must be based on sequence (tartib) which entails two movements. In that case, a simple concept cannot serve as a cause (sabab) or a definition (hadd). The commentator then explains the text 'wa la muktasaban' (and not acquired): a simple concept cannot be acquired because knowledge of it cannot be obtained either through itself (circular) or through a compound (since any composite definition would reduce to accidents, which cannot convey the essence). This aligns with Hanafi usul methodology, which emphasizes the necessity of sequential reasoning (nazar) for acquiring knowledge of the unknown.

Key Terms
نظر (nazar): Speculative thought that requires ordering (tartib) of two movements to produce knowledge of the unknown
بسیط (baseet): A simple concept that cannot be defined by parts (no essential or accidental composition)
کسب (kasb): Acquisition of knowledge through deliberate effort, not mere observation
ملاحظہ (mulahazah): Intentional observation or consideration of a meaning
لوازم بینہ (lawazim bayyinah): Evident requisites that necessarily follow from something without need for acquisition
تعریف لفظی (ta'rif lafzi): Verbal definition that explains a term but does not provide real knowledge of essence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why can a simple concept (baseet) not be defined?
A) Because it is unknown
B) Because it has no parts and any definition would either be circular or reduce to accidents which cannot convey essence
C) Because it is too complex
D) Because the scholar of al-Mawaqif forbade it

Key Takeaway
Nazar must involve two ordered mental movements; simple concepts (baseet) cannot serve as causes or be acquired because they have no parts and their requisites are self-evident.

Definition of Ta'rif in Hanafi Usul
Opening of the logical definition section in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of mu'arraf, distinguish between real, formal, and verbal definitions, and explain the conditions of jam' and mani'.

Core Idea
A proper definition prevents both false inclusion and false exclusion — it must be jam' and mani'.

This passage from the matn of Muslim al-Thubut begins the section on definition (ta'rif) in logic, which is foundational for understanding how Hanafi usul scholars define technical terms. The author lays down the basic requirement that a definition must prevent unwanted entry and unwanted exit, establishing the twin criteria of inclusiveness and exclusiveness. He then categorizes definitions into three types based on the kind of properties used.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the literal meaning
Understand the phrase 'prevents the entering from going out and the one outside from entering'. This means the definition must include all intended instances (jam') and exclude all others (mani').
This is the core requirement of a valid definition.
2
Identify the three types of definition
Real (haqiqi) uses essential properties; formal (rasmi) uses necessary concomitants; verbal (lafzi) uses a synonym or a more obvious word.
Each type has its own use in scholarly discourse.
3
Understand the essential (dhati)
Recognize that dhati is understood only when the essence is understood, and it is defined as that which has no cause (ghayr ma'lul).
This distinguishes essential from accidental properties.
4
Apply to a Hanafi fiqh term
Consider the term 'salah' and see if its definition meets jam' and mani'. For example, 'salah is specific words and actions beginning with takbir and ending with taslim' includes all valid salah and excludes invalid acts.
This illustrates practical application.

Source Text
