ترجمہ :۔ معرف وہ ہے جو داخل کو خارج ہونے سے اور خارج کو داخل ہونے سے روک دے اس لئے معرف کا جامع و مانع ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اور تمام اعتراضات جو تعرات پر کئے جاتے ہیں دعاوی ہیں ان کے جواب میں ”لا“ کہنا کافی ہے۔ اور وہ حقیقی ہے اگر تعریف ذاتیات سے ہو اور رکھی ہے اگر لازم کے ذریعہ سے ہو۔ اور تعریف لفظی کہلاتی ہے اگر اس سے زیادہ مشہور واضح اور مرادف لفظ سے ہو۔ اور تعریف لفظی کی عام سے بھی اجازت دی گئی ہے۔ اور ذاتی وہ چیز ہے جسکا سمجھنا ذات کے سمجھنے پر موقوف ہو اور کہا گیا ہے کہ ذاتی وہ ہے جو غیر معلل ہو ( یعنی ذاتی وہ جس کا ثبوت
Text of al-Muslim: The definition is that which prevents the entering from going out and the one outside from entering. Therefore it must be inclusive and exclusive. All objections to definitions are mere claims, and denial suffices in response. It is real (haqiqi) if it is by essential properties, and formal (rasmi) if by necessary concomitants, and verbal (lafzi) if by a more obvious synonym. And it has been permitted [to define] by a more general term. The essential (dhati) is that whose understanding is dependent on understanding the essence, and it is said: it is that which is not caused, and it is refuted by possibility if there is no possibility by another.
Translation: The definition is that which prevents the entering from going out and the one outside from entering. Therefore the definition must be comprehensive and exclusive. All objections made against definitions are mere claims, and saying 'no' in response suffices. It is real if the definition is by essential properties, and formal if by a necessary concomitant. It is called verbal if it is by a more famous, clear, and synonymous word. And it has been permitted [to define] by a general [term]. The essential is that whose understanding is dependent on understanding the essence, and it is said that the essential is that which is not caused (i.e., the essential is that whose proof
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage introduces the concept of definition (ta'rif) in logic as applied to usul al-fiqh. The definition must be jam' (comprehensive, including all instances) and mani' (exclusive, excluding non-instances). The author, following the text of Muslim al-Thubut, explains that criticisms of definitions are mere claims and can be answered by simple denial (man'). Three types of definition are distinguished: haqiqi (real definition) using essential properties, rasmi (formal definition) using necessary properties, and lafzi (verbal definition) using a synonymous term. The essential (dhati) is defined as that which is understood only when the essence is understood, or as that which has no cause (ghayr ma'lul). This sets the foundation for the logical analysis of definitions in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
معرف (mu'arraf): A definition that prevents the entry of what should be excluded and excludes what should enter
تعریف حقیقی (ta'rif haqiqi): Real definition using essential (dhati) properties
تعریف رسمی (ta'rif rasmi): Formal definition using necessary properties (lazim)
تعریف لفظی (ta'rif lafzi): Verbal definition using a more obvious synonym
ذاتی (dhati): Essential property that is understood when the essence is understood

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what type of definition uses a more obvious synonym?
A) Real definition (haqiqi)
B) Formal definition (rasmi)
C) Verbal definition (lafzi)
D) Essential definition

Key Takeaway
A proper definition in Hanafi usul must be comprehensive (jam') and exclusive (mani'), and can be real, formal, or verbal depending on the properties used.

8 min
Definition of Definition in Hanafi Usul
Explanation of the definiens and the tard wa 'aks condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the early and later Hanafi positions on the condition of tard wa ‘aks in definition, and explain the practical consequence of this difference.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, a valid definiens must be coextensive with its definiendum — unless you are a later Hanafi.

This passage from Ashraf al-Nu‘ut, a commentary on Musallam al-Thubut, tackles a foundational question: what makes a definition valid? The author presents two competing Hanafi views on whether the definiens must perfectly match the definiendum. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of how later Hanafi usul evolved, particularly in allowing broader, more practical definitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context and purpose of the passage
The author has just finished discussing nazar (speculative thought) and now turns to the method in which nazar occurs. Knowledge is either tasawwur (conceptualization) or tasdiq (assent), and the method for reaching speculative conceptualization is called mu'arrif (definiens). The passage aims to define what mu'arrif is.
Understanding this context clarifies why the author discusses definition before proof (hujjah).
2
Extract the definition of mu'arrif from the text
The text states: 'al-mu'arrif is that which prevents the entrant from exiting and prevents the outsider from entering.' This means the definiens must include all individuals of the definiendum (comprehensiveness) and exclude all non-individuals (exclusiveness).
This is the literal definition given in the matn.
3
Understand the condition of tard wa ‘aks
The author adds 'thus tard and 'aks are necessary.' Tard means coextension: the definiens applies to everything the definiendum applies to. 'Aks means coexistence: the definiens applies only to things the definiendum applies to. Together they require exact equivalence (musawat) between definiens and definiendum.
This is the condition of a perfect definition according to early Hanafis.
4
Compare the early and later Hanafi positions
Early Hanafis (mutaqaddimin) insist on tard wa 'aks as necessary. Later Hanafis (muta'akhkhirin) do not; they allow a definition using a more general term, because the purpose of definition is merely to produce conceptualization (ta'sir).
The commentator notes that the author's wording can be interpreted either as following the early method or as describing the perfect instance for the later method.
5
Determine the actual purpose of the passage
The commentator clarifies that the passage does not give a strict definition of mu'arrif, but rather a statement of its ruling (according to early scholars) or a depiction of its perfect instance (according to later scholars). The later scholars define mu'arrif as 'a statement said about something for the purpose of conceptualizing it.'
This distinguishes between a definition (hadd/rasm) and a description of conditions/rulings.

Source Text

تمهيد: جب مصنف نظر کی تعریف اور وجوب نظر کے بیان سے فارغ ہوئے تو وہ کیا اس طریق کے بیان کرنے کا جس میں نظر واقع ہوتی ہے، چنانچہ یہ معلوم ہے کہ علم تصور ہوگا یا تصدیق اور ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک بدیہی و نظر ہوتا ہے ، پس تصوری نظری کے لئے ایک ایسا طریق نظر چاہئے جس میں نظر کرنے سے تصور نظری کے حصول تک پہنچنا ممکن ہو سکے اس طرح تصدیق نظری کے لئے بھی ایسا طریق نظر چاہئے جس میں نظر کرنے سے تصدیق نظری کے حصول تک پہو نچنا ممکن ہو سکے۔ طریق اول کو معرف کہتے ہیں، اور طریق دوم کو صحت سے تعبیر کرتے ہیں۔ پھر چونکہ تصدیق اپنے تحقق میں تصور کا محتاج ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس طریق سے بحث کرنا جو موصل بجانب تصور ہو مقدم ہوگا اس طریق کی بحث پر جو موصل بجانب تصدیق ہے اس لئے مصنف نے نظر کے دونوں طریق کو بیان کیا اور معرف کو حجت پر مقدم کیا تا کہ وضع طبع کے موافق ہو جائے تو کہا المعرف ما منع ۔
تشريح قوله المعرف مامنع الوالج من الخروج الخ معرف بالکسر وہ ایسا قول یا طریق کا سب ہے جو معرف بالفتح ، کے افراد میں داخل کو خروج سے اور معرف بالفتح کے افراد سے خارج کو دخول سے منع کرے۔ معنی یہ ہے کہ معرف بالکسر اس حیثیت کا ہو کہ معرف بالفتح بھی اسی پر صادق آئے جس پر معرف بالکسر صادق آتا ہے جس کا مفہوم مطابقی یہ ہے کہ معرف معرف کے جمیع افراد کو جامع ہو۔ اور اسی طرح معرف بالکسر بھی اسی پر صادق آئے جس پر معرف بافتح صادق آرہا ہے جس کا مفہوم مطابقی یہ ہے کہ معرف معرف میں غیر افراد کے دخول کو مانع ہو۔ اس مفہوم کی طرف ماتن نے اپنے قول فیجب الطر دو العکس سے اشارہ کیا ہے۔ حاصل تعریف :- یہ ہے کہ معرف بالکسر معرف بالفتح کے ساتھ صدق میں مساوی ہوگا یعنی معرف ہر اس چیز پر صادق آئے گا جس پر معرف صادق آتا ہے اور جس پر معرف صادق آتا ہے اس پر معرف بھی صادق آئے گا۔ چونکہ معرف و معرف میں تساوی ہے جو تلازم فی الثبوت اور تلازم فی الانتفاء کو مستلزم ہے۔ یعنی جن افراد پر معرف صادق آئے گا معرف بھی صادق آئے گا اور جن افراد پر معرف صادق نہیں آئے گا معرف بھی صادق نہیں آئیگا۔
مندرجہ بالا تفصیل سے ظاہر ہے کہ مصنف روش قد ماء پر چلے ہیں جو تعریف میں طردو عکس کو لازم گردانتے ہیں کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک معرف و معرف میں مساوات شرط ہے۔ اس کے برعکس حضرات متأخرین طر دو عکس کو لازم نہیں قرار دیتے ہیں چنانچہ لفظ عام سے بھی ان کے نزدیک تعریف جائز ہے گو کہ یہ تعریف کا فرد ناقص ہے مگر اس سے تعریف جائز ہے اور وہ تعریف جوھی کی مساوی کے ذریعہ سے ہوتی ہے وہ رسم کامل کہلاتی ہے۔ الغرض مصنف کی ذکر کردہ تعریف مذاق قدماء پر بر بنائے شہرت ہے یا پھر مسلک متاخرین پر معرف کے فرد کامل کی تفسیر ہے مگر ہر دو تقدیر یہ معرف کی تعریف نہیں ۔ بلکہ قدماء کے مذہب پر معرف بالکسر کے حکم کا بیان ہے اس لئے کہ جامع مانع ہونا معرف کے احکام میں سے ہے یونہی مذہب متأخرین کے مطابق بھی یہ معرف تعریف نہیں بلکہ تعریف کے فرد کامل کے حکم کا بیان ہے اس لئے کہ وہ جوشی کے لئے امر مساوی ہے اس پر یہ تعریف صادق آتی ہے گرچہ وہ امر مساوی معرف نہ ہو جیسے متعجب کہ وہ انسان کے مساوی ہے حالانکہ متعجب انسان کا معرف نہیں ہے، اس لئے متاخرین نے معرف کی ایسی تعریف کی ہے جو امر مساوی ، اعم واخص سب کو شامل ہے اور وہ یہ ہے۔ المعرف المقول علی الشئی لافادة تصورہ ۔ لہذا یہ کہا جائے کہ مصنف کا مقصود اس مقام پر تعریف ، کرنا نہیں ہے بلکہ معرف کی تصویر کشی مقصود ہے چونکہ ان چیزوں کا ذہن میں حاصل کرنا جو اپنی ذاتیات وعرضیات کے ساتھ پہلے حاصل نہیں تھی تعریف کہلاتی ہے جبکہ ذاتیات و عرضیات کو اس طرح ترتیب دیا جائے کہ وہ ترتیب مطلوب تک پہو نچادے۔
Prolegomenon: When the author completed the definition of nazar and the obligation of nazar, he proceeded to the method in which nazar occurs. Thus it is known that knowledge is either tasawwur or tasdiq, and each of these is either badihi or nazari. For tasawwur nazari, a method of nazar is needed such that by looking one can reach attainment of the tasawwur nazari; similarly for tasdiq nazari, a method is needed such that by looking one can possibly reach the tasawwur nazari. The first method is called mu‘arrif, and the second method is called hujjah. Then, because tasdiq in its verification is in need of tasawwur, discussion of the method that leads to tasawwur takes precedence over discussion of the method that leads to tasdiq. Therefore the author mentioned both methods of nazar and placed mu‘arrif before hujjah to follow the natural order. So he said: 'al-mu‘arrif is that which prevents...'

Explanation of his statement: 'al-mu‘arrif is that which prevents the entrant from exiting, etc.' Mu‘arrif (with kasr) is a statement or method that prevents the entry of what is inside from exiting, and prevents the exit of what is outside from entering the individuals of mu‘arraf (with fatha). The meaning is that mu‘arrif (with kasr) is such that mu‘arraf (with fatha) also applies to whatever mu‘arrif applies to, which by its lexical meaning is that mu‘arrif encompasses all individuals of mu‘arraf. Similarly, mu‘arrif also applies to whatever mu‘arraf applies to, which by its lexical meaning is that mu‘arrif prevents the entry of non-individuals into mu‘arraf. The author indicated this meaning by his statement: 'Thus tard and ‘aks are necessary.' The summary of the definition is that mu‘arrif is equivalent to mu‘arraf in application; i.e., mu‘arrif applies to everything mu‘arraf applies to, and everything mu‘arraf applies to, mu‘arrif also applies to. Since mu‘arrif and mu‘arraf are equivalent, this entails co-presence and co-absence: i.e., to whatever individuals mu‘arrif applies, mu‘arraf also applies, and to whatever individuals mu‘arrif does not apply, mu‘arraf also does not apply.

From the above detail it is clear that the author follows the method of the early scholars who consider tard and ‘aks necessary in definition, because in their view equivalence between mu‘arrif and mu‘arraf is a condition. In contrast, the later scholars do not consider tard and ‘aks necessary. Thus, in their view, definition by a general term is permissible, even though such definition is an imperfect instance, but definition by it is permissible. And the definition that is by way of equivalence is called 'perfect delineation' (rasm kamil). In short, the definition mentioned by the author is either based on the taste of the early scholars by way of reputation, or it is an interpretation of the perfect instance of mu‘arrif according to the later scholars. But in both cases this is not the definition of mu‘arrif. Rather, according to the early scholars it is a statement of the ruling of mu‘arrif, because being comprehensive and exclusive is among the rulings of mu‘arrif. Similarly, according to the later scholars this is not the definition of mu‘arrif; rather it is a statement of the ruling of the perfect instance of definition, because that which is equivalent to a thing, this definition applies to it even if that equivalent is not a mu‘arrif for it – for example, 'muta‘ajjib (the rational animal)' is equivalent to 'insan' but 'muta‘ajjib' is not a mu‘arrif for 'insan'. Therefore the later scholars defined mu‘arrif with a definition that includes equivalent, more general, and more specific cases, which is: 'al-mu‘arrif is [a statement] said about something for the purpose of conceptualizing it.' So it can be said that the author's purpose here is not to define but rather to depict mu‘arrif. Because obtaining in the mind things that were not previously obtained along with their essentials and accidents is called 'definition' when those essentials and accidents are arranged in a way that leads to the desired end.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Musallam al-Thubut, specifically discussing the definition of a 'definition' (mu‘arrif) in usul al-fiqh. The author begins by explaining that after finishing the definition of nazar (speculative thought), the text proceeds to the method in which nazar occurs. Knowledge is divided into conceptualization (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq), and each is either intuitive (badihi) or speculative (nazari). The method to reach a speculative conceptualization is called 'mu‘arrif' (definiens), and the method for speculative assent is called 'hujjah' (proof). Since assent depends on conceptualization, the author discusses mu‘arrif first. The text then provides the definition of mu‘arrif: it is a statement that prevents the entry of what is not in the definiendum (mu‘arraf) and prevents the exit of what is in the definiendum. In other words, the definiens must be coextensive with the definiendum: it applies to all and only those things that the definiendum applies to. This is the condition of 'tard wa ‘aks' (coextension and coexistence). The commentator notes that this follows the method of the early scholars (mutaqaddimin) who require exact equivalence between definiens and definiendum. The later scholars (muta’akhkhirin) do not require this; they allow definition using a more general term, even if it is not coextensive. According to them, a perfect definition (al-rasm al-kamil) is one that uses an equivalent term, but a definition using a broader term is also permissible. The commentator clarifies that what the author has stated is not actually a definition of mu‘arrif but rather a description of its ruling (hukm) or a depiction of its perfect instance. The later scholars define mu‘arrif as 'a statement said about something for the purpose of conceptualizing it.' Thus, the author's purpose here is not to give a strict definition but to illustrate the concept.

Key Terms
المعرف بالکسر (al-mu‘arrif bi al-kasr): The definiens: a statement or method that serves to define something.
طرد (tard): Coextension: the definiens applies to everything the definiendum applies to.
عکس (‘aks): Coexistence: the definiens applies only to things the definiendum applies to.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the early Hanafi scholars (mutaqaddimin), what condition is necessary for a valid definiens (mu‘arrif)?
A) It must be more general than the definiendum.
B) It must be coextensive with the definiendum (tard wa ‘aks).
C) It must be a single word.
D) It must be derived from the Quran.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, whether tard wa ‘aks are necessary conditions for a valid definition depends on whether you follow the early or later scholars.

Definition Criteria: Coextensiveness (Tard wa 'Aks) in Hanafi Usul
Explaining the disagreement on definition criteria between early and later Hanafi scholars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the early and later Hanafi positions on definition criteria and evaluate the practical impact of accepting a broader definition.

Core Idea
Early scholars require coextensiveness; later scholars accept definitions via broader terms.

In Hanafi usul, the criteria for a valid definition have been debated. The early scholars (متقدمون) insisted that a definition must be coextensive (طرد و عكس) with the definiendum. The later scholars (متأخرون) relaxed this, allowing definition by a general term or an equal accident. This lesson unpacks that debate and its implications for how we define legal concepts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Locate the early scholars' requirement of coextensiveness and the later scholars' acceptance of broader definitions.
2
Understand the early requirement
Early scholars demand equality (musawat) between definition and definiendum; definition must be jami' mani' (comprehensive and exclusive).
3
Understand the later flexibility
Later scholars define definition as any statement conveying the concept (tafhid al-tasawwur), allowing definition by a general term (amm) or equal accident (musawi).
4
Examine the concrete example
Consider the case of 'muta'ajjib' (the amazed one) which is equal to 'insan' (human) but not a definition of human. This illustrates the later view accepting non-coextensive definitions.
The example shows that equality does not guarantee definition.
5
Derive the practical outcome
Early scholars would reject definitions that are not coextensive; later scholars would accept them if they convey the concept. This affects which definitions are used in legal reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مندرجہ بالا تفصیل سے ظاہر ہے کہ مصنف روش قد ماء پر چلے ہیں جو تعریف میں طردو عکس کو لازم گردانتے ہیں کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک معرف و معرف میں مساوات شرط ہے۔ اس کے برعکس حضرات متأخرین طر دو عکس کو لازم نہیں قرار دیتے ہیں چنانچہ لفظ عام سے بھی ان کے نزدیک تعریف جائز ہے گو کہ یہ تعریف کا فرد ناقص ہے مگر اس سے تعریف جائز ہے اور وہ تعریف جوھی کی مساوی کے ذریعہ سے ہوتی ہے وہ رسم کامل کہلاتی ہے۔ الغرض مصنف کی ذکر کردہ تعریف مذاق قدماء پر بر بنائے شہرت ہے یا پھر مسلک متاخرین پر معرف کے فرد کامل کی تفسیر ہے مگر ہر دو تقدیر یہ معرف کی تعریف نہیں ۔ بلکہ قدماء کے مذہب پر معرف بالکسر کے حکم کا بیان ہے اس لئے کہ جامع مانع ہونا معرف کے احکام میں سے ہے یونہی مذہب متأخرین کے مطابق بھی یہ معرف تعریف نہیں بلکہ تعریف کے فرد کامل کے حکم کا بیان ہے اس لئے کہ وہ جوشی کے لئے امر مساوی ہے اس پر یہ تعریف صادق آتی ہے گرچہ وہ امر مساوی معرف نہ ہو جیسے متعجب کہ وہ انسان کے مساوی ہے حالانکہ متعجب انسان کا معرف نہیں ہے، اس لئے متاخرین نے معرف کی ایسی تعریف کی ہے جو امر مساوی ، اعم واخص سب کو شامل ہے اور وہ یہ ہے۔ المعرف المقول علی الشئی لافادة تصورہ ۔ لہذا یہ کہا جائے کہ مصنف کا مقصود اس مقام پر تعریف کرنا نہیں ہے بلکہ معرف کی تصویر کشی مقصود ہے چونکہ ان چیزوں کا ذہن میں حاصل کرنا جو اپنی ذاتیات وعرضیات کے ساتھ پہلے حاصل نہیں تھی تعریف کہلاتی ہے جبکہ ذاتیات و عرضیات کو اس طرح ترتیب دیا جائے کہ وہ ترتیب مطلوب تک پہو نچادے۔
From the above detail it is apparent that the author follows the method of the early scholars who consider coextensiveness (tard wa 'aks) necessary in definition, because according to them equality between the definiendum and the definition is a condition. In contrast, the later scholars do not consider coextensiveness necessary; thus according to them definition by a general term is permissible even though it is an imperfect individual of definition, but definition by it is permissible. And that definition which is through an equal of the thing is called a complete descriptive definition (rasm kamil). In short, the definition mentioned by the author is based on the preference of the early school, or it is an interpretation of the perfect individual of the definiendum according to the later school. But on both estimations, it is not a definition of the definiendum. Rather, according to the early school it is a statement of the ruling of the definiendum, because being comprehensive and exclusive is among the rulings of the definiendum. Similarly, according to the later school it is not a definition of the definiendum but a statement of the ruling of the perfect individual of definition, because it is equal to the thing; this definition applies to it even if that equal is not the definiendum, like 'the one who is amazed' (muta'ajjib) which is equal to 'human', although 'the one who is amazed' is not a definition of 'human'. Therefore, the later scholars made a definition of the definiendum that includes equal, more general, and more specific all, and it is: 'A definition is that which is said about a thing for the purpose of gaining its concept.' Hence it may be said that the author's purpose here is not to define but to depict the definiendum. Since obtaining something in the mind that was not previously obtained with its essential and accidental properties is called definition, when the essential and accidental properties are arranged in such a way that the arrangement leads to the desired end.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage discusses the criteria for a valid definition (تعريف) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, focusing on the disagreement between the early scholars (متقدمين) and later scholars (متأخرين). The author follows the early view that definition must be coextensive (طرد و عكس) with the definiendum, meaning it must apply to all and only instances of the definiendum. The later scholars, however, allow definition by a broader term (عام) even if it is not perfectly coextensive, calling such a definition 'complete descriptive definition' (رسم كامل). The passage clarifies that the author's definition is not actually defining the definiendum but either stating a ruling about it (according to early scholars) or describing a perfect individual of definition (according to later scholars). The later scholars define 'definition' broadly as something that conveys the concept of the thing, whether equal, general, or specific. The passage concludes that the author's intent is depiction (تصویر) rather than strict definition.

Key Terms
طرد و عكس (tard wa 'aks): Coextensiveness: the definition applies to all instances of the definiendum and only those instances.
رسم کامل (rasm kamil): A complete descriptive definition using equal accidentals.
معرف (mu'arraf): The definiendum: the thing being defined.
تعریف (ta'rif): Definition: a statement that conveys the concept of a thing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to early Hanafi scholars, what is required for a valid definition?
A) It must be coextensive (tard wa 'aks) with the definiendum.
B) It can be broader than the definiendum.
C) It must be narrower than the definiendum.
D) It can be any statement that conveys the concept.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains two valid views on definition: one requiring coextensiveness (early) and one allowing broader terms (later).

Objections to Definitions Require Evidence: The Rule of Man', Naqd, and Mu'arada
Explaining that objections require evidence and are claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that objections to definitions in usul al-fiqh must be supported by evidence, and distinguish between valid and invalid objections.

Core Idea
An objection to a definition is a claim that requires proof; otherwise, the definer may simply reject it.

In usul al-fiqh, definitions are precise constructs. When someone objects to a definition, that objection is itself a claim about the definition's shortcomings. This passage establishes a procedural rule: the objector must provide evidence for his objection. Without evidence, the definer can respond with mere prevention (man'). This ensures that definitions are not dismissed lightly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of objection
Recognize the three standard objections: man' (prevention), naqd (refutation), and mu'arada (confrontation). Each is a claim about the definition's validity.
These are the 'three objections' (اعتراضات ثلاث) mentioned in the text.
2
Recognize the implicit claims in a definition
Every definition carries implicit claims (da'awi dhimniyya), such as being a proper definition (haddi), descriptive (rasmi), comprehensive and exclusive (jami' mani'), etc. Objections target these implicit claims.
Without these implicit claims, objections would have no basis.
3
Understand the requirement of evidence
The objector must provide proof (shahid) for his objection. Mere assertion is insufficient. The evidence supports the objection and prevents the definer from simply closing the door.
The text says: 'منع مجرد نا کافی ہے بلکہ منع کے ساتھ شاہد بھی ضروری ہے'
4
Apply the procedural response
If the objector provides no evidence, the definer can respond with mere man' (prevention), which is sufficient procedurally. If evidence is provided, the objection transforms into naqd or a claim of deficiency.
The definer may also provide his own evidence for a stronger response.

قوله وجميع الايرادات على التعريفات دعادى الخ تقریر سابق سے معلوم ہو گیا کہ وہ جو نظر وفکر سے حاصل نہ ہوں جیسے ملزومات کا تصور اس کے لوازم سے وہ بالیقین تعریف نہیں ہوتی بلکہ تعریف وہ ہوتی ہے جو بطریق نظر وفکر حاصل ہو البتہ اسکو تصویر کہہ سکتے ہیں اور جب معرف تعریف نہیں تصویر ہوتی ہے تو اس پر اقامت دلیل کی حاجت بھی نہیں ہوگی اس وجہ سے اعتراضات ثلاث منع نقض اور معارضہ میں سے کسی سے بھی تعریف پر اعتراض کرنا صحیح نہیں کیوں کہ ان تینوں میں سے کسی سے اعتراض کرنے کے لئے اولا دعوی ضروری ہے اور ثانیا اس دعوی کی دلیل ضروری ہے تا کہ اس دلیل کے کسی مقدمہ معینہ پر منع نقض اور معارضہ وارد کیا جا سکے .. ہاں البتہ تعریف دعاوی ضمیہ پر مشتمل ہوتی ہے جیسے یہ دھوئی کہ یہ تعریف مثلا حدی ہے رسمی ہے یا تعریف جامع و مانع ہے وغیرہ پس ان دعاوی ضمنیہ کے پیش نظر تعریف پر منوع ثلثہ مذکورہ متوجہ ہو سکتے ہیں لیکن منع مجرد نا کافی ہے بلکہ منع کے ساتھ شاہد بھی ضروری ہے تا کہ تعریف کا دروازہ بند نہ ہو جائے ۔ اور جب منع شاہد کے ساتھ وارد ہوگا تو وہ نقض کی طرف اور عدم جامعیت، مانعیت کے دعوی کی طرف راجع ہوتا ہے اسلئے مصنف نے کہا و جمیع الا سرادات علی التعریف دعاوی ۔ یعنی تمام اعتراضات جو تعریف وارد کئے جاتے ہیں وہ در حقیقت دعوے ہوتے ہیں اور دعاوی ضمنیہ کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے وارد کئے جاتے ہیں اس لئے معترض کے لئے لازم ہے کہ اپنے دعوی یا اعتراض پر دلیل و شاہد بھی پیش کرے مثال کے طور پر معترض تعریف پر یہ اعتراض کرے کہ یہ تعریف حدی نہیں ہو سکتی، یار کمی نہیں ہو سکتی یا جامع ومانع نہیں ہے وغیرہ اور اس پر شاہد و دلیل نہ پیش کرے تو ان اعتراضات کے جواب میں منع کافی ہے یعنی تعریف کرنے والا یہ کہے گا کہ اے معترض ! تم نے جو اعتراض وارد کیا ہے ہم اس پر منع وارد کرتے ہیں یا ہم اسے تسلیم نہیں کرتے جیتک تم اس منع کے ساتھ دلیل نہ پیش کرو گے اور اگر تعریف کنندہ تعریف پر اعتراض کے جواب میں منع کے ساتھ شاہد بھی ذکر کر دیتا ہے تو یہ زیادہ نفع بخش ہوگا گو کہ صرف منع بھی کافی ہے۔
His statement: 'And all objections to definitions are claims, etc.' From the previous discussion it became clear that what is not obtained through reflection and consideration, like the conception of entailments from their correlates, is certainly not definition; rather definition is what is obtained through the method of reflection and consideration. However, it can be called a depiction. And when the definiendum is not a definition but a depiction, then there is no need to provide evidence for it. For this reason, it is not correct to object to a definition by any of the three objections: prevention (man'), refutation (naqd), and confrontation (mu'arada), because to object by any of these three requires first a claim and second a proof for that claim, so that prevention, refutation, or confrontation can be directed at a specific premise of that proof. Yes, but a definition contains implicit claims (da'awi dhimniyya), such as that this definition is, for example, a proper definition (haddi) or a descriptive definition (rasmi), or that the definition is comprehensive and exclusive (jami' mani'), etc. So in view of these implicit claims, the three mentioned objections can be directed at the definition. However, mere prevention (man' mujarrad) is insufficient; rather, evidence (shahid) is necessary along with the prevention, so that the door of definition is not closed. And when prevention is presented with evidence, it reverts to refutation (naqd) and to the claim of lack of comprehensiveness or exclusivity. Therefore the author said: 'And all objections to definitions are claims.' That is, all objections that are made to definitions are in fact claims, and they are made with regard to implicit claims. Hence it is necessary for the objector to present proof and evidence for his claim or objection. For example, if the objector objects to a definition saying 'this definition cannot be a proper definition, or it cannot be a descriptive definition, or it is not comprehensive and exclusive,' etc., and does not present evidence and proof for it, then in response to these objections, prevention (man') is sufficient. That is, the definer will say: O objector! The objection you have made, we prevent it (we do not accept it) until you present proof along with this prevention. And if the definer, in response to the objection on the definition, mentions evidence along with prevention, this would be more beneficial, although mere prevention is also sufficient.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage explains the proper method of objecting to definitions in usul al-fiqh. It distinguishes between concepts obtained through reflection (which constitute true definitions) and those obtained through entailments (which are merely depictions). The three standard objections (منع prevention, نقض refutation, معارضة confrontation) are only valid if they are based on a claim supported by evidence (دلیل). Definitions themselves contain implicit claims (دعاوی ضمنیة) about their nature (e.g., being a proper definition, comprehensive, etc.). A bare objection without evidence is not sufficient; the objector must provide evidence (شاہد) to support his objection. If the definer responds with mere prevention (منع), it is acceptable until evidence is provided. However, it is better for the definer to also provide evidence to strengthen his position. This procedural rule ensures that definitions are not rejected without substantive argument.

Key Terms
منع (man'): Prevention: rejecting an objection or claim as unfounded without evidence.
نقض (naqd): Refutation: showing that the definition does not cover a case it should or includes a case it should not.
معارضہ (mu'arada): Confrontation: presenting a counter-definition or counter-argument.
دعوی ضمنی (da'wa dhimniyya): Implicit claim: a claim that is necessarily implied by a statement, e.g., that a definition is comprehensive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is required for an objection to a definition to be valid according to this passage?
A) The objection must be stated clearly.
B) The objector must provide evidence for his objection.
C) The objection must be from the Quran or Sunnah.
D) The definer must accept the objection immediately.

Key Takeaway
An objection to a definition is a claim; without supporting evidence, the definer may reject it outright.

Types of Definitions: Essential, Descriptive, Verbal
Classification of definitions into three types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define and distinguish the three types of definition (ta'rif haqiqi, rasmi, lafzi) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh and apply this classification to given definiendums.

Core Idea
Definitions in usul are classified by whether they use essential properties, accidental properties, or synonyms.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the precision of definition is crucial for legal reasoning. This passage from Ashraf al-Nu'ut introduces the threefold classification of definitions: essential (haqiqi), descriptive (rasmi), and verbal (lafzi). Understanding each type and their appropriate context enables the usuli to evaluate the strength of a definition in fiqh arguments. The passage also hints at a subtle difference between logicians and usul scholars, which affects how definitions are categorized.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types
Recognize the names haqiqi, rasmi, and lafzi and their Arabic terms from the passage.
These are the foundational categories in usul definitions.
2
Match each type with its defining characteristic
Essential definitions use essential properties (dhatiyat), descriptive definitions use accidents or consequences (lawazim), and verbal definitions use synonyms.
Pay attention to the examples given for each type.
3
Analyze the logician vs. usuli distinction
Note that logicians consider verbal definition as opposite to essential, while usul scholars have a different classification. The passage indicates that usul scholars do not treat verbal as the direct opposite.
This nuance affects the acceptance and use of definitions in legal reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وهو حقيقى ان كان بالذاتيات الخ یہاں سے مصنف معرف کی تقسیم کرنا چاہتے ہیں اس لئے کہا وھو حقیقی ۔ یعنی اجمالاً مجموعی طور پر معرف کی تین قسمیں ہیں۔ حقیقی ، رسمی لفظی ، تعریف حقیقی وہ ہے جوٹی کی تعریف ذاتیات کے ذریعہ سے ہو جیسے انسان کی تعریف حیوان ناطق ہے۔ رسمی وہ ہے جوشی تعریف اس کے لوازم کے ذریعہ سے ہو جیسے انسان کی تعریف کا تب سے اور شراب کی تعریف ہر اس بہنے والی چیز سے کی جاوے جو جھاگ لائے۔ تعریف لفظی اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ جو معرف کے مرادف اور اس سے لفظ سے ہو جیسے غضنفر کی تعریف اسد سے اور عقار کی تعریف خمر ہے۔ واضح رہے کہ منطقی کے نزدیک تعریف لفظی تعریف حقیقی کا مقابل ہوتی ہے پس حقیقی کے اندر حدور تم دونوں شامل ہوتی ہیں مگر اصولی کے نزدیک حقیقی کا مقابل
His statement: 'And it is essential if it is by essential properties, etc.' From here the author intends to divide the definiendum (or definition). Therefore he said 'it is essential'. That is, in brief, there are three types overall: essential (haqiqi), descriptive (rasmi), and verbal (lafzi). Essential definition is that which is a definition of a thing by means of its essential properties, like the definition of human as 'rational animal'. Descriptive definition is that which is a definition of a thing by means of its accidents or consequences (lawazim), like the definition of human as 'one who walks upright' and the definition of wine as 'every flowing thing that produces foam'. Verbal definition is that which is a synonym (muradif) of the definiendum and [is given] by a word, like the definition of ghadanfar (lion) by 'asad (lion) and the definition of 'uqqar (wine) by khamr (wine). It should be noted that according to the logician (mantiqi), verbal definition is opposite to essential definition; thus essential includes both proper definition (hadd) and descriptive definition (rasm). But according to the usuli (scholar of usul al-fiqh), the opposite of essential...
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage introduces the classification of definitions (تعریف) into three types in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author of the matn begins dividing the definiendum (or definition) into: 1) Essential definition (حقیقی): defined by the essential properties (ذاتیات) of the thing, e.g., 'human is a rational animal'. 2) Descriptive definition (رسمی): defined by accidents or consequential properties (لوازم), e.g., 'human is a walking upright being' or 'wine is a flowing thing that foams'. 3) Verbal definition (لفظی): defined by a synonym, e.g., 'ghadanfar is asad' or 'uqqar is khamr'. The passage notes a difference between logicians and usul scholars: logicians consider verbal definition as opposite to essential, while essential includes both proper definition (حد) and descriptive definition (رسم). Usul scholars have a different classification. The text is cut off but indicates that usul scholars treat the opposite of essential differently. This classification helps in analyzing definitions used in legal arguments.

Key Terms
تعریف حقیقی (ta'rif haqiqi): Essential definition: using essential properties (ذاتیات) of the thing.
تعریف رسمی (ta'rif rasmi): Descriptive definition: using accidents or consequences (لوازم) of the thing.
تعریف لفظی (ta'rif lafzi): Verbal definition: using a synonymous word.
ذاتیات (dhatiyat): Essential properties: properties that constitute the essence of a thing.
لوازم (lawazim): Accidents or necessary consequences of a thing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Descriptive definition (تعریف رسمی)
C) Verbal definition (تعریف لفظی)
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
The three types of definition in Hanafi usul—essential, descriptive, and verbal—differ in their use of essential properties, accidental properties, or synonyms, and their application depends on the context of legal reasoning.

Classification of Definitions: Haqiqi, Rasmi, Lafzi and Dhati
Explains the division of definitions and the meaning of dhati in usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between haqiqi, rasmi, and lafzi definitions according to Hanafi usul al-fiqh, and explain the meaning of dhati.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, definitions are haqiqi (real), rasmi (formal, within haqiqi), and lafzi (verbal); dhati means essential attributes.

This passage from Ashraf al-Nu'ut clarifies the classification of definitions (ta'rif) in usul al-fiqh, contrasting the approach of logicians with that of usuliyyun. You'll learn how Hanafi scholars divide definitions and why the term 'dhati' is crucial for understanding real definitions.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the logicians' classification
Identify how logicians divide definitions into haqiqi (giving an unacquired form) and lafzi (discriminating an acquired form), and then subdivide haqiqi into definition according to reality and according to name (rasmi).
Logicians treat rasmi as separate from haqiqi.
2
Identify the usuliyyun's modification
Note how usul scholars redefine the division: they consider rasmi a subtype of haqiqi and add lafzi as a primary division alongside haqiqi and rasmi.
This is a key difference between logic and usul.
3
Understand the term dhati
Examine the definition of dhati: 'what is understood in understanding the essence' – the intrinsic attributes that constitute the quiddity.
Dhati is used in haqiqi definitions.
4
Apply the classification
Practice classifying sample definitions into haqiqi, rasmi, or lafzi, and identify the dhati attributes.
Familiarize with examples like 'insan = hayawan natiq' (haqiqi), 'kalima = lafz wadi' li-ma'na mufrad' (rasmi), 'ghudanfar = asad' (lafzi).

رہی ہوتی ہے لفظی نہیں ، اس لئے مصنف نے رسی کوحقیقی کے مقابل رکھا ہے۔ اس کی مزید تفصیل یہ ہے کہ منطق کی اصطلاح میں حقیقی کا اطلاق کبھی لفظی کے مقابل ہوتا ہے اس تقدیر پر حقیقی بولی جاتی ہے ایسی چیز پر جس کے ذریعہ مٹی کی صورت غیر حاصلہ کو حاصل کیا جائے اور کبھی حقیقی کا اطلاق تعریف بحسب الحقیقہ پر ہوتا ہے جو تعریف بحسب الاسم کے مقابل ہوتی ہے جس میں معرف موجود کی حقیقت کی طرف وصول مقصود ہوتا ہے۔ چونکہ مناطقہ تعریف کی اس طرح تقسیم کرتے ہیں کہ تعریف یا تو ذہن میں صورت غیر حاصلہ حاصل کرائیگی یا صورت حاصلہ کا اپنے ماعدا اسے تمیز کا افادہ کرے گی بر تقدیر ثانی وہ تعریف لفظی ہے اس لئے کہ اس کا فائدہ یہ ہوتا ہے کہ معنی معین کے بالمقابل لفظ کی معرفت ہوتی ہے جیسے الغضنفر حوالاسد ۔ پھر لفظی کبھی مفرد ہوتی ہے جیسے مثال مذکور میں اور کبھی مرکب ہوتا ہے جیسے وجود کی تعریف الثابت العین وغیرہ الفاظ مرکبہ سے کرنا ، اور بر تقدیر اول (یعنی تعریف صورت غیر حاصلہ ذہن میں حاصل ہونے کا افادہ کرے گی ) تو اس کی بھی دوصورت ہوتی ہے کیونکہ ذہن میں یا تو ایسی صورت حاصل ہوگی جس کا وجود نفس الامر کے اعتبار سے جانا گیا ہو یانہیں برصورت اول تعریف بحسب الحقیقہ ہوتی ہے جیسے انسان کی تعریف حیوان ناطق ہے ۔ اور برصورت ثانی (یعنی اگر ایسی صورت کا علم حاصل ہو جس کا موجود ہو تانفس الامر کے اعتبار سے نہیں جانا گیا ہو بلکہ اسکا وجود صرف باعتبار اصطلاح دو ماہیات اعتباریہ میں سے ہونا معلوم ہو تو وہ تعریف بحسب الاسم ( تعریف رسمی ) ہے جیسے کلمہ کی تعریف ”لفظ وضع لمعنی مفرد سے کرنا۔
اس تفصیل سے ظاہر ہے کہ رسمی حقیقی میں داخل ہے اور لفظی حقیقی کے مقابل ہے۔ کا مناطقہ کا مذہب ہے اسکے برخلاف اصولیین کی اصطلاح میں حدوہ ہے جو مناطقہ کے نزدیک معرف ہے اس لئے اصولیین اس طرح تقسیم کرتے ہیں کہ حد سے یا تو صورت غیر حاصلہ کے حاصل کرنے کا قصد کیا جائے گا یا نہیں بلکہ خزانہ ذہن میں محفوظ معنی کے حاضر کرنے کا قصد کیا جائے گا بر تقدیر اول یا توشی کے ذات کی صورت حاصل ہوگی یا اس کے وجوہ میں سے کسی وجہ کی صورت حاصل ہوگی اول حقیقی ہے اس لئے کہ اس سے شئی کا تصور بالکنہ حاصل ہوتا ہے اور ثانی رسمی ہے اس لئے کہ اس سے شئی کا تصور بالوجہ حاصل ہوتا ہے۔ اور بر تقدیر ثانی (یعنی ظرف ذہن میں موجود و مخزون معنی کا احضار مقصود ہو ) تو لفظی
ہے۔ الغرض اصولین نے اطلاق حقیقی میں اور تعریف رسمی کو حقیقی کا مقابل قرار دینے میں مناطقہ کی مخالفت کی ہے اس لئے ان کے نزدیک معرف کی اقسام اولیہ حقیقی ، رسمی اور لفظی کہلاتی ہیں پس لفظی حقیقی اور رہی میں جاری ہو سکتی ہے جب ان دونوں پر ڈھول طاری ہو حالانکہ لفظی بظاہر حقیقی ورمی کی قسم ہے۔ قوله - قد اجيز بالاعم" یعنی لفظی تعریف میں چونکہ لفظ کی توضیح اس کے مرادف اظہر لفظ سے کی جاتی ہے اس لئے اس کی تعریف و توضیح ائم سے جائز قرار دی گئی ہے جیسے معدا نہ کی تعریف نسبت سے اور غضنفر کی تعریف اسد سے کی جائے ۔ مگر لفظی کے ساتھ یہ تخصیص بے محل ہے کیونکہ جنہوں نے عام سے تعریف کو جائز قرار دیا ہے ان کے نزدیک لفظی کی طرح حقیقی بھی عام سے جائز ہے اور جو عام سے تعریف کو جائز قرار نہیں دیتے ان کے نزدیک حقیقی ولفظی ہر ایک میں عام سے تعریف صحیح نہیں ہے۔
یہاں یہ بات ذہن نشین رہے کہ تعریف لفظی سے صورت حاصلہ کی تمیز مقصود یعنی اس کا مقصود اصلی ذہن میں حاصل شدہ معنی کی معرفت کہ اس کے مقابلہ میں لفظ کو وضع کیا جائے اور تصدیق ی نمکی جائے کہ لفظ مثلا اس معنی کیلئے ہے اس تقدیر پر لفظی مطالب تصدیقیہ سے ہوگی چنانچہ اسی لئے کہ لفظی سے احضار مقصود ہوتا ہے بعض لوگوں نے کہا کہ تعریف لفظی مطالب تصدیقیہ سے ہے۔ اور اگر لفظی سے معانی مخزونہ کے درمیان لفظ کے مدلول کا بیان اور لفظ اشہر سے معنی کی تصویر مقصود ہو تو اس وقت لفظی مطالب تصوریہ سے ہوگی اس لئے کہ لفظی سے لفظ کے مدلول کا بیان و تصویر ہوتا ہے بعض لوگوں نے کہا ہے کہ تعریف لفظی مطالب تصوریہ کے قبیل سے ہے حق یہ ہے کہ دونوں احتمال کے اعتبار سے دونوں مطالب سے ہو سکتی ہے۔
قوله والذاتى مافهمه في فهم الذات،
حقیقی کی تعریف میں مصنف نے لفظ ذاتیات کا استعمال کیا ہے اس لئے ضروری ہوا کہ ذاتی کی تعریف کی جائے کیونکہ بمطابق اصطلاح ایسا غوجی وفن برہان ذاتی کا اطلاق متعدد معنوں پر ہوتا ہے پس قاری کے لئے مقام تشویش تھا کہ مصنف نے تعریف حقیقی میں ذاتیات سے ذاتی کا کو نسا معنی مراد لیا ہے۔ اسلئے کہا الذاتي مافهمه في فهم الذات.
It remains verbal, not [real]. Therefore the author has placed 'rasmi' in contrast to 'haqiqi'. Further detail: In the terminology of logic, 'haqiqi' is sometimes used in contrast to 'lafzi'; in that case, 'haqiqi' is applied to something through which an unacquired mental form is acquired. Sometimes 'haqiqi' is applied to definition according to reality, which is opposite to definition according to name, where reaching the reality of the defined is intended. The logicians divide definition such that either it provides an unacquired form in the mind, or it provides discrimination of an acquired form from others. In the second case, it is 'lafzi' because its benefit is knowledge of the word corresponding to a specific meaning, like 'al-ghudanfar' is 'al-asad'. Then 'lafzi' is sometimes simple, as in the mentioned example, and sometimes compound, like defining existence as 'al-thabit al-ayn' with compound words. In the first case (definition providing an unacquired form), it has two types: either the form is known to exist in reality, or not. In the first case, it is definition according to reality, like defining human as 'hayawan natiq'. In the second case (if knowledge is obtained of a form whose existence in reality is unknown, but its existence is known only in terms of conventional matters), then it is definition according to name (rasmi definition), like defining 'kalima' as 'a word placed for a singular meaning'. From this detail it is clear that 'rasmi' is included in 'haqiqi' and 'lafzi' is opposite to 'haqiqi'. This is the view of the logicians. In contrast, in the terminology of the usuliyyun, 'hadd' is what the logicians call 'mu'arraf'. Therefore the usuliyyun divide such that by 'hadd' either the acquisition of an unacquired form is intended, or not, rather the bringing to mind of a meaning stored in the treasury of the mind is intended. In the first case, either the form of the thing's essence is obtained or the form of one of its aspects. The first is 'haqiqi' because it gives a complete conceptualization of the thing; the second is 'rasmi' because it gives a conceptualization by aspect. In the second case (i.e., bringing to mind a meaning present and stored in the mind is intended), then it is 'lafzi'. In short, the usuliyyun opposed the logicians in the usage of 'haqiqi' and in making 'rasmi' opposite to 'haqiqi'. Therefore according to them, the primary divisions of definition are called 'haqiqi', 'rasmi', and 'lafzi'. Thus 'lafzi' can apply to both 'haqiqi' and 'rasmi' when both are dominated [?], even though 'lafzi' apparently is a type of 'haqiqi' and 'rasmi'. His saying: 'It has been permitted with the more general' means: In lafzi definition, since the word is clarified by its more apparent synonym, its definition and clarification from the imams is deemed permissible, such as defining 'ma'dan' by 'nisbah' and 'ghudanfar' by 'asad'. But this specification with 'lafzi' is out of place, because those who permit definition by the more general consider it permissible for 'haqiqi' as well, and those who do not consider definition by the more general permissible do not accept it for either 'haqiqi' or 'lafzi'. Here it should be kept in mind: In lafzi definition, the discrimination of the acquired form is intended, i.e., its main purpose is knowledge of the meaning already acquired in the mind, that the word is placed for it, and verification that the word is for that meaning. In this case, lafzi definition is from the category of tasdiqi demands. Therefore, because lafzi definition aims at bringing to mind, some have said that lafzi definition is from tasdiqi demands. If by lafzi definition the expression of the word's meaning among stored meanings and the depiction of the meaning by a more famous word is intended, then lafzi definition is from tasawwuri demands, because by lafzi definition the expression and depiction of the word's meaning occurs. Some have said that lafzi definition is from the category of tasawwuri demands. The truth is that it can be from both demands depending on the probability. His saying: 'Al-dhati is what is understood in understanding the essence.' In the definition of haqiqi, the author used the word 'dhatiyat', so it became necessary to define 'dhati', because according to terminology, 'dhati' has multiple meanings in logic and the art of demonstration. So the reader would be confused as to which meaning of 'dhati' the author intended from 'dhatiyat' in the definition of haqiqi. Therefore he said: 'Al-dhati is what is understood in understanding the essence.'
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Nu'ut, a commentary on Muslim al-Thubut, discusses the classification of definitions (ta'rif) and clarifies the term 'dhati' (essential). The author first explains the logicians' (mantiqiyyun) division: they sometimes contrast 'haqiqi' with 'lafzi' (verbal), where 'haqiqi' gives an unacquired mental form, and 'lafzi' merely discriminates a known form. They then divide further: 'haqiqi' according to reality (bi hasab al-haqiqa) vs. according to name (bi hasab al-ism), the latter being 'rasmi' (formal). Usul al-fiqh scholars (usuliyyun) differ: they consider 'rasmi' within 'haqiqi' and treat 'lafzi' separately. For them, the primary divisions are haqiqi (real definition giving the essence), rasmi (formal definition giving an aspect), and lafzi (verbal definition explaining the word). The text then addresses the ruling on defining by a more general word (a'am): some permit it for both haqiqi and lafzi, others reject it entirely. Finally, the author explains 'dhati' because the matn used 'dhatiyat' in defining haqiqi. He states that 'dhati' is that which is understood in understanding the essence itself—i.e., the essential attributes that constitute the quiddity.

Key Terms
حقیقی (haqiqi): A definition that gives the complete essence (dhat) of a thing, providing a conceptualization of its quiddity.
رسمی (rasmi): A definition that gives an aspect (wajh) of the thing, not its complete essence; provides conceptualization by aspect.
لفظی (lafzi): A verbal definition that explains the meaning of a word by a synonym or more apparent term, without providing new conceptual content.
ذاتی (dhati): That which is understood in understanding the essence itself; the intrinsic attributes that form the quiddity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what does 'dhati' mean in the context of definition?
A) It refers to the essential attributes that constitute the essence of a thing.
B) It refers to accidental attributes that are not part of the essence.
C) It is synonymous with lafzi definition.
D) It is a type of formal definition (rasmi).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul classification of definitions—haqiqi, rasmi, and lafzi—with rasmi nested under haqiqi, provides a flexible tool for defining legal concepts, and dhati denotes the essential attributes that form the core of real definitions.

Resolving the Tahsil al-Hasil Objection in Defining Mahiyya
Resolving the objection that definition by parts is tautological

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi usul tradition resolves the tahsil al-hasil objection by distinguishing between detailed and unitary knowledge.

Core Idea
Defining mahiyya by its parts produces a new unitary form, not a tautology.

This passage tackles a foundational objection against definition itself: if a thing's essence is already known, breaking it into parts yields no new knowledge. The Hanafi scholar refutes this by showing that the ordered combination of parts generates a holistic conception (sura wahidaniyya) that was not previously possessed. Understanding this resolution is critical for appreciating why definitions are meaningful in legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
State the tahsil al-hasil argument: defining mahiyya by itself or its parts is redundant because both are already known.
The objection assumes knowledge of the whole implies knowledge of the parts in detail.
2
Examine the answer's key distinction
The author distinguishes between knowing parts individually (tafsil) and knowing them as an ordered, restricted whole (ijmal).
3
Understand the sura wahidaniyya
The unitary form is a new mental object that emerges from the arrangement of parts; it was not obtained before.
This is not simply the sum of parts, but their structured unity.
4
Relate to the broader debate on tasawwurat
The passage notes that some scholars hold all conceptions are intuitive, making definition useless. The commentator argues that some are theoretical, requiring definition.
This debate underpins the necessity of definitions in usul.
5
Apply to usul al-fiqh
Definitions of legal terms (e.g., salah, sawm) are composed of essential parts; the ordered definition yields the correct understanding of the legal concept.
Without this resolution, definitions would be circular.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متن المسلم : واورد أن تعريف الماهية بنفسها وأجزائها تحصيل الحاصل و العوارض خارجة فلا يتحصل بها الحقيقة ...... والجواب أن التصورات المتعلقة بالاجزاء تفصيلا اذا رتبت وقيدت فهذا المجموع هو الحد الموصل الى الصورة الواحدانية المتعلقة بجميع الاجزاء اجمالاً وهو المحدود فهناک تحصیل امرلم یکن حاصلاً فتدبر
ترجمہ :۔ اور اعتراض کیا گیا کہ ماھیت کی تعریف نفس ماهیت اور اجزاء ماهیت سے تحصیل حاصل ہے اور عوارض ماھیت سے خارج ہوتے ہیں اس لئے کہ عوارض سے حقیقت حاصل نہیں ہو سکتی اور جواب یہ ہے کہ وہ تصورات جو معرف کے اجزاء تفصیلیہ سے متعلق ہیں جب ان کو ترتیب دیکر مقید کر دیا جاتا ہے تو یہی مجموعہ حد ہے جو اس صورت و حدانیہ کی طرف موصل ہے جس کا جمیع اجزاء کے ساتھ اجمالا تعلق ہے اور یہی محدود ہے پس یہاں ایک ایسے امر کا حاصل کرنا ہے جو پہلے حاصل نہ تھا اس لئے غور رو! مهيد: - ماسبق سے یہ معلوم ہو گیا ہے کہ معرف تصور کا کا سب ہے مگر تصور کا کا سب ہونا اس وقت صحیح ہو سکتا ہے جب یہ ثابت ہو جائے کہ بعض تصورات نظری ہوتے ہیں اس لئے اس کے کسب کی ضرورت ہے جب کہ مناطقہ کا ایک گروہ اس بات کا قائل ہے کہ تمام تصورات بدیہی ہیں اس لئے کسب کاسب کی بالکل ہی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ اس تو ہم کا منشاء دو امر ہے۔ امر اول مطلوب و مکتب کی جہت سے اور امر دوم کا سب یعنی طریق اکتساب کی جہت ہے۔ چنانچہ حضرت امام رازکی نے اپنی کتاب میں دونوں امروں کا تذکرہ کیا ہے جو تمام تصورات کے بداہت کا منشاء ہیں مگر مصنف نے امراول کو اس کے مشہور یا ضعیف ہونے کی وجہ سے ترک کر دیا اور امر دوم کے قوی اور اہم ہونے کے سبب اس کو بیان
Matn of al-Muslim: And it was objected that defining the quiddity by itself and its parts is a obtaining of what is already obtained (tahsil al-hasil), and accidents are external to it, so the reality cannot be obtained by them. The answer is that the conceptions related to the parts in detail when arranged and restricted, this totality is the definition which leads to the unitary form related to all parts in a general way, and that is the defined. So here there is an obtaining of something that was not obtained before, so ponder. 
Translation: An objection was raised that defining the quiddity by the quiddity itself and its parts is obtaining what is already obtained, and accidents are external to the quiddity, so the reality cannot be obtained by them. The answer is that the conceptions related to the detailed parts when arranged and restricted, this totality is the definition which leads to the unitary form that has a general relation to all parts, and that is the defined. Thus here there is an obtaining of something that was not previously obtained, so reflect. 
Commentary: From the above it is known that the definiens is a cause for the conception, but the definiens being a cause is correct only when it is established that some conceptions are theoretical, so there is need to acquire them. Whereas a group of logicians holds that all conceptions are intuitive, so there is no need for acquisition at all. The basis of this discussion is two matters: the first is from the aspect of the desired and the written, and the second is from the aspect of the cause, i.e. the method of acquisition. Thus Imam Razi mentioned both matters in his book which are the basis of the intuitiveness of all conceptions, but the author left out the first because it is well-known or weak, and mentioned the second because it is strong and important.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection to the definition of mahiyya (quiddity). The objection claims that defining a thing by itself and its parts is tahsil al-hasil (obtaining what is already had) and thus redundant. The answer is that while the parts are known individually, the ordered and restricted totality produces a new unitary form (sura wahidaniyya) that was not previously known. This shows that definition does yield new knowledge. The commentary then discusses whether tasawwurat (conceptions) are badihi (intuitive) or nazari (theoretical). The author argues that some conceptions are theoretical and require acquisition through definition. This is a key usul point: if all conceptions were intuitive, definitions would be useless. The author sides with the view that some are theoretical, supporting the utility of definition.

Key Terms
تحصیل الحاصل (tahsil al-hasil): The fallacy of obtaining something already obtained; an objection against definition by parts
ماهية (mahiyya): Quiddity; whatness of a thing, its essence
صورت واحدانیہ (sura wahidaniyya): Unitary form; the holistic conception resulting from ordered parts in a definition

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the passage refute the objection that defining mahiyya by its parts is tahsil al-hasil?
A) By claiming that parts are unknown before definition.
B) By arguing that accidents must be included.
C) By explaining that the arranged parts produce a new unitary form not previously known.
D) By stating that all conceptions are intuitive.

Key Takeaway
The arranged parts of a definition yield a new unitary form (sura wahidaniyya), resolving the tahsil al-hasil objection and validating the role of definitions in usul.

The Third Figure Syllogism: Conditions and Conclusions
Explains the third figure syllogism and its two conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two conditions of the third figure syllogism and determine whether its conclusion is particular affirmative or particular negative.

Core Idea
The third figure's conclusion is always particular: affirmative when both premises are affirmative, negative when the major is negative.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the third figure syllogism is a key tool for constructing arguments. This passage from 'Ashraf al-Nu'ut' explains its conditions and the resulting types of conclusions. Understanding this helps in evaluating istidlal (legal reasoning) within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the structure of the third figure
Recognize that in the third figure, the middle term is the subject in both premises. This sets it apart from other figures and determines the logical flow.
Middle term = term that appears in both premises but not in the conclusion.
2
State the two conditions
The passage specifies two mandatory conditions: the minor premise must be affirmative, and at least one of the two premises must be universal.
If either condition fails, the argument is not a valid third figure syllogism.
3
Determine conclusion type based on major premise
If the major premise is affirmative (universal or particular), the conclusion is particular affirmative (e.g., 'some S are P'). If the major is negative, the conclusion is particular negative (e.g., 'some S are not P').
The conclusion is always particular because the minor is particular in force due to the first condition.
4
Apply to the given example
Example: 'Some animals are rational' (minor, affirmative), 'No animal is lifeless' (major, universal negative). The conclusion is 'Some rational beings are not lifeless' (particular negative). Verify that the conditions hold and the conclusion matches the rule.
This example is a valid third figure syllogism (mode 2 according to the passage).

اشراف النعوت شرح مسلم الثبوت ۱۵۴ طرح صغری و کبری کو ترتیب دیں گے تو اکبر کا سلب بعض اصغر سے لازما ہوگا۔ جیسے بـعـض الـحـيـوان ناطق، ولاشئى من الحيوان بجماد ، فبعض الناطق ليس بجماد مثال مذکور شکل ثالث کی دونوں شرطوں کے مطابق ہے چنانچہ صغری موجبہ ہے اور مقدمتین میں سے ایک کلیہ ہے مگر چونکہ کبری سالبہ ہے اس لئے اکبر کا سلب اصغر کے بعض افراد سے لازم ہے کیونکہ صغریٰ میں جب یہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ بعض حیوان کے لئے نطق ثابت ہے اور پھر کبری میں حیوان کے جملہ افراد سے جماد کلیۂ مسلوب ہے تو یقیناً معلوم ہو گیا کہ نطق و جماد یکجا نہیں ہو سکتے اس لئے مصنف نے کہا فیعلم عدم انتقاء [؟] قوله فلايكون اللازم الاجزئياً موجباً اوسالباً شکل مذکور کی شرط ایجاب صغری و کلیت احدى المقدمتین پر متفرع ہے۔ حاصل یہ ہے کہ شرط شکل ثالث کے پیش نظر اس قیاس کا نتیجہ ہمیشہ یا تو موجہ جزئیہ ہوگا یا پھر سالبہ جزئیہ آئے گا۔ چنانچہ شرط اول کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے جب قیاس ضرب اول کے طریقہ پر موجبہ کلیہ صغری، موجبہ کلیہ کبری سے اور ضرب ثالث کے طریقہ پر موجبہ جزئیہ صغری و موجبہ کلیہ کبری سے ، اور ضرب خامس کے طریقہ پر موجہ کلیہ صغری ، موجبہ جزئیہ کبری سے مرکب ہوگا تو نتیجہ وقیاس یا مطلوب ہمیشہ موجبہ جزئیہ آئے گا جیسا کہ گذشتہ مثالوں سے ظاہر ہے۔ اور شرط ثانی کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے جب قیاس ضرب ثانی کے طریقہ پر، موجبہ کلیہ صغری و سالیہ کلیہ کبری سے اور ، ضرب رابع کے مطابق موجبہ جزئیہ صغریٰ و سالہ کلیہ کبری اور ضرب سادس کے طریق پر موجہ کلیہ صغری وسالبہ جزئیہ کبری سے مرکب ہوگا تو نتیجہ قیاس یا مطلوب ہمیشہ سالبہ جزئیہ آئے گا جیسا کہ گذرا۔
We will arrange the minor and major premises, then the negation of the major necessarily applies to some of the minor. For example: some animals are rational, and no animal is lifeless, so some rational beings are not lifeless. This example matches both conditions of the third figure: the minor is affirmative and one of the two premises is universal, but because the major is negative, the negation of the major necessarily applies to some individuals of the minor. Because in the minor it is known that some animals have rationality, and in the major lifelessness is negated from all animals, then it is known with certainty that rationality and lifelessness cannot coexist. Therefore the author said: 'So it is known that the non-occurrence of [?].' His statement: 'So the necessary consequent is not particular affirmative or negative.' The condition of this figure is branched on the affirmation of the minor and the universality of one of the premises. The summary is that, considering the condition of the third figure, the result of this syllogism is either particular affirmative or particular negative. So, considering the first condition, when the syllogism is composed according to the first mode: universal affirmative minor and universal affirmative major, and according to the third mode: particular affirmative minor and universal affirmative major, and according to the fifth mode: universal affirmative minor and particular affirmative major, then the result of the syllogism is always particular affirmative, as evident from previous examples. And considering the second condition, when the syllogism is composed according to the second mode: universal affirmative minor and universal negative major, and according to the fourth mode: particular affirmative minor and universal negative major, and according to the sixth mode: universal affirmative minor and particular negative major, then the result of the syllogism is always particular negative, as has passed.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage explains the third figure syllogism in Aristotelian logic as applied in usul al-fiqh. The author demonstrates that the third figure always yields a particular conclusion, either affirmative or negative, depending on whether the major premise is affirmative or negative. The key conditions are that the minor must be affirmative and one premise must be universal. The example given is a valid third figure syllogism: some animals are rational (minor), no animal is lifeless (major), therefore some rational beings are not lifeless. This matches the pattern where the middle term is the subject of both premises. The author then details the six modes (darb) of the third figure, showing that in modes 1,3,5 (where both premises are affirmative) the conclusion is particular affirmative, and in modes 2,4,6 (where the major is negative) the conclusion is particular negative. This is a standard treatment in logic and usul methodology.

Key Terms
شکل ثالث (shakl thalith): Third figure of syllogism where the middle term is subject in both premises
موجبه جزئیه (mujiba juz'iyya): Particular affirmative proposition (some S are P)
سالبہ جزئیه (saliba juz'iyya): Particular negative proposition (some S are not P)

The third figure syllogism always yields a particular conclusion, and the two conditions (affirmative minor, one universal premise) guarantee this.

Conditional Syllogism and the Meaning of Entailment
Defines conditional syllogism and rebuts an objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qiyas istithna'i, explain the definition of luzum, and apply it to determine valid conditional syllogisms.

Core Idea
The conditional syllogism requires strict entailment: positing the antecedent necessitates the consequent, but only negation of the consequent negates the antecedent.

This passage from Muslim al-Thubut introduces the fourth near syllogistic form—conditional syllogism (qiyas istithna'i). The author defines its structure and addresses a subtle objection about the converse, reinforcing that valid entailment means impossibility of separation across all times and states. Understanding this logical tool is essential for constructing sound legal analogies in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the syllogism type
Recognize that 'the fourth' refers to the conditional syllogism (qiyas istithna'i), where the conclusion or its contradictory is explicitly mentioned in the premises.
This is distinct from simple syllogisms like the first figure (e.g., Barbara).
2
Understand the structure
A conditional syllogism consists of a conditional premise (e.g., 'If A then B') and an exceptive premise that affirms or negates one part, leading to the affirmation or negation of the other part.
The exceptive particle 'but' (lākin) is used.
3
Define strict entailment (luzum)
Luzum is the impossibility of separation between two things in all times and periods. Positing the antecedent necessitates positing the consequent; conversely, negating the consequent necessitates negating the antecedent.
The converse (negating antecedent leads to negating consequent) is not automatically valid.
4
Analyze the objection
The objection claims that if the consequent's non-existence is impossible, then assuming its non-existence violates the entailment, so negating the antecedent is not necessitated. The author rebuts that this objection merely denies the assumed luzum.
The objection conflates the hypothetical assumption with the definition of luzum.
5
Apply the rule
Practice constructing conditional syllogisms using strict luzum. For example: 'If the command is general, then it indicates obligation. The command for prayer is general, so it indicates obligation.'
Ensure that the entailment is genuine and not merely coincidental.

متن المسلم : "والرابعة أن يثبت الملازمة بين امرين فينتج فيه وضع المقدم وضع التالى والافلا لزوم ولا عكس لجواز اعمية اللازم والرفع بالعكس واورد منع استلزام الرفع الرفع لجواز استحالة انتفاء اللازم فاذا وقع جاز عدم بقاء اللزوم فلايلزم انتفاء الملزوم اقول اللزوم حقيقة امتناع الانفكاك في جميع الاوقات والتقادير وقت الانفكاك وهو عدم بقاء اللزوم داخل في الجميع فهذا المنع يرجع الى منع اللزوم وقد فرض هكذا فتدبر" ترجمه : چوتھی صورت یہ ہے کہ دو امر کے درمیان ملازمت ثابت کر دیا جائے تو اس میں وضع مقدم وضع تالی کا نتیجہ دے گا ورنہ دونوں امر کے درمیان لزوم نہیں رہے گا اور اس کا عکس نہیں ہو سکتا اس لئے کہ ممکن ہے کہ لازم عام ہو اور رفع برعکس وضع ہے، اور اعتراض کیا گیا ہے کہ تالی کا رفع مقدم کے رفع کو مستلزم ہونا ممنوع ہے اس لئے کہ ایسا ہو سکتا ہے کہ انتفاء لازم محال ہو پس جب انتفاء لازم کا وقوع فرض کر لیا جائے تو لزوم باقی نہیں رہ جائے گا تو ملزوم کا انتفاء لازم نہیں آئے گا میں کہوں گا کہ لزوم حقیقت میں تمام اوقات و جملہ تقادیر میں انفکاک کے امتناع کا نام ہے لہذا وقت انفکاک اور وہ لزوم کا باقی نہ رہنا ہے، جمیع تقادیر میں داخل ہے غرض یہ اعتراض تو منع لزوم کی طرف راجع ہے حالانکہ لزوم فرض کیا گیا ہے یہ خلاف مفروض ہے اسلئے غور کرو! تشریح : - قیاس کے صور خمسہ قریبہ میں سے چوتھی صورت قیاس استثنائی کا ذکر اس عبارت میں ہے۔ اور شکل رابع کو مصنف نے ترک کر دیا کہ وہ قریب الانتاج نہیں ہوتا بلکہ بعید از قیاس ہے۔ اس کے بر عکس شکل ثانی و ثالث چونکہ بعید از قیاس نہیں ہیں بلکہ قریب الانتاج ہوتے ہیں اس لئے قریبہ میں داخل میں چونکہ شکل ثانی کو شکل اول کی طرف نقل کرنے کے لئے نقیض نتیجہ کو صغری بنا دینا کافی ہے ایسے ہی شکل ثالث کو اول کی طرف پھیرنے کے لئے نقیض نتیجہ کو کبری بنا دینا کافی ہے کسی مقدمہ اجنبیہ کے سہارا لینے کی ضرورت نہیں پڑتی جیسا کہ گذرا ۔ اس لئے مصنف نے صرف اول و ثانی اور ثالث کو ذکر کیا اور رابع کو ترک کر دیا پھر شروع کیا قیاس استثنائی کے بیان میں تو کہا الرابعة ان يثبت الملازمة الخ ۔ قوله الرابعة ان يثبت الملازمة بين أمرين الخ اس عبارت سے قیاس استثنائی کی طرف اشارہ ہے۔ اس کی تفصیل مندرجہ ذیل ہے۔ قیاس استثنائی :۔ اس کو کہتے ہیں جس میں نتیجہ یا نقیض نتیجہ بالفعل مذکور ہو۔ یہ قیاس بھی دو مقدمہ سے مرکب ہوتا ہے اولا ایک قضیہ شرطیہ کو ذکر کرتے ہیں پھر حرف استثنائی "لکن" کے ذریعہ دوسرا مقدمہ وضعیہ لاتے ہیں جس میں اس کے دونوں جزؤوں میں سے ایک کا اثبات یا رفع ہوتا ہے تاکه جزء آخر کی وضع یا اس کا رفع لازم ہو سکے۔ شرطیہ متصلہ میں اس کی مثال اس طرح دی جاتی ہے۔ كلما كانت الشمس طالعة فالنهار موجود ، لكن الشمس طالعة - ج أن
The text of al-Muslim: 'And the fourth is that entailment is established between two things, so therein positing the antecedent requires positing the consequent; otherwise there is no entailment and no converse because the consequent may be more general, and the negation is opposite to the positing. And an objection is raised: that the negation of the consequent necessitating the negation of the antecedent is denied, because it is possible that the non-existence of the consequent is impossible. So when its occurrence is assumed, it is permissible that the entailment does not remain, so the non-existence of the antecedent is not necessitated. I say: entailment is in reality the impossibility of separation in all times and periods; the time of separation, which is the non-remainder of entailment, is included in all periods. So this objection reverts to denying the entailment, while entailment has been assumed as such, so reflect.' Translation: The fourth form is that entailment is established between two things; then in it positing the antecedent yields the positing of the consequent; otherwise there is no entailment between the two things, and its converse is not possible, because it is possible that the consequent is more general, and negation is the opposite of positing. And an objection is raised: that the negation of the consequent necessitating the negation of the antecedent is denied, because it is possible that the non-existence of the consequent is impossible. So when its occurrence is assumed, then the entailment does not remain, so the non-existence of the antecedent is not necessitated. I say: entailment is in reality the impossibility of separation in all times and periods; so the time of separation, which is the non-remainder of entailment, is included in all periods. In short, this objection reverts to denying the entailment, while entailment has been assumed; this is contrary to the assumption, so reflect! Clarification: Among the five near forms of syllogism, the fourth form is the conditional syllogism mentioned in this passage. And the author omitted the fourth figure because it is not near in producing the result but far from syllogism. In contrast, the second and third figures are not far from syllogism but are near in producing the result, so they are included in the near forms. Because to convert the second figure to the first, it suffices to make the contradictory of the result the minor premise; similarly, to convert the third to the first, it suffices to make the contradictory of the result the major premise; no need to take external premises, as has passed. Therefore the author mentioned only the first, second, and third, and omitted the fourth. Then he began the discussion of conditional syllogism, saying: 'The fourth is that entailment is established...' His statement: 'The fourth is that entailment is established between two things' indicates the conditional syllogism. Its details are as follows. Conditional syllogism: it is called that in which the result or its contradictory is actually mentioned. This syllogism is also composed of two premises: first a conditional proposition is mentioned, then through the exceptive particle 'but' (lakin) a second premise, which is a positive proposition, is brought in which either affirms or negates one of its two parts, so that the positing or negation of the other part becomes necessary. An example in a conjunctive conditional: 'Whenever the sun is shining, then day exists; but the sun is shining.' So that...
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage discusses the fourth type of syllogism in the classification of near syllogisms, which is the conditional syllogism (qiyas istithna'i). The author first presents the matn from Muslim al-Thubut, which states that this syllogism works by establishing entailment between two things: positing the antecedent leads to positing the consequent. However, the converse (negating the antecedent leading to negating the consequent) does not necessarily hold because the consequent may be more general than the antecedent. An objection is then raised: if the consequent's non-existence is impossible, then assuming its non-existence violates the entailment itself, so the conclusion that the antecedent is negated is not valid. The author responds by defining lizum (entailment) as the impossibility of separation in all times and periods; thus any time of separation (i.e., the consequent not existing) would contradict the entailment, so the objection merely denies the assumed entailment. Therefore the objection is invalid because it goes against the hypothesis. The commentary then clarifies that the author omitted the fourth figure because it is not productive, unlike the second and third which can be converted to the first figure. The conditional syllogism is defined as a syllogism where the conclusion or its contradictory is explicitly stated within the premises. It consists of a conditional premise and an exceptive premise that affirms or negates one part, leading to the positing or negation of the other. An example is given: 'Whenever the sun is shining, day exists; but the sun is shining' (so day exists).

Key Terms
قیاس استثنائی (qiyas istithna'i): A syllogism in which the conclusion or its contradictory is explicitly mentioned in the premises, consisting of a conditional premise and an exceptive premise affirming or negating one part.
لزوم (luzum): Entailment; the impossibility of separation between two things in all times and periods.
وضع مقدم (wad' muqaddam): Positing the antecedent of a conditional.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The necessity of conjunction in all times and periods
C) The impossibility of separation in all times and periods

Key Takeaway
The validity of a conditional syllogism depends on strict entailment (luzum) that negates the possibility of separation in any time or period.
